Necessity of Raising Hands Between Prostrations and the Wisdom of Two Sajdahs
Ruling with proof and discussion of hikmah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raising hands between sajdahs, identify the supporting dalil, and explain why the two sajdahs are classified as devotional (ta'abudi).

Core Idea
Raising hands from the ground between sajdahs is wajib because hands prostrate like the face; two sajdahs are devotional without rational cause.

The details of prayer are often dismissed as trivial, but they carry significant legal weight. One such detail is whether the worshipper must lift his hands after the first prostration before performing the second. In this passage, the author of Imdad al-Fattah establishes the Hanafi position that it is indispensable, citing prophetic practice and refuting opposing views. He then turns to the wisdom behind the repetition of sujood, affirming that it is a devotional act whose inner meaning is known to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is raising the hands from the ground after the first sajdah before the second. The author states it is 'indispensable' (لا بد منه), implying obligation (wajib).
Obligation level: not fard but wajib due to zanni evidence.
2
Locate and analyze the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'Indeed the two hands prostrate as the face prostrates...' combined with 'Pray as you see me praying.' The imperative indicates obligation per Hanafi usul.
The hadith is from Abu Dawud and Nasa'i; its transmission is zanni but meaning is clear.
3
Note the ikhtilaf and the author's tarjih
Abu al-Layth (Hanafi) and al-Suyuti (Shafi'i) hold it is not a condition. The author refutes them with explicit hadith, giving tarjih to the necessity view.
The practical difference: if omitted, according to the author, the second sajdah is not fully valid.
4
Explain the nature of two sajdahs as devotional
The majority of Hanafi jurists hold that the repetition of sujood is ta'abudi – a ritual act not subject to rational explanation, like the number of rak'ahs.
Some mention wisdoms (humiliating devil, creation/return, covenant) but these are not the basis of the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولأصحاب مالك في ذلك قولان وقال ابن العماد أيضاً في كتاب آخر : يجب على المصلي إذا رفــع رأسه من السجدة الأولى أن يرفع يديه من الأرض كما يرفع جبهته؛ لأن السجود يكون بهما مرتين كما يكون بالجبهة، وهذا ظاهر نص الإمام الشافعي في «الأم» فإنه قال: إن القول بوجوب السجود على هذه الأعضاء هو الموافق للحديث، والثابت في الحديث أنه صلى الله عليه وسلم كَانَ إِذَا سَجَدَ وَرَفَعَ رَأْسَهُ مِنَ السجدَةِ الأولى رَفَعَ يَديهِ مِنَ الأرض ووَضَعُهُمَا عَلَى فَخِذَيْهِ ) (۱) وقال : «صلوا كَمَا رَأَيْتُمُونِي أصلي ) . وروى ابن عمر عنه أنه قال: ( إِنَّ اليدين يسجدان كما يَسْجُدُ الوَجْهُ، فَإِذَا وَضَعَ أَحَدُكُمْ وَجْهَهُ فَلْيَضَعَهُمَا، وإذا رفعه فَلْيَرْفَعهُمَا ) (۳). أخرجه أبو داود والنسائي. وروى مالك في « الموطأ » : أن ابن عمر كان يقول: «مَنْ وَضَعَ جَبْهَتَهُ بِالْأَرْضِ فَلْيَضَعْ كَفَّيْهِ عَلَى الَّذِي وَضَعَ عَلَيْهِ جَبْهَتَهُ، وَإِذَا رَفَعَ فَلْيَرْفَعْهُمَا فَإِنَّ الْيَدَيْنِ يَسْجُدَانِ كَمَا يَسْجُدُ الْوَجْهُ ) () انتهى عبارة الإمام السيوطي رحمه الله، قلت: فالحاصل أن رفع اليدين عن الأرض لا بد منه ليتحقق تكرار السجود بـهما كالجبهة، وأمـا صـفـة وضعهما على الفخذين حالة الجلوس بين السجدتين فسنّة، ومن أنكر هذا عليه الدليــل لِمَا يَدَّعِيه، وعليه رَدُّ قول الفقيه أبي الليث الذي قد حكيناه بدليله، والمخالف من الشافعية لمـا قـالـه الجـلال السيوطي حيث قال: لا يشترط رفع اليدين عن الأرض لصحة السجدة الثانية، هو كالمخالف مـن الحنفية لما قاله الفقيه أبو الليث. وتكلموا في حكمة تكرار السجود دون الركوع، فمذهب الفقهاء أن هذا تعبدي لا يطلب فيه المعنى، كأعداد الركعات، وفي (المبسوط » : قيل: إنما كان السجود مثنى ترغيماً للشيطان، فإنه أمِرَ بالسجود فلم يفعل، فنحن نسجد مرتين ترغيمـاً لـه، وإليه أشــار النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في سجود السهو ترغيماً للشيطان. وقيل: السجدة الأولى إشارة إلى أنـه خـلـق مـن الأرض، والثانية إشارة إلى أنه يعود إليها. قال تعالى: مِنْهَا خَلَقْنَكُمْ وَفِيهَا نُعِيدُكُمْ [طه: ٥٥] وفي « مبسوط» شيخ الإسلام أكثر مشايخنا على أنه توقيف غير معقول المعنى، ومنهم من يذكر لذلك حكمة فقال: حكمته ما روي في بعض الأخبار أن الله تعالى لما أخذ الميثاق من ذرية آدم عليه الصلاة والسلام حيث قال: ﴿وَإِذْ أَخَذَ رَبُّكَ مِنْ بَنِي ءَادَمَ ﴾ [الأعراف: ۱۷۲] أمرهم بالسجود تصديقاً لمـا قـالوا، فسجد المسلمون كلهم وبقي الكافرون، فلما رفعوا رؤوسهم رأوا الكفار لم يسجدوا، فسجدوا ثانياً شكراً لما وفقهم الله تعالى إليه، فصار المفروض سجدتين كذا في «معراج الدراية»، وزاد في المستصفى»، قيل: إن الأولى لشكر نعمة الإيمان والأخرى لبقاء الإيمان. انتهى.
For the followers of Malik there are two sayings in this matter. And Ibn al-Imad also said in another book: It is obligatory for the one praying, when he raises his head from the first prostration, to raise his hands from the ground just as he raises his forehead, because prostration is done with them twice just as it is with the forehead. And this is the apparent text of Imam al-Shafi'i in al-Umm, for he said: The statement that prostration is obligatory on these limbs is the one that agrees with the hadith, and what is established in the hadith is that the Prophet, peace be upon him, when he prostrated and raised his head from the first prostration, he raised his hands from the ground and placed them on his thighs. And he said: 'Pray as you see me praying.' And Ibn Umar narrated from him that he said: 'Indeed the two hands prostrate just as the face prostrates. So when one of you places his face, let him place them, and when he raises it, let him raise them.' It was recorded by Abu Dawud and al-Nasa'i. And Malik narrated in al-Muwatta that Ibn Umar used to say: 'Whoever places his forehead on the ground, let him place his palms on what he placed his forehead on, and when he raises, let him raise them, for indeed the two hands prostrate just as the face prostrates.' End of the statement of Imam al-Suyuti, may Allah have mercy on him. I say: The result is that raising the hands from the ground is indispensable in order to realize the repetition of prostration with them like the forehead. As for the manner of placing them on the thighs during the sitting between the two prostrations, it is Sunnah. And whoever denies this has the evidence against what he claims. And upon this is the refutation of the statement of al-Faqih Abu al-Layth which we have mentioned with its evidence. And the dissenter from the Shafi'is due to what al-Jalal al-Suyuti said—that raising the hands from the ground is not a condition for the validity of the second prostration—is like the dissenter from the Hanafis due to what al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said. And they discussed the wisdom of repeating prostration without bowing. The school of the jurists is that this is devotional (ta'abudi), in which meaning is not sought, like the numbers of rak'ahs. And in al-Mabsut: It is said that prostration was made twofold to humiliate the devil, for he was commanded to prostrate but did not, so we prostrate twice to humiliate him. And the Prophet, peace be upon him, alluded to this in the prostration of forgetfulness to humiliate the devil. And it is said: The first prostration indicates that he was created from the earth, and the second indicates that he will return to it. Allah says: 'From it We created you and into it We will return you.' [Ta-Ha: 55] And in Mabsut of Shaykh al-Islam, most of our scholars hold that it is a ritual command (tawqif) with no comprehensible meaning. Among them are those who mention a wisdom for it, saying: Its wisdom is what is narrated in some reports that when Allah took the covenant from the descendants of Adam, peace be upon him, when He said: 'And when your Lord took from the children of Adam' [al-A'raf: 172], He commanded them to prostrate in affirmation of what they said. So all the Muslims prostrated, and the disbelievers remained. When they raised their heads, they saw that the disbelievers had not prostrated, so they prostrated a second time in gratitude for what Allah had guided them to. Thus the obligatory became two prostrations. This is in Ma'raj al-Dirayah. And in al-Mustasfa it adds: It is said the first is for gratitude for the blessing of faith, and the second for the continuation of faith. End.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and includes intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab disputes. The author begins by quoting a Maliki view and Ibn al-Imad, then presents the Shafi'i position from al-Umm. He then cites hadith from Abu Dawud, Nasa'i, and Malik's Muwatta to support the necessity of raising hands from the ground during sujood, as the hands prostrate like the face. The author then gives his own conclusion (قلت): raising hands is indispensable (لا بد منه) for the second sajdah, while placing them on the thighs during the sitting between sajdahs is only Sunnah. He refutes the view of Abu al-Layth (a Hanafi) and Jalal al-Suyuti (Shafi'i) who claimed it is not required. The second part discusses the hikmah (wisdom) of repeating sujood without bowing. The majority of Hanafi jurists consider it devotional (ta'abudi) with no rational meaning, like the number of rak'ahs. However, some mention wisdoms such as humiliating the devil, or the first sajdah indicating creation from earth and the second indicating return to it, or the covenant story from the Qur'an. The passage ends with citations from Ma'raj al-Dirayah and al-Mustasfa.

Key Terms
سجود (sujood): Prostration, a position in which the worshipper places his forehead, nose, hands, knees, and toes on the ground. The text emphasizes that the hands also prostrate.
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands from the ground after the first sajdah before performing the second sajdah. The text argues it is necessary for the second sajdah of the hands.
تعبدي (ta'abudi): A devotional act whose wisdom may not be rationally understood; accepted as commanded by Allah without seeking a cause, like the number of rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of Imdad al-Fattah, what is the ruling on raising the hands from the ground between the two prostrations?
A) It is Sunnah, not required.
B) It is indispensable (necessary) for the validity of the second sajdah.
C) It is forbidden to raise the hands.
D) It is only required for the Shafi'i school.

Key Takeaway
Raising hands from the ground between sajdahs is wajib based on hadith; the two sajdahs are devotional acts not subject to rational explanation.

Salah — Prayer

The Final Sitting (Qa'dah Akheerah): Ruling, Measure, and Conditions
Defines the ruling of final sitting, its duration, conditions, and dispute on reading while asleep

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the final sitting, apply its conditions, and evaluate the dispute regarding recitation while asleep.

Core Idea
The final sitting is fard to the extent of tashahhud; pillars must be performed awake.

The final sitting (qa'dah akheerah) is a critical component of prayer that often confuses students: is it fard, wajib, or sunnah? This passage from Sharh Nur al-Idah establishes it as fard by consensus, backed by the Prophet's continuous practice and the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud. We'll explore its obligatory measure, the condition that it must come after all other pillars, and the requirement of wakefulness for pillars. The lesson also tackles an interesting intra-Hanafi dispute about whether recitation performed while asleep is valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The passage opens stating that the final sitting is fard (obligatory) by consensus. Note the author uses 'يفترض' (is made obligatory) and cites the Quranic command to establish prayer and the Prophet's continuous practice. Identify the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud as the primary dalil.
The author treats it as fard, though in standard Hanafi usul it is often wajib. This is a later preference.
2
Determine the measure of the sitting
The text says 'المفروض القعود قدر قراءة التشهد في الأصح' – the obligatory sitting is to the extent of reciting the tashahhud. Note that some Hanafi scholars (e.g., in al-Burhan) said just the two shahadas, but the author takes the majority view.
3
Analyze the condition of postponement
The sitting must be delayed until after all other pillars. If one remembers a missed prostration after sitting, he must perform it and repeat the sitting, because the first sitting was premature.
This illustrates the principle that order is a condition for pillars.
4
Examine the condition of wakefulness for pillars
Pillars (e.g., bowing, prostration) must be performed while awake. Actions done entirely while asleep are invalid. However, if one starts an action awake and then sleeps during it, the pillar is valid. This leads to the dispute about recitation.
5
Evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on recitation while asleep
Two positions: Abu al-Layth (valid) vs. Fakhr al-Islam and al-Hidaya (invalid). The more correct view in later texts (al-Muhit, al-Mubtagha) is that recitation while asleep is invalid, but the author leaves the question open. Understand the reasoning: initial intention vs. absence of choice.
This applies only to recitation, not to physical pillars which are invalid by consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يفترض القعُودُ الأخِيرُ ) بإجماع العلماء وإن اختلفوا في قدره، وعبر بالأخير دون الثاني ليشمل قعدة الفجر وقعدة المسافر، لأنها أخيرة وليست ثانية، كذا في ( الدراية » ، والمراد وصفه بأنه واقــع آخر الصلاة، وإلا فالأخير يقتضي سبق غيره وعليه لو قال آخر عبد أملكه فهو حر، فملك عبداً لم يعتق فليتأمل، والمفروض القعود (قَدْرَ) قراءة ( التَّشهدِ ) في الأصح، وسنذكر ألفاظه، إن شاء الله تعالى لقوله تعالى: ﴿أَقِيمُوا الصَّلوةَ [الانعت : ۷۲] وقد التحق فعل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وقوله بياناً، وهو أنه لم يفعلها قط بدون القعدة الأخيرة، والمواظبة من غير ترك دليل الفرضية، فإذا وقــع بيـانـاً للمجمل المفروض كان فرضاً بالضرورة، إلا ما خرج بدليل، وقَدَّرَهُ أئمتنا بقدر التشهد « لأنه أخذ بيد عبد الله بن مسعود له وعلمه التشهد إلى قوله : وأشهد أن محمداً عبده ورسوله، ثم قال: إذا فعلت هذا أو قلت هذا، فقد قضيت صلاتك إن شئت أن تقم فقم، وإن شئت أن تقعد فاقعد )، علق تمام الصلاة به وما لا يتم الفرض إلا به فهو فرض وزعم بعض مشايخنا أن المفروض في القعدة ما يأتي فيه بكلمة الشهادتين كما في ( البرهان فكان فرضاً عملياً. (وَ) يشترط (تَأخِيرُهُ) أي: القعود الأخير (عن) أداء (الأرْكان) لأنه شرع لختمها، حتى لو تذكر سجدة بعد قعوده يسجدها ويلزمه إعادة الجلوس؛ لأن السابق لم يعتد به لكونه قبل تمام الأركان كما قد علمته. (و) يشترط لصحة الأركان ونحوها (أدَاؤُهَا مُسْتَيْقِظَاً) فإذا ركع نائماً أو قام نائماً لم يعتد به، وأما إذا قام مستيقظاً ثــم نام أو ركع مستيقظاً فنام، فإنه يصح لحصول الركن قبل النوم واختلفوا في قراءة النائم قيل : يُعْتَدُ بها. واختاره الفقيه، أبو الليث؛ لأن الشرع جعل النائم كالمستيقظ في الصلاة تعظيماً لأمر المصلي، واختار فخر الإسلام وصاحب الهداية وغيرهما : أنها لا تجوز . ونص في « المحيط » و « المبتغى» على أنه الأصح؛ لأن الاختيار شرط لأداء العبادة ولم يوجد حالة النوم. وقال الكمال: الأوجه اختيار الفقيه والاختيار المشروط قد وجد في ابتداء الصلاة وهو كاف، ألا يرى أنه لو ركع وسجد ذاهلاً عن فعله كل الذهول أنه يجزئه انتهى. قال صاحب ( البحر » : وهذا يفيد أنه لو ركع وسجد حالة النوم يجزئه. وقد نَصُوا على أنه لا يجزئه. قال في ( المبتغى »: ركــع وهـو نــائـم لا يجوز إجماعاً. انتهى. وفرقهم بين القراءة والركوع والسجود بأن كلا من الركوع والسجود ركن أصلي
And the final sitting is obligatory by consensus of the scholars, although they differed on its measure. He used the term 'final' (al-akhir) instead of 'second' (al-thani) to include the sitting of Fajr and the sitting of the traveler (musafir), because it is final and not second. As stated in al-Diraya. And the intention is to describe it as occurring at the end of the prayer; otherwise the term 'final' implies precedence of others. Upon this, if one said 'the last slave I own is free' and then he owned a slave, the slave would not be freed. So reflect. And the obligatory (mafrud) is the sitting to the extent of reciting the tashahhud in the most correct opinion. We will mention its wording, Allah willing. Because Allah says: 'Establish the prayer' [al-Baqara: 43]. And the action and statement of the Prophet, peace be upon him, came as an explanation, and he never performed it without the final sitting. Continuous practice without omission is evidence of obligation. So when it occurs as an explanation of the obligatory (mujmal), it becomes obligatory by necessity, except what is excluded by evidence. Our imams determined it as the extent of the tashahhud because he took the hand of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and taught him the tashahhud until he said 'and I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and messenger,' then said: 'When you do this or say this, you have completed your prayer. If you wish to stand, stand, and if you wish to sit, sit.' He tied the completion of the prayer to it, and what the obligation cannot be completed without is itself an obligation. Some of our scholars claimed that what is obligatory in the sitting is uttering the two shahadas, as in al-Burhan, so it is a practical obligation (fard 'amili). And its postponement (ta'khir) after the performance of the pillars is required because it is prescribed to seal them, to the extent that if one remembers a prostration after his sitting, he performs it and must repeat the sitting, because the previous one is not considered due to being before the completion of the pillars, as you have learned. And for the validity of the pillars and the like, their performance while awake (mustayqizan) is required. So if one bows while asleep or stands while asleep, it is not considered. But if he stands while awake then sleeps, or bows while awake then sleeps, then it is valid because the pillar occurred before sleep. They differed regarding the recitation of a sleeping person: it is said that it is considered. Abu al-Layth chose this because the law made the sleeping person like the awake one in prayer out of reverence for the one praying. Fakhr al-Islam and the author of al-Hidaya and others chose that it is not permissible. And in al-Muhit and al-Mubtagha it is stated as the more correct opinion because choice (ikhtiyar) is a condition for performing worship, and it does not exist in the state of sleep. Al-Kamal said: The more appropriate is the choice of al-Faqih (Abu al-Layth), and the required choice existed at the beginning of the prayer, and it suffices. Do you not see that if one bows and prostrates while completely oblivious of his action, it suffices him? End. The author of al-Bahr said: This implies that if one bows and prostrates while asleep, it suffices him. But they have explicitly stated that it does not suffice. In al-Mubtagha: Bowing while asleep is not permissible by consensus. End. And they differentiated between recitation and bowing and prostration, saying that both bowing and prostration are original pillars (rukn asli).
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the final sitting (qa'dah akheerah). It begins by stating that the final sitting is obligatory (يفترض) by consensus, though scholars differed on its minimum measure. The author explains that 'final' is used instead of 'second' to include cases like Fajr prayer which has only one sitting, and the traveler's prayer. The obligatory measure is the recitation of the tashahhud (qadr al-tashahhud). The proof is the Qur'anic command to establish prayer, which is explained by the Prophet's continuous practice of the final sitting, and the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud where the Prophet taught the tashahhud and said completion of prayer is tied to it. The rule 'what the obligation cannot be completed without is itself an obligation' is applied. Some scholars said the obligatory part is just the two shahadas (practical obligation). Two conditions are then stated: (1) The final sitting must be postponed after all other pillars; if one remembers a forgotten sajdah after sitting, he must perform it and repeat the sitting. (2) Pillars must be performed while awake; if one bows or stands while asleep, it is invalid. However, if one starts an action while awake then sleeps during it, it is valid. The passage ends with an intra-Hanafi dispute about the recitation of a sleeping person. Abu al-Layth considered it valid, while Fakhr al-Islam and the author of al-Hidaya considered it invalid; the more correct view is that it is invalid. But al-Kamal and the author of al-Bahr argued for validity based on the initial intention. The final line differentiates between recitation and the physical pillars (bowing, prostration) because the latter are original pillars (rukn asli).

Key Terms
القعود الأخير (al-qa'dah al-akheerah): The final sitting in prayer after the last prostration, during which the tashahhud is recited. The text emphasizes it is obligatory.
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The specific supplication recited while sitting, containing the testimony of faith. The obligatory measure of the sitting is the time to recite this.
مستيقظاً (mustayqizan): In a state of wakefulness. The text requires that pillars be performed while awake; actions done in sleep are invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the minimum obligatory measure of the final sitting (qa'dah akheerah) in prayer?
A) The entire sitting until the imam gives salam.
B) The time it takes to recite the tashahhud.
C) Just uttering the two shahadas.
D) The sitting is not obligatory; it is Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
The final sitting is fard (obligatory) to the measure of tashahhud, must be performed after all other pillars, and pillars require wakefulness; recitation while asleep is disputed.

8 min
The Last Sitting: Obligation and Minimum Amount
Establishes obligation of last sitting and its minimal amount as tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the last sitting of prayer, identify the minimal amount required (tashahhud), and explain the evidence from the Prophet's continuous practice.

Core Idea
The last sitting is fard; its minimal amount is the full tashahhud.

In this lesson, we delve into one of the pillars of prayer: the last sitting (qa'dah akhirah). While all schools agree on its obligation, the precise amount that must be recited differs. The Hanafi school, relying on the Prophet's constant practice and specific hadith, holds that the obligatory sitting must be at least the length of the tashahhud. We will trace the proof from the Quranic command to establish prayer and the Sunnah's explanatory role.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the last sitting in prayer. The ruling is fard (obligatory). The text states 'ويفترض القعود الأخير' — it is made obligatory. Consensus (ijma') is cited.
Note: The author uses 'الأخير' (last) to include Fajr and traveler's prayer, where the sitting is last but not second.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary dalil is the Quranic command 'أَقِيمُوا الصَّلَاةَ' (establish prayer). This general command is explained by the Prophet's continuous action (muwazabah) without ever omitting the last sitting.
The usul principle: continuous practice without omission indicates obligation (al-muwazabah min ghayr tark dalil al-fardiyyah).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'aqimu' indicates obligation. The Prophet's sunnah explains the general command, and his constancy proves that the last sitting is an integral part of prayer. Thus, omitting it violates the command.
This is a classic example of bayan (explanation) of a mujmal (general) text.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Scholars agree on the obligation of the last sitting but differ on its minimal amount. The Hanafi position: the extent of the tashahhud. Some Hanafis (as in al-Burhan) say only the two shahadahs are fard. The text declares the first as 'al-ashah' (most correct).
The ikhtilaf is intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab. The relied-upon view is the entire tashahhud.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text gives preference to the entire tashahhud based on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, where the Prophet taught him the tashahhud and said when you say this, you have completed your prayer. This links completion to the entire recitation.
Tarjih authority: 'fee al-ashah' — the author explicitly marks the preferred view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويفترض القُعُودُ الأخِيرُ بإجماع العلماء وإن اختلفوا في قدره، وعبر بالأخير دون الثاني ليشمل قعدة الفجر وقعدة المسافر، لأنها أخيرة وليست ثانية، كذا في الدراية، والمراد وصفه بأنه واقـع آخر الصلاة، وإلا فالأخير يقتضي سبق غيره وعليه لو قال آخر عبد أملكه فهو حر، فملك عبداً لم يعتق فليتأمل، والمفروض القعود قَدْرَ قراءة التَّشهدِ في الأصح، وسنذكر ألفاظه إن شاء الله تعالى لقوله تعالى: ﴿أَقِيمُوا الصَّلوةَ﴾ [الانعت: ۷۲] وقد التحق فعل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وقوله بياناً، وهو أنه لم يفعلها قط بدون القعدة الأخيرة، والمواظبة من غير ترك دليل الفرضية، فإذا وقـع بيـاناً للمجمل المفروض كان فرضاً بالضرورة، إلا ما خرج بدليل، وقَدَّرَهُ أئمتنا بقدر التشهد لأنه أخذ بيد عبد الله بن مسعود له وعلمه التشهد إلى قوله: وأشهد أن محمداً عبده ورسوله، ثم قال: إذا فعلت هذا أو قلت هذا، فقد قضيت صلاتك إن شئت أن تقم فقم، وإن شئت أن تقعد فاقعد، علق تمام الصلاة به وما لا يتم الفرض إلا به فهو فرض، وزعم بعض مشايخنا أن المفروض في القعدة ما يأتي فيه بكلمة الشهادتين كما في البرهان فكان فرضاً عملياً.
And the last sitting is obligatory by consensus of the scholars, though they differed about its amount. He used 'last' instead of 'second' to include the sitting of Fajr and the sitting of the traveler, because it is last and not second. So and so in al-Dirayah. The intended meaning is to describe it as occurring at the end of the prayer; otherwise, 'last' implies something before it. Therefore, if someone said 'the last slave I own is free,' then he owns a slave, he is not freed; this should be considered. And the obligatory sitting is to the extent of reciting the tashahhud in the most correct view, and we will mention its wording, Allah willing, due to His saying: 'Establish prayer' [al-Ankabut/72?]. And the action and saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him, are attached as an explanation: he never performed prayer without the last sitting, and constancy without omission is proof of obligation. So when it occurs as an explanation of the obligatory general command, it is necessarily obligatory, except what is excluded by evidence. Our imams determined its amount as the tashahhud because he (the Prophet) took the hand of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and taught him the tashahhud up to his words: 'and I bear witness that Muhammad is His slave and His messenger,' then said: 'When you have done this or said this, you have completed your prayer; if you wish to stand, stand, and if you wish to sit, sit.' He attached the completion of prayer to it, and what the obligation cannot be fulfilled without is obligatory. Some of our scholars held that the obligatory part in the sitting is that in which the two testimonies occur, as in al-Burhan, so it is a practical obligation.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof establishing the obligation of the last sitting (qa'dah akhirah) in prayer. The author explains that there is consensus (ijma') on its obligation, but scholars differed on its minimal amount. The preferred view (al-ashah) is that it must be the extent of reciting the entire tashahhud. The proof is from the Qur'anic command to establish prayer (interpreted as including all its components) and the continuous practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who never omitted it, which indicates obligation (al-muwazabah min ghayr tark dalil al-fardiyyah). Additionally, the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud explicitly states that when one performs the tashahhud, the prayer is complete. This makes the last sitting a necessary component without which the prayer is invalid. Some Hanafi scholars, as mentioned in al-Burhan, consider only the two testimonies (shahadatayn) as the minimal obligatory part, but the text favors the entire tashahhud.

Key Terms
القعود الأخير (al-qu'ud al-akhir): The last sitting in prayer, after the final prostrations, before the taslim.
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The specific formula of testimony recited in the sitting, including the shahadah and salawat.
المواظبة (al-muwazabah): The Prophet's continuous practice without omission, used as evidence for obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimal amount of the last sitting according to the preferred Hanafi view?
A) The duration of saying 'Subhan Allah' three times
B) The extent of reciting the entire tashahhud
C) Just the two shahadahs
D) Any short sitting

Key Takeaway
The last sitting is fard and its minimal amount is the recitation of the entire tashahhud, established by the Prophet's continuous practice.

Condition: Last Sitting After All Pillars
States a condition for the last sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for the validity of the last sitting and apply it when a missed pillar is remembered.

Core Idea
The last sitting must be after all other pillars; if a pillar is missed, the sitting must be repeated after performing it.

In the prayer, the last sitting is a wajib act that seals the prayer. However, its validity depends on a crucial condition: it must be performed after all other pillars (arkan) are completed. This lesson unpacks that condition and its practical consequence when a person remembers a missed prostration after sitting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
The act is the last sitting (qa'dah akhirah). The condition is that it must be delayed (ta'khir) until after all other pillars are performed.
The condition is a shart for validity.
2
Understand the rationale
The last sitting is prescribed to seal the prayer (khatm). It can only seal a complete prayer, so it must come after all pillars.
The Arabic says 'li-anna-hu shuri'a li-khatmi-ha'.
3
Apply the condition to a scenario
If a person remembers an omitted prostration after the last sitting, the sitting is invalid because it preceded the completion of pillars. He must perform the missed prostration and then repeat the last sitting.
The earlier sitting is 'not counted' (lam yu'tad bihi).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) يشترط (تَأخِيرُهُ) أي: القعود الأخير (عن) أداء (الأرْكان) لأنه شرع لختمها، حتى لو تذكر سجدة بعد قعوده يسجدها ويلزمه إعادة الجلوس؛ لأن السابق لم يعتد به لكونه قبل تمام الأركان كما قد علمته.
And it is a condition to delay it, meaning the last sitting, after performing the pillars, because it is prescribed to seal them. So if he remembers a prostration after his sitting, he performs it and is obliged to repeat the sitting, because the earlier one is not counted due to being before completion of the pillars, as you have already learned.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage states a condition for the validity of the last sitting: it must come after all the pillars (arkan) of the prayer, such as the bowing and prostrations. The last sitting is designed to conclude the prayer. If the worshipper remembers an omitted prostration after sitting, he must perform it and then repeat the sitting because the initial sitting preceded the completion of the pillars and is therefore invalid. This ruling emphasizes the sequential order of the prayer's components.

Key Terms
تأخير (ta'khir): The condition that the last sitting must be delayed until after all other pillars are completed.
الأركان (al-arkan): The essential pillars of prayer: qiyam, ruku', sujud, etc., excluding the last sitting itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a worshipper do if he remembers an omitted prostration after performing the last sitting?
A) He has completed his prayer; no need to do anything
B) He must perform the prostration and may skip the last sitting
C) He must perform the prostration and then repeat the last sitting
D) He must perform the prostration but the last sitting suffices as is

Key Takeaway
The last sitting must be performed after all other pillars; if a pillar is missed and remembered, the sitting must be repeated after performing the pillar.

Validity of Prayer Actions While Asleep
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of prayer actions while asleep

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the rulings for different prayer actions performed while asleep and apply the Hanafi condition of ikhtiyar (conscious choice).

Core Idea
Sleep invalidates pillars requiring conscious intent, but recitation and last sitting are disputed within the Hanafi school.

Sleep can interrupt prayer, but not all actions are treated equally. This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explores which prayer actions remain valid if performed while asleep, revealing an important intra-Hanafi dispute about the role of conscious choice (ikhtiyar). Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correct prayer and fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general condition
The passage begins by stating that pillars and similar actions must be performed while awake. This is the baseline rule.
This covers ruku', sujud, and qiyam (standing).
2
Analyze the dispute over qira'ah
There is a clear difference of opinion: Abu al-Layth deems recitation while asleep valid, while Fakhr al-Islam and the author of al-Hidayah hold it invalid. The proof of each side revolves around the necessity of ikhtiyar.
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is invalidity.
3
Understand the consensus on ruku' and sujud
Despite the disagreement on recitation, there is a consensus that bowing and prostrating while asleep are invalid.
This is because they are original pillars requiring conscious intention.
4
Examine the dispute over the last sitting
The last sitting (qa'dah akhirah) is treated differently: if it is a condition (shart), it can be performed while asleep; if a pillar (rukn), it cannot. The passage contrasts Munyat al-Musalli (requiring repetition) with Jami' al-Fatawa (deeming it valid).
The author points out the practical consequence (thamarah) of this classification.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if the last sitting is a condition, sleeping through it is tolerable; if a pillar, the prayer becomes invalid. This resolves an apparent contradiction in later sources.
This exemplifies how ikhtiyar applies differently to conditions vs. pillars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) يشترط لصحة الأركان ونحوها (أدَاؤُهَا مُسْتَيْقِظَاً) فإذا ركع نائماً أو قام نائماً لم يعتد به، وأما إذا قام مستيقظاً ثـم نام أو ركع مستيقظاً فنام، فإنه يصح لحصول الركن قبل النوم واختلفوا في قراءة النائم قيل : يُعْتَدُ بها. واختاره الفقيه، أبو الليث؛ لأن الشرع جعل النائم كالمستيقظ في الصلاة تعظيماً لأمر المصلي، واختار فخر الإسلام وصاحب الهداية وغيرهما : أنها لا تجوز . ونص في « المحيط » و « المبتغى» على أنه الأصح؛ لأن الاختيار شرط لأداء العبادة ولم يوجد حالة النوم. وقال الكمال: الأوجه اختيار الفقيه والاختيار المشروط قد وجد في ابتداء الصلاة وهو كاف، ألا يرى أنه لو ركع وسجد ذاهلاً عن فعله كل الذهول أنه يجزئه انتهى. قال صاحب ( البحر » : وهذا يفيد أنه لو ركع وسجد حالة النوم يجزئه. وقد نَصُوا على أنه لا يجزئه. قال في ( المبتغى »: ركــع وهـو نــائـم لا يجوز إجماعاً. انتهى. وفرقهم بين القراءة والركوع والسجود بأن كلا من الركوع والسجود ركن أصلي بخلاف القراءة لا يجدي نفعاً. وأما القعدة الأخيرة إذا فعلها نائماً ففي « منية المصلي» : إذا نام في القعدة كلها عليه أن يقعد إذا انتبه قدر التشهد، وإن لم يقعد فسدت صلاته، ويخالفه ما في «جامع الفتاوى : أنه لو قعد قدر التشهد نائماً يعتد به وعلله في التحقيق للشيخ عبد العزيز البخاري: بأنـهـا ليست بركن ومبناها على الاستراحة فيها فيلائمها النوم. انتهى. قلت: وهذا ثمرة الخلاف بين مـن قـال: إنها شرط ومن قال: إنها ركن فتصح نائماً على القول بشرطيتها لا ركنيتها، وهـو جـواب عـــن قـول صاحب البحر » اتفقوا على فرضية القعود الأخير واختلفوا في ركنيته، ولم أر من تعرض لثمرة هذا الاختلاف. انتهى فلله الحمد.
And it is a condition for the validity of the pillars and the like that they be performed while awake. So if he bows while asleep or stands while asleep, it is not counted. But if he stands while awake then sleeps, or bows while awake then sleeps, it is valid because the pillar was performed before sleep. They differed about the recitation of the sleeper: it was said that it is counted, and al-Faqih Abu al-Layth chose this because the Lawgiver made the sleeper like the wakeful in prayer out of reverence for the worshipper. Fakhr al-Islam, the author of al-Hidayah, and others chose that it is not valid. And it is explicitly stated in al-Muhit and al-Mubtagha that this is the most correct view, because choice (ikhtiyar) is a condition for performing worship and it does not exist during sleep. Al-Kamal said: the most appropriate view is the choice of al-Faqih, and the required choice existed at the beginning of prayer, which is sufficient. Does he not see that if he bows and prostrates while completely heedless of his action, it is sufficient for him. The author of al-Bahr said: This implies that if he bows and prostrates while asleep, it is sufficient for him. But they explicitly stated that it is not sufficient. He said in al-Mubtagha: 'He bowed while asleep — it is not permissible by consensus.' They differentiated between recitation and bowing/prostration by saying that each of bowing and prostration is an original pillar, unlike recitation, which has no effect. As for the last sitting if performed while asleep: in Munyat al-Musalli: if he slept through the entire sitting, he must sit when he wakes up to the extent of the tashahhud; if he does not sit, his prayer is invalidated. This is contradicted by what is in Jami' al-Fatawa: that if he sits to the extent of the tashahhud while asleep, it is counted. And it is reasoned in al-Tahqiq by Shaykh Abd al-Aziz al-Bukhari: because it is not a pillar and its basis is rest, so sleep is compatible with it. I say: This is the practical result of the difference between those who say it is a condition and those who say it is a pillar: it is valid while asleep according to the view that it is a condition, not a pillar. And this is a response to the statement of the author of al-Bahr: 'They agreed on the obligation of the last sitting and differed on its being a pillar, and I have not seen anyone who addressed the practical result of this difference.' So praise be to Allah.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This lengthy passage addresses the validity of prayer actions performed while asleep. It begins with the general condition that pillars (like ruku', sujud, and qiyam) must be performed while awake; if done while asleep, they are invalid. However, if the action begins while awake and sleep occurs during it, it is valid. The main dispute concerns qira'ah (recitation) while asleep: Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi considers it valid, reasoning that the Lawgiver treats the sleeper like the awake in prayer out of respect. Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi and the author of al-Hidayah hold it invalid, as choice (ikhtiyar) is a condition lacking in sleep. Al-Kamal ibn al-Humam favors Abu al-Layth's view, arguing that the initial choice at the start of prayer suffices. Regarding ruku' and sujud while asleep, the text states there is consensus that they are invalid (see al-Mubtagha). As for the last sitting, there are two positions: if it is considered a condition, it can be performed while asleep; if a pillar, it cannot. The author mentions Munyat al-Musalli requiring repetition if one sleeps through the entire sitting, while Jami' al-Fatawa deems it valid if the tashahhud is recited while asleep, because the last sitting is not a pillar but a condition based on rest. This difference yields practical consequences.

Key Terms
الاختيار (al-ikhtiyar): The condition of conscious choice and awareness required for valid worship.
شرطية vs ركنية (shartiyyah vs rukniyyah): The debate whether the last sitting is a condition (shart) for prayer's validity or a pillar (rukn) integral to it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most authentic view (al-ashah), what is the ruling on reciting the Qur'an while asleep in prayer?
A) It is valid and counts
B) It is invalid and must be compensated (e.g., sajdah al-sahw or repetition)
C) It is valid only if the person was awake at the start
D) It is invalid but the prayer is still valid without compensation

Key Takeaway
The condition of conscious choice (ikhtiyar) governs the validity of prayer pillars, but disputes remain for recitation and last sitting, with the mufta bihi being invalidity for recitation and validity for last sitting under certain conditions.

Condition: Knowledge of Obligatory and Sunnah Aspects of Prayer
States the condition of knowing the obligatory aspects of prayer to distinguish them from sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two valid conditions for the intention of fard prayer and apply them to scenarios involving a worshipper's knowledge state.

Core Idea
For a fard prayer, you must either know which parts are fard or believe it all is fard — a supererogatory can be intended as fard, but not vice versa.

This passage addresses a critical requirement for the validity of obligatory prayers: correct intention. The condition is not that you memorize every sunnah and fard detail, but that your overall intention matches the nature of the prayer. Let's break down the two options the Hanafi school provides.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
Read the passage and note the two options for the worshipper's knowledge state.
The first requires distinguishing fard from sunnah; the second requires belief that everything is fard.
2
Understand the first condition
The worshipper must know the modality of prayer and be able to distinguish fard characteristics from sunnah ones across the prayers. This does not require distinguishing within a single prayer.
The text gives examples: knowing Fajr has 2 fard and 2 sunnah.
3
Understand the second condition
The worshipper believes that all rak'ahs of the prayer are fard. This is acceptable because a supererogatory act can be performed with the intention of fard.
This covers the ignorant but well-intentioned person.
4
Apply to the cases from al-Tajnis
Consider the four scenarios: (1) no knowledge of obligation, (2) knowledge of mix but no distinction, (3) belief all fard, (4) general knowledge but no detail within a prayer. Determine validity.
Refer to the text for the rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ) يشترط لصحة أداء الفرض أحد أمرين وهما أدنـي ما يسقط به الفرض الأول منهما: (معرفة كيفية) أي: صفة ( الصَّلاةِ وَ) ذلك بمعرفة حقيقة (مَا فِيهَا ) أي : ما في جملة الصلوات ( مِنَ الخِصَالِ) أي: الصفات الفرضية يعني كونها فرضاً كاعتقاده افتراض ركعتي الفجر، وافتراض الأربع في الظهر، وأن سنة الصبح ركعتين غير الفرض، وأن سُنَّة الظهر أربعاً غير الفرض، وهكذا باقي الصلوات (المَفْرُوضَةِ) فيكون ذلك ( على وجه يُمَيِّزُها) بما ذكرنا وليس الشرط أن يميز ما اشتملت عليه صلاة الصبح ونحوها من الفرض والسنة، كأن يعتقد أن القيام ركن، والثناء والتعوذ سنة، والقراءة فرض والتسبيح سنة، بل المراد تمييز الصلاة في حدّ ذاتها بأنها فرض، فتتميز به ( عن الخِصَالِ) أي: الصفات (المَسْنُونَةِ) باعتقاد سُنّية ركعات يصليـهـا غـيـر الـفـرض، كالسـنـن الرواتب وغيرها. والثاني من الأمرين أشار إليه بقوله: (وَاعْتِقَادُ) المصلي (أنَّهَا) أي: إن الصلوات التي يؤديها كلها (فَرْضُ ) كاعتقاده أن جميع الأربع في الصبح فرض، والخمس في المغــرب فـرض، ويصلي ثلاث ركعات منها على حدتها. لأن النفل يصح بنية الفرض دون عكسه، وإليه أشار بقوله (حتى لا يتنفّلَ بمفروض باعتقاد أن ما فعله نفل قال في « التجنيس والمزيد » : رجل لم يعرف أن الصلوات الخمس فريضة على العباد إلا أنه كان يصليها -يعني: بلا نيتها في مواقيتها - لا يجوز وعليه أن يقضيها؛ لأنه لم ينو الفرض، والنية شرط. وكذلك إن علم أن منها ركعات فريضة ومنها سُنّة ولا يعرف الفريضة من السنة لم تجز لما قلنا، إلا إذا صلى خلف الإمام ونوى صلاته، وإن كان يظن أن كلها فريضة أجزأه ما صلى لأن النفل يتأدى بنيّة الفرض، أما الفرض لا يتأدى بنية النفل، وإن كان يعرف الفرائض من النوافل لكن لا يعلم ما في الصلاة أي ما في نفس الصلاة الواحدة من الفريضة والسنة، جازت صلاته؛ لأنه إذا عرف الفرائض ينوي الفرائض. انتهى.
And for the validity of performing the obligation, one of two things is required — and they are the minimum by which the obligation is fulfilled. The first of them is: knowing the modality of prayer, that is, knowing the reality of what is in it of the obligatory characteristics, meaning that it is fard, like his belief that the two rak'ahs of Fajr are fard, and that the four of Zuhr are fard, and that the sunnah of Fajr is two rak'ahs other than the fard, and that the sunnah of Zuhr is four other than the fard, and so on for the rest of the prayers, such that he distinguishes them in the manner we mentioned. The condition is not that he distinguishes what the Fajr prayer and the like contain of fard and sunnah, like his belief that standing is a pillar, the thana' and ta'awwudh are sunnah, recitation is fard, and tasbih is sunnah. Rather, the intended meaning is distinguishing the prayer itself as being fard, so it is distinguished from the sunnah characteristics by his belief that the rak'ahs he prays other than the fard are sunnah, like the regular sunan and others. The second of the two things is referred to by his saying: 'And the worshipper's belief that they — meaning the prayers he performs — are all fard,' like his belief that all four in Fajr are fard, and the five in Maghrib are fard, and he prays three rak'ahs of them separately. Because a supererogatory act is valid with the intention of fard, not the opposite. And he referred to this by his saying: 'So that he does not perform a supererogatory act thinking it is fard.' He said in al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid: A man who did not know that the five prayers are obligatory upon people, but he used to pray them — meaning without intending them in their times — it is not permissible and he must make them up, because he did not intend the fard, and intention is a condition. Similarly, if he knew that among them are fard rak'ahs and sunnah rak'ahs but does not know which is which, it is not valid for what we said, unless he prays behind an imam and intends his prayer. If he thought that all are fard, what he prayed suffices him, because supererogatory is performed with the intention of fard, but fard is not performed with the intention of supererogatory. If he knew the fara'id from the nawafil but does not know what is in the prayer — i.e., in the same prayer of fard and sunnah — his prayer is valid, because when he knows the fara'id, he intends the fara'id.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage defines a condition for the validity of fard prayers: the worshipper must either know the detailed obligatory and sunnah components of each prayer, or at least believe that all parts of the prayer are fard. The first option requires distinguishing, for example, that Fajr has two fard rak'ahs and two sunnah rak'ahs. The second option allows one to believe all rak'ahs are fard, since a supererogatory act can be performed with the intention of fard, but the opposite is not true. The text quotes al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid giving cases: if a person does not know the five prayers are obligatory at all, his prayer is invalid and must be repeated. If he knows some are fard and some sunnah but cannot differentiate, his prayer is invalid unless he follows an imam. If he mistakenly thinks all are fard, it is valid. If he knows the fard from sunnah generally but does not distinguish within a single prayer, it is valid because he intends the fard component. This condition ensures the proper intention (niyyah) is present.

Key Terms
تمييز الفرض من السنة (tamyiz al-fard min al-sunnah): The ability to distinguish obligatory rak'ahs from sunnah rak'ahs within a prayer.
نية الفرض (niyyat al-fard): Intention to perform the obligatory prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person knows that the five daily prayers are obligatory but does not know which rak'ahs are fard and which are sunnah within each prayer, what is the ruling?
A) His prayer is valid because he knows the prayers are obligatory
B) His prayer is invalid unless he follows an imam
C) His prayer is valid if he intends the entire prayer as fard
D) He must repeat the prayer after learning

Key Takeaway
For a fard prayer, correct intention is achieved either by knowing which parts are fard or by believing the entire prayer is fard.

The Four Pillars of Prayer and Classification of Conditions
Defines pillars and conditions of prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four agreed-upon pillars of prayer, distinguish them from conditions, and explain the Hanafi internal dispute regarding the final sitting and takbir al-tahrimah.

Core Idea
Prayer has four pillars and two kinds of conditions; the dispute over the final sitting affects whether it is a pillar or condition.

This lesson clarifies the essential building blocks of prayer. While many elements are required, only four are unanimously considered pillars (arkan) that must be performed within the prayer itself. Other requirements are conditions (shurut), divided between those that must be present before starting and those that must be maintained throughout. A key Hanafi internal dispute over the final sitting and opening takbir will sharpen your understanding of how these classifications work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four agreed-upon pillars
From the passage, list the four elements called 'the pillars agreed upon' (الاركان المتفق عليها). They are standing (qiyam), recitation (qira'ah), bowing (ruku'), and prostration (sujud).
These are the only elements that are pillars by consensus in the Hanafi school.
2
Note the disputed elements
The passage mentions that some consider the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) and the opening takbir (takbir al-tahrimah) as pillars. Recognize that these are not agreed upon; they are subject to internal Hanafi ikhtilaf.
The practical consequence (thamarah) of this dispute was explained in the previous lesson.
3
Classify the rest as conditions (shurut)
All other mentioned elements are conditions. The passage divides them into two categories: conditions for the validity of beginning the prayer (shurut al-in'aqad) and conditions for the continuity of validity (shurut al-dawam).
External conditions: purification, covering 'awrah, facing qiblah, time, intention, takbir. Internal conditions: include remaining in purity and facing qiblah throughout.
4
Apply the classification
Consider a scenario: someone prays without the final sitting. Is the prayer valid? The answer depends on whether the final sitting is a pillar or a condition. If a pillar, the prayer is invalid. If a condition, it may be valid if the omission was unintentional (per earlier discussion).
This demonstrates why the classification matters in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أراد التنبيه على الأركان وغيرها مما سبق فقال: (وَالأرْكَانُ) المتفق عليها ( مِنَ المَذْكُورَاتُ) التي بينـاهـا بـأكثر من سبعة وعشرين (أربَعَةٌ) وهي (القيام)، والقراءة، والركوع والسجود. وقيل: القعود الأخير مقدارَ التَّشَهدِ) ركن أيضاً وقيل : شرط، وقد علمت ذلك وثمرة الخلاف فيه، وقيل التحريمة أيضاً ر (وبَاقِيها ) أي: المذكورات (شَرَائِط: بعضُها شرط لصحة الشروع في الصَّلاةِ، وهو ما كــان خـارجـهـا ) وهـو : الطهارة من الحدث والخبث وستر العورة واستقبال القبلة والوقت والنية والتحريمة، (وغيـره شــرط لدوام صحتها ) وقد علمت ذلك بفضل الله ومنه وله الشكر على التوفيق لجمعها بعد التفرق.
Then he intended to draw attention to the pillars and other than them from what preceded, so he said: (And the pillars) that are agreed upon (from the mentioned) that we explained with more than twenty-seven (are four): (standing), recitation, bowing, and prostration. And it is said: the final sitting the extent of the tashahhud (is also a pillar) and it is said: a condition, and you have known that and the fruit of the difference in it. And it is said: the takbir al-tahrimah is also a pillar. (And the rest of them), i.e., the mentioned (are conditions: some of them are a condition for the validity of beginning the prayer, which is what was outside it), and that is: purification from hadath and najasah, covering the 'awrah, facing the qiblah, time, intention, and takbir al-tahrimah. (And other than that is a condition for the continuity of its validity), and you have known that by the grace of Allah and His favor, and to Him is thanks for the ability to compile them after their dispersal.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah is a commentary on the list of prayer requirements. The commentator reports that the author of the matn now points to the pillars (arkan) among the previously mentioned elements (which were listed earlier as over twenty-seven items). He states that the four agreed-upon pillars are: standing (qiyam), recitation (qira'ah), bowing (ruku'), and prostration (sujud). There is a difference of opinion regarding the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah): some consider it a fifth pillar, others a condition. The commentator reminds the reader that the practical consequence of this difference was explained earlier (in the previous lesson): if it is a condition, performing it while asleep is valid; if a pillar, it is not. Similarly, some consider the opening takbir (tahrimah) a pillar, but the text notes this as a minority view. The remaining elements from the list are all conditions (shurut). They are divided into two categories: conditions for the validity of beginning the prayer (shurut al-in'aqad), which are external to the prayer itself: purification from major and minor impurities (hadath) and physical impurities (najasah), covering the 'awrah, facing the qiblah, correct time, intention (niyyah), and the opening takbir (tahrimah). The second category is conditions for the continuity of the prayer's validity (shurut al-dawam), which are internal and must be maintained throughout the prayer; these include things like facing the qiblah and staying in a state of purity. The commentator ends by praising Allah for enabling him to compile these rulings.

Key Terms
ركن (rukn): Pillar of prayer; omission invalidates prayer.
شرط (shart): Condition for validity; divided into external and internal.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that begins the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is considered an agreed-upon pillar (rukn) of prayer?
A) Takbir al-tahrimah
B) Facing the qiblah
C) Recitation (qira'ah)
D) Intention

Key Takeaway
Prayer has four pillars (qiyam, qira'ah, ruku', sujud) and two kinds of conditions; the classification of the final sitting and takbir al-tahrimah is disputed within the Hanafi school.

The Four Pillars of Prayer and Classification of Conditions
Summary of the four pillars and classification of conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four agreed-upon pillars of prayer, classify the remaining elements as conditions, and explain the Hanafi position on the final sitting.

Core Idea
The four pillars of prayer are standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration; everything else is a condition, not a pillar.

This passage from Nur al-Idah clarifies the essential structure of prayer. It lists four agreed-upon pillars and then categorizes all other required elements as conditions. Understanding this distinction is crucial because omitting a pillar invalidates the prayer, whereas missing a condition may prevent the prayer from starting or continuing. The text also highlights a difference of opinion on the final sitting, which has practical consequences in the prayer's validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four agreed-upon pillars
Look for the explicit list: standing (qiyam), recitation (qira'ah), bowing (ruku'), and prostration (sujud). These are the only elements considered pillars (arkan) in the Hanafi school.
The text says 'الأركان... أربعة' and lists them.
2
Recognize the dispute on final sitting and takbir
Note that the text mentions 'وقيل' (it is said) regarding the final sitting and takbirat al-ihram. Some scholars consider them pillars, but the relied-upon Hanafi position is that the final sitting is wajib and the takbir is a condition.
This dispute affects the ruling on omission.
3
Classify the remaining elements as conditions (shurut)
The text divides conditions into two types: those required before starting prayer (shurut al-shuru') and those required for the prayer's validity throughout (shurut al-dawam). The external conditions include purification, covering awrah, facing qibla, time, intention, and takbir.
These are listed explicitly in the passage.
4
Apply the classification to a scenario
Consider the example given: a prayer leader who does not know the difference between obligatory and supererogatory prayers. The text shows how the ruling differs based on whether the prayer has a preceding sunnah.
This demonstrates the practical application of the classification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومثله في: والأركان من المذكورات أربعة: القيام، والقراءة، والركوع والسجود. وقيل: القعود الأخير مقدارَ التَّشَهْدِ. وباقيها شرائط، بعضُها شرط لصحةِ الشروع في الصَّلاةِ، وهو ما كان خارجها. وغيره شرط لدوام صحتها. الخلاصة» ثم قال: فلو أمّ قوماً وهو لا يعرف صلاة الفرض من صلاة النفل، ونوى الفرض الكُلّ جازت صلاته. وأما صلاة القوم فكل صلاة ليس لها سُنّة قبلها كالعصر والمغرب والعشاء تجوز، ولا تجوز صلاة القوم في كل صلاة لها سُنّة قبلها كالفجر والظهر. ثم أراد التنبيه على الأركان وغيرها مما سبق فقال: (وَالأرْكَانُ) المتفق عليها ( مِنَ المَذْكُورَاتُ) التي بينـاهـا بـأكثر من سبعة وعشرين (أربَعَةٌ) وهي (القيام)، والقراءة، والركوع والسجود. وقيل: القعود الأخير مقدارَ التَّشَهدِ) ركن أيضاً وقيل : شرط، وقد علمت ذلك وثمرة الخلاف فيه، وقيل التحريمة أيضاً ر (وبَاقِيها ) أي: المذكورات (شَرَائِط: بعضُها شرط لصحة الشروع في الصَّلاةِ، وهو ما كــان خـارجـها ) وهـو : الطهارة من الحدث والخبث وستر العورة واستقبال القبلة والوقت والنية والتحريمة، (وغيـره شــرط لدوام صحتها ) وقد علمت ذلك بفضل الله ومنه وله الشكر على التوفيق لجمعها بعد التفرق.
And similar to it in: The pillars from the mentioned things are four: standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration. And it is said: the final sitting to the extent of the tashahhud. And the rest are conditions, some of which are conditions for the validity of commencing prayer, and that is what is outside it. And other than that is a condition for the continuity of its validity. Al-Khulasa. Then he said: If he leads a people while he does not know obligatory prayer from supererogatory prayer, and intends the obligatory for all, his prayer is valid. As for the prayer of the people, every prayer that has no sunnah before it, like 'Asr, Maghrib, and 'Isha, is permissible; and it is not permissible for the people in every prayer that has a sunnah before it, like Fajr and Zuhr. Then he wanted to draw attention to the pillars and other things mentioned earlier, so he said: (And the pillars) that are agreed upon (from the mentioned things) which we have explained in more than twenty-seven (are four), namely (standing), recitation, bowing, and prostration. And it is said: the takbirat al-ihram is also a pillar. (And the rest of them), i.e., the mentioned things (are conditions: some of them are a condition for the validity of commencing prayer, and that is what was outside it), namely: purification from hadath and khabath, covering the 'awrah, facing the qibla, time, intention, and takbirat al-ihram. (And other than that is a condition for the continuity of its validity.) And you have known that by the grace of Allah and His favor, and to Him is thanks for granting success to compile them after dispersion.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is a summary of the pillars (arkan) and conditions (shurut) of prayer. The author, expanding on a previous summary from al-Khulasa, states that the agreed-upon pillars are four: standing (qiyam), recitation (qira'ah), bowing (ruku'), and prostration (sujud). There is a difference of opinion regarding the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah): some consider it a pillar, others a condition, with practical consequences for missing it. Similarly, the takbirat al-ihram is sometimes called a pillar. The remaining elements (e.g., facing qibla, time, intention) are conditions, divided into those required before starting (shurut al-shuru') and those required for the prayer's validity throughout (shurut al-dawam). The author also notes a related ruling: a prayer leader who does not know obligatory from supererogatory prayers but intends the obligatory for all is valid; but the congregation's prayer is valid only if the prayer has no preceding sunnah (like 'Asr, Maghrib, 'Isha).

Key Terms
ركن (rukn): An integral part of the prayer whose omission invalidates the entire prayer.
شرط (shart): A condition external to the prayer's essence; without it the prayer is invalid either at start or throughout.
التحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that initiates the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Understanding the distinction between pillars (arkan) and conditions (shurut) is essential for proper prayer validity; the final sitting is a wajib, not a rukn.

Covering Awrah with Impure or Partial Cover
Rulings on covering awrah with impure or partial cover

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for covering the awrah when only impure or partial cover is available, and identify the operative ruling when only one part can be covered.

Core Idea
Covering the awrah takes priority - use any available cover, even impure or silk, rather than pray naked.

This passage from Nur al-Idah covers situations where the worshipper lacks a proper clean garment. The rulings prioritize covering the awrah over other concerns, such as purity of the garment or the normal prohibition of silk for men. Even if the cover is impure or made of grass or mud, it must be used to avoid praying completely naked. The passage also addresses partial cover and the preferred area to shield when full coverage is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall obligation
Recognize that covering the awrah is wajib; the passage gives exceptions when proper cover is unavailable.
The ruling is for cases of necessity (dharurah).
2
Apply the quarter rule
When the available cover has at least a quarter pure, one must use it and cannot pray naked. If less than a quarter is pure, one has a choice but the impure garment is preferred over nakedness.
The quarter (rub') is a standard measure in Hanafi fiqh for purity rulings.
3
Handle less than a quarter pure
If less than a quarter of the cover is pure, the worshipper may choose between using the impure garment or praying naked with gestures. However, using the impure cover is more beloved (ahabb).
This balances the obligation to cover awrah with the prohibition of impurity.
4
Manage partial cover
If only part of the awrah can be covered, it must be used. There is a difference of opinion on which part to cover: the back (dubur) or the front (qubul). The preferred view is to cover the back because it is more exposed during sujud and ruku'.
For a woman, if praying standing exposes a quarter of a limb, she should pray sitting to cover it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا إعادة على فاقد ما يستر عورته ولو حريراً، أو حشيشاً، أو طيناً، فإن وجده ولو بالإباحة وربعه طاهر لا تصح صلاته عارياً على الأصح، وخير إن طهر أقل من ربعه، وصلاته في ثوب نجس الكل أحب من صلاته عرياناً، ولو وجد ما يستر بعض العورة وجب استماله. ويستر القبل والدبر، فإن لم يستر إلا أحدهما قيل يستر الدبر وقيل القبل. ولو صلت قائمة ينكشف ربع عضو منها وإن صلت جالسة استتر تصلي جالسة لأن ترك القيام أهون.
And there is no repetition upon one who lacks something to cover his awrah, even if it is silk, or grass, or mud. If he finds it even by permission and a quarter of it is pure, his prayer is not valid while naked according to the most correct view. And he is given a choice if less than a quarter is pure. His prayer in a completely impure garment is more beloved than his prayer while naked. And if he finds something that covers part of the awrah, its use is obligatory. He covers the front and back. If it does not cover except one of them, it is said: he covers the back, and it is said: he covers the front. And if she prays standing and a quarter of her limb becomes exposed, but if she prays sitting it is covered, she prays sitting because leaving standing is easier.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage covers situations where a person has no proper cover for the awrah. Even if the available cover is silk (normally prohibited for men), or grass, or mud, it must be used to avoid praying completely naked. If the cover found has a quarter that is pure, one must wear it and cannot pray naked. If less than a quarter is pure, one has a choice: praying in that impure garment is better than naked, but one may also pray naked with gestures. If only partial cover exists, one must cover the entire awrah; if not possible, there is a difference on which part to cover first (back or front). The passage also notes a special case: if a woman's quarter limb is exposed when standing, she should sit to cover it, as leaving standing is easier than exposing awrah. The overall principle: covering awrah is prioritized over other rulings.

Key Terms
ربع الشيء (rub' al-shay'): One quarter of the cover; if a quarter is pure, one must use it and cannot pray naked.
عارياً (ariyan): Praying completely naked (without any cover).
قبل (qubul): The front private parts (genitals).
دبر (dubur): The rear private parts (anus).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person finds a garment that is completely impure (najis kull), what is the ruling?
A) He must pray naked as the garment is impure.
B) He should pray in the impure garment and it is better than naked.
C) He must purify the garment before praying.
D) He may choose between naked and impure garment.

Key Takeaway
The principle is: covering the awrah overrides other concerns; use any available cover, even impure or silk, and if only partial cover is possible, covering the back is preferred.

Salah — Prayer

Ruling When Covering Has One Quarter Pure
Ruling when covering has at least one quarter pure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a person finds a covering that is at least one quarter pure and explain why prayer naked is invalid.

Core Idea
If a covering has one quarter pure, you must use it; prayer naked is invalid.

This lesson focuses on the first scenario: when you find a covering material that is at least one quarter pure. The Hanafi school rules that you must use it, and praying naked without it is invalid. The key principle is that a quarter of a garment stands in place of the whole for covering obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Condition
The condition is that the person finds a covering (cloth, grass, mud, turbid water) and at least one quarter of it is pure (tahir). The covering must be usable, even if permission is needed to obtain it.
The covering can be impure except for the quarter.
2
State the Ruling
The ruling is that it is wajib to use this covering. If the person prays naked while this covering is available, the prayer is not valid (la tasihhu).
The phrase 'la tasihhu salatuhu ariyan' means the prayer is invalid.
3
Understand the Principle
In Hanafi fiqh, a quarter of something can stand in place of the whole in matters of covering. This is based on the principle that the obligation of covering is fulfilled by covering the majority of the awrah, and a quarter is considered sufficient to meet that requirement.
This principle also applies in tayammum.
4
Apply to a Scenario
If a man finds a torn cloth that is one quarter pure, he must cover his awrah with it. If he prays naked, his prayer is invalid even if the cloth is impure except for that quarter.
The ruling applies similarly for women.

And in 'al-Bahr' and from 'al-Mubtagha' with ghain: if he has a piece with which he covers the smallest part of the 'awrah and does not cover, the prayer is invalid. End. And in 'al-Khulasa': If a woman finds what covers a quarter of her body and quarter of her head, and she leaves covering the head, her prayer is not valid. And if it covers less than a quarter, leaving the covering does not harm her. End. And covering is better to reduce exposure, thus in 'al-Bahr'. And it is recommended for the naked person to pray sitting with gestures, extending his legs toward the qiblah, because of covering. (And if) the naked person (prays standing with gestures) standing, performing (bowing and prostration, it is valid because he performs the pillars, so he may incline to whichever he wishes, but the first is preferred as we mentioned. And if he prays naked while having a garment he did not know about, it is not sufficient, as narrated from Abu Hanifa. And al-Karkhi mentioned that it is on the disagreement about the one who forgot water in his luggage. And the distinguishing factor according to the first narration is that clothing has no substitute, so it transfers to him and he did not perform the original obligation nor its substitute, unlike wudu' because it has a substitute (tayammum), and unlike the qiblah because it has a substitute (direction of best estimation), as in 'al-Tajnisi wal-Mazid'.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on covering the 'awrah for prayer when only impure or insufficient material is available. The author presents several scenarios. First, if a person finds a covering (cloth, grass, mud, or turbid water) that is at least one quarter pure, he must cover himself and his prayer naked is invalid. The principle is that a quarter of a thing stands in place of the whole in this context, due to the importance of covering. If the covering has less than a quarter pure, the person has a choice between three options: praying in that garment (best), praying naked while sitting with gestures, or praying naked while standing with full movements (least preferred). The general rule is that when faced with two equal evils, one may choose, but when they differ, the lesser must be chosen. Additional rulings include: if only one part (front or back) can be covered, there are two opinions on which to cover (the back due to its exposure in bowing/prostration, or the front because it faces the qiblah and cannot be covered otherwise). A note clarifies that covering with untanned animal skin from a dead animal invalidates prayer because its impurity is more severe. Also, if a woman finds a covering that covers a quarter of her body and head, she must cover both; leaving the head uncovered invalidates the prayer. It is recommended for a naked person to pray sitting with gestures toward the qiblah for maximum covering. Finally, if a person prays naked while unaware that a garment is available, the prayer is not valid because clothing has no substitute in that situation, unlike wudu' or qiblah direction.

Key Terms
ربع (rub'): One quarter of the garment; if pure, it suffices for covering obligation.
ساتر (satir): Any material that can cover the awrah, including impure cloth, grass, mud, or turbid water.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) He must wash the garment before praying.
D) He should pray without covering because the majority is impure.

Key Takeaway
A garment that has one quarter pure obligates its use for covering in prayer; praying naked invalidates the prayer.

Definition of 'Awrah for Men and Female Slaves
Defines 'awrah boundaries for men and female slaves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of a man's 'awrah, identify the relied-upon opinion, and explain the additional covering for female slaves.

Core Idea
A man's 'awrah excludes the navel but includes the knee; a female slave must also cover her belly and back.

Covering the 'awrah is a condition for valid prayer. This passage from Imdad al-Fattah defines the exact boundaries for men and female slaves according to the Hanafi school, based on the hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ). It also presents the textual analysis that led the Hanafis to exclude the navel but include the knee, and notes alternative internal opinions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
State that covering the 'awrah is wajib in prayer, and the passage defines its boundaries for men and female slaves. The primary proof is the hadith: 'The 'awrah of a man is what is between his navel to his knee.'
2
Analyse the hadith interpretation
Examine how the word 'to' (ila) is interpreted as 'with' (ma'a), making the knee inclusive. Another hadith explicitly states 'The knee is from the 'awrah', confirming inclusion. The navel is excluded because the hadith says 'between his navel' (ma bayna surratihi), which implies the navel itself is not included.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There are three opinions: Zahir al-Riwayah (below navel to below knee, knee included), Abu 'Ismah (navel inclusive), and Muhammad ibn al-Fadl (from the hairline). Understand that the first is the mufta bihi.
4
Confirm the mufta bihi
The text declares that the Zahir al-Riwayah is the relied-upon definition. Abu Hanifa's position is that the navel is not 'awrah and the knee is.
5
Apply the extension for female slaves
According to Abu Hanifa, a female slave (of any category) must cover additionally the belly and back beyond the male 'awrah. This is due to the existence of slavery, which reduces her covering compared to a free woman but increases it compared to a man.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَعَوْرَةُ الرّجُل حُراً كان أو رقيقياً ما بين السُّرَّةِ ومنتهى الرُّكبةِ لقوله : (عَورَةُ الرَّجلِ مَا بَينَ سُرِّتِهِ إِلى رُكْبَتِهِ » ) ويروى مــا دون سرته حتى يجاوز ركبته، وكلمة إلى نحملها على كلمة مع عملاً بكلمة حتى، أو عملاً بقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: (( الركبةُ مِنَ العورة» (۳) وبهذا تبين أن السرة ليست مــن الـعــورة والركبة منها. وقال أهل اللغة: سميت العورة عورة لقبح ظهورها ولغض الأبصار عنها، مأخوذة مـن الـعــور وهـو النقص والعيب والقبح وعلى ما ينبغي ستره، وعلــى مـا يستحى منه، ومنــه عــور الـعـيـن، والكلمـة العوراء القبيحة، وفي الشرع على ما يفترض ستره في الصلاة، وهذا الذي ذكرناه من تحديد العورة هو «ظاهر الرواية » . وقيل : ابتداؤها من السرة، وقائله « أبو عصمة وقيل : ابتداؤها من المنبت وقائله محمد بن الفضل كما في ( الدراية » ، (وَتَزيدُ عَلَيْهِ) أي: على الرجل (الأمةُ) (۳) القنّة، وأم الولد)، والمدبرة، والمكاتبة)، والمستسعاة ) عند أبي حنيفة لوجـود الـرق (البطن، والظَّهْرَ)؛
And the 'awrah of a man, whether free or slave, is what is between the navel and the end of the knee, due to his statement: 'The 'awrah of a man is what is between his navel to his knee.' And it is also narrated: 'What is below his navel until it passes his knee.' And we interpret the word 'to' as 'with' in accordance with the word 'until', or in accordance with his statement, peace be upon him: 'The knee is part of the 'awrah.' And by this it becomes clear that the navel is not from the 'awrah, and the knee is from it. And the linguists said: It is called 'awrah because of the ugliness of its appearance and the lowering of gazes from it, derived from 'awr meaning deficiency, defect, and ugliness, and what is worthy of being covered, and what one is ashamed of, from which is 'awr of the eye, and the 'awra' (one-eyed) word meaning ugly. And in the Shari'ah it refers to what is obligatory to cover in prayer. And this which we have mentioned of defining the 'awrah is the 'Zahir al-Riwayah'. And it is said: its beginning is from the navel, said by Abu 'Ismah. And it is said: its beginning is from the hairline, said by Muhammad ibn al-Fadl as in 'al-Diraya'. (And added to it) i.e., to the man (the female slave) (the bondswoman, umm walad, mudabbara, mukataba, mustas'at) according to Abu Hanifa due to the existence of slavery (the belly and the back).
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage defines the 'awrah (parts to be covered) for men and additionally for female slaves. The relied-upon opinion (Zahir al-Riwayah) states that a man's 'awrah is from below the navel to below the knee, including the knee itself, based on the hadith: 'The 'awrah of a man is what is between his navel to his knee.' The scholars explain that the word 'to' (ila) is interpreted as 'with' (ma'a) or as inclusive, so the knee is part of the 'awrah. The navel is excluded. Linguistic derivation: 'awrah comes from 'awr meaning defect or ugliness. There are two minor alternative opinions: one by Abu 'Ismah says it starts at the navel, and another by Muhammad ibn al-Fadl says it starts from the hairline (above the pubic area), but these are not the relied-upon view. For female slaves (all categories: qinnah, umm walad, mudabbara, mukataba, mustas'at), according to Abu Hanifa, they must cover additionally the belly and back, because slavery reduces the 'awrah standards compared to free women, but increases it relative to free men due to the potential for fitnah.

Key Terms
عورة ('awrah): The body parts that must be covered during prayer; for men, from below navel to below knee including knee.
سرة (surrah): Navel; according to the relied-upon opinion, it is not part of the 'awrah.
ركبة (rukbah): Knee; included in the 'awrah according to the hadith 'The knee is from the 'awrah'.
أمة (amah): Female slave; her 'awrah in prayer includes additional areas (belly and back) beyond that of a free man.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The navel and the knee.
B) The navel but not the knee.
C) The knee but not the navel.
D) Both the navel and the knee are excluded.

Key Takeaway
The Zahir al-Riwayah defines a man's 'awrah from below the navel to below the knee (knee included); a female slave additionally covers her belly and back.
