Ruling on the Prayer of a Naked Person
States the recommended posture and validity of standing prayer for a naked person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended posture for a naked person's prayer and apply the ruling regarding an unknown garment.

Core Idea
Sitting with gestures is best; standing is valid; unknown clothing invalidates the prayer.

When a person has no clothing to cover their 'awrah, the prayer still has specific guidelines to maximize modesty. This passage from Nur al-Idah clarifies the preferred posture and addresses a nuanced case: if the person later discovers they had a garment they were unaware of, the prayer is invalid according to Abu Hanifa. Understanding these details helps ensure the prayer meets the conditions of validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on posture
Read the passage to find the recommended (mandub) posture for the naked person. Note that it is sitting with gestures and legs extended toward the qibla.
2
Analyze the validity of standing
The text states that standing with actual bowing and prostration is valid because the pillars are performed. Recognize that this is a valid option, though less preferred.
3
Examine the unknown garment scenario
Find the condition: if the naked person had a garment they did not know about, the prayer does not suffice. This is narrated from Abu Hanifa.
4
Understand the legal reasoning (qiyas)
The text differentiates clothing from wudu and qibla: clothing has no substitute, so if it was available unknowingly, the obligation transfers to it and the prayer is invalid. Compare with wudu (substitute: tayammum) and qibla (substitute: ijtihad).
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Al-Karkhi relates this to a difference of opinion (khilaf) between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the case of forgetting water. Understand the basis of the disagreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والستر أفضل تقليلاً للانكشاف، كذا في ( البحر». ونُدِبَ صلاة العــاري جالساً بالإيماء، ماداً رِجْلَيْهِ نحوَ القِبْلَةِ لما فيه من الستر (فإنْ صَلَّى) العاري (قائماً بالإيماء) قائماً آتياً (بالركوع والسجودِ، صح لإتيانه بالأركان، فيميل إلى أيهما شاء، والأفضل الأول كما قدمناه ولـــو صلى عارياً وعنده ثوب لم يعلم به لا تجزئه، كذا روى عن أبي حنيفة، وذكر « الكرخي»: أنـه عـلـى الخلاف في الذي نسي الماء في رحله، ووجه الفرق على الرواية الأولى أن الكسوة لا بدل لها، فتنتقل إليه فلم يكن آتياً بأصل الفرض ولا ببدله، بخلاف الوضوء لأن له بدلاً وهو التراب، وبخلاف القبلة لأن لها بدلاً وهو جهة تحريه كما في ( التجنيس والمزيد ».
And covering is better to minimize exposure, as in al-Bahr. And it is recommended for the naked person to pray sitting with gestures, extending his legs towards the qibla because of the covering it provides. If the naked person prays standing by gestures or by bowing and prostrating, it is valid because he performs the pillars. He may choose whichever he wishes, but the first is better as we have mentioned. If a naked person prays and has a garment he does not know about, it does not suffice him. This is narrated from Abu Hanifa. Al-Karkhi mentioned that it is based on the difference of opinion regarding one who forgot water in his luggage. The distinction according to the first narration is that clothing has no substitute, so the obligation transfers to it and he did not perform the original obligation nor its substitute, unlike wudu which has a substitute (tayammum) and unlike the qibla which has a substitute (one's best guess). As in al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the prayer of a person who has no clothing to cover his 'awrah. It begins by stating that covering is better, then presents the ruling: it is recommended (mandub) for such a person to pray sitting while making gestures (īmā') for bowing and prostration, with legs extended towards the qibla to maximize covering. However, if he prays standing (either by gestures or by actual bowing and prostration), it is also valid because he has fulfilled the essential pillars of prayer. The better option is the first (sitting). The text then addresses a scenario: if a naked person prays and later discovers he had a garment he was unaware of, his prayer is not valid according to Abu Hanifa. This is because clothing is an indispensable condition for the validity of prayer; it has no substitute (unlike wudu which can be replaced by tayammum, or qibla which can be replaced by ijtihad). Al-Karkhi relates this to the case of one who forgets water in his luggage—a similar principle applies. The Hanafi position is that if one has the means to cover but is unaware, the obligation remains and the prayer is invalid.

Key Terms
العاري (al-'ārī): A person who has no clothing to cover the 'awrah during prayer.
الإيماء (al-īmā'): Gestures made with the head or body in place of bowing (rukū') and prostration (sujūd) when one cannot perform them normally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a naked person prays standing with actual bowing and prostration while completely uncovered, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid because he must sit.
B) The prayer is valid but sitting is better.
C) The prayer is invalid because he must cover his 'awrah.
D) The prayer is valid and standing is better.

Key Takeaway
The naked person should sit with gestures for maximum coverage, but standing is valid; however, if a garment was present unknowingly, the prayer is invalid per Abu Hanifa.

Minimum 'Awrah Coverage: The Ruling and Its Application
Ruling on minimal 'awrah covering and its proportional application.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the minimum 'awrah that must be covered for prayer validity and apply the rule on proportional covering when insufficient cloth is available.

Core Idea
Even a tiny uncovered part of the 'awrah invalidates prayer; but if only partial covering is available, the obligation adjusts proportionally.

This passage establishes that exposing even the smallest part of the 'awrah invalidates prayer. However, a scenario from al-Khulāsa shows that when a woman has only a limited cloth, the obligation is scaled back: if the cloth covers at least a quarter of her body and head, she must cover her head; otherwise she is excused. This lesson unpacks both the strict ruling and its practical nuance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Principle
The first sentence declares that if the smallest part (aṣghar) of the 'awrah is uncovered, the prayer becomes invalid. This establishes that covering the 'awrah is a strict condition for validity; any exposure of the minimal 'awrah (genitals) breaks the prayer.
The term 'aṣghar al-'awrah' refers to the genitals in the Hanafi school.
2
Analyze the Scenario from al-Khulāsa
The text then provides a specific case for a woman: if she has a cloth that covers at least a quarter of her body and a quarter of her head, she must cover her head; failure to do so invalidates the prayer. But if the cloth covers less than a quarter, leaving the head uncovered does not harm her prayer.
This is an example of the principle that the obligation to cover is proportional to the available covering.
3
Apply the Ruling to a New Scenario
Given a woman with a cloth that covers a quarter of her body but only an eighth of her head, is her prayer valid if she does not cover her head? According to the rule, since the cloth covers less than a quarter of her head, leaving it uncovered does not harm; her prayer is valid. Practice applying this distinction to similar cases.
The threshold of a quarter is specific to this ruling; it is a recognized measure in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text

أصغر العورة فلم يستر فسدت الصلاة. انتهى. وفي «الخلاصة» : وإذا وجد ما يغطي ربع جسدها وربع رأسها فتركت تغطية الرأس لا تجوز صلاتها، ولو كان يغطي أقل من الربع لا يضرهـا تـرك التغطية انتهى.

But if it covers less than a quarter, leaving it uncovered does not harm her. End.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the minimum amount of 'awrah that must be covered for prayer to be valid. It states that if even the smallest part (aṣghar) of the 'awrah is left uncovered, the prayer is invalid. The term 'aṣghar al-‘awrah' refers to the minimal area that constitutes 'awrah; in Hanafi fiqh, this is typically the genitals. The text then quotes from al-Khulāsa a specific application for a woman: if she has a cloth that covers at least a quarter of her body and a quarter of her head, she must cover her head; otherwise, her prayer is invalid. If the cloth covers less than a quarter of each, leaving the head uncovered does not harm her prayer. This is a nuanced ruling that considers the extent of covering available. The underlying principle is that covering the 'awrah is a condition (shart) for prayer; if the available covering is insufficient to cover the entire 'awrah, the obligation is reduced proportionally.

Key Terms
أصغر العورة (aṣghar al-'awrah): The minimal part of the 'awrah that if left uncovered invalidates prayer; in Hanafi, it is the genitals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Her prayer is valid only if she covers her entire body.
D) Her prayer is invalid unless she covers her head with a different cloth.

Key Takeaway
The smallest part of the 'awrah must be covered or prayer is invalid; when resources are limited, the obligation to cover non-core parts (like a woman's head) is proportional—if the cloth covers less than a quarter, she is excused.

The 'Awrah of a Man: Definition, Proof, and Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Definition of a man's 'awrah with hadith evidence and intra-Hanafi differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi definition of a man's 'awrah, identify its primary hadith proof, and explain the intra-Hanafi differences regarding its boundaries.

Core Idea
A man's 'awrah is from below the navel to below the knee; the navel is excluded, the knee is included.

This lesson defines the 'awrah of a man according to the Hanafi school, which is the area that must be covered during prayer. The primary evidence comes from hadith, and the school's well-known transmission (zāhir al-riwāyah) settles the precise boundaries. We will also explore two minority opinions within the madhhab that differ slightly.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi definition
Read the passage to find the authoritative definition of a man's 'awrah. Note that it is the area 'between the navel and the end of the knee' – and that the navel itself is not included, but the knee is.
This is the 'zāhir al-riwāyah' position.
2
Identify the primary hadith proof
The passage cites a hadith: 'The 'awrah of a man is what is between his navel and his knee.' Also a second hadith: 'The knee is from the 'awrah.' Locate these in the Arabic text.
The hadith are of ahad transmission, so they are zannī in both thubūt and dalālah.
3
Understand the linguistic interpretation
Notice that the word 'ilā (to) in the first hadith is interpreted as 'ma'a (with), based on the second hadith which explicitly includes the knee. This is a key usulī move to exclude the navel but include the knee.
This linguistic twist is the basis for the Hanafi distinction between navel (excluded) and knee (included).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Two other views within the Hanafi school are mentioned: Abū 'Ismah holds that the 'awrah begins from the navel (including it), and Muhammad ibn al-Fadl holds that it begins from the pubic hairline (excluding the area above the pubes). Recognize that these are weak (marjūḥ) opinions.
The author of the text (likely al-Ḥaṣkafī or al-Shurunbulālī) prefers the zāhir al-riwāyah.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The passage states that the definition given first is the zāhir al-riwāyah, which is the relied-upon position for fatwa. Confirm that the navel is not part of the 'awrah and the knee is part of it.
This is the operative ruling (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَعَوْرَةُ الرّجُل حُراً كان أو رقيقياً ما بين السُّرَّةِ ومنتهى الرُّكبةِ لقوله : (عَورَةُ الرَّجلِ مَا بَينَ سُرِّتِهِ إِلى رُكْبَتِهِ » ) ويروى مــا دون سرته حتى يجاوز ركبته، وكلمة إلى نحملها على كلمة مع عملاً بكلمة حتى، أو عملاً بقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: (( الركبةُ مِنَ العورة» (۳) وبهذا تبين أن السرة ليست مـن الـعــورة والركبة منها. وقال أهل اللغة: سميت العورة عورة لقبح ظهورها ولغض الأبصار عنها، مأخوذة مـن الـعــور وهـو النقص والعيب والقبح وعلى ما ينبغي ستره، وعلــى مـا يستحى منه، ومنــه عــور الـعـيـن، والكلمـة العوراء القبيحة، وفي الشرع على ما يفترض ستره في الصلاة، وهذا الذي ذكرناه من تحديد العورة هو «ظاهر الرواية » . وقيل : ابتداؤها من السرة، وقائله « أبو عصمة وقيل : ابتداؤها من المنبت وقائله محمد بن الفضل كما في ( الدراية ».
And the 'awrah of a man, whether free or slave, is what is between the navel and the end of the knee, due to his saying: 'The 'awrah of a man is what is between his navel and his knee.' And it is narrated as: 'What is below his navel until it passes the knee.' The word 'ilā (to) is interpreted as 'ma'a' (with) in accordance with the word 'hattā' (until), or in accordance with his saying, peace be upon him: 'The knee is part of the 'awrah.' By this it becomes clear that the navel is not part of the 'awrah, and the knee is part of it. The linguists said: It is called 'awrah because of the ugliness of its appearance and the lowering of the eyes from it, derived from 'awr which is deficiency, defect, and ugliness, and that which should be covered, and that which one is ashamed of. From it comes 'awr al-'ayn (blemish of the eye) and al-kalimatu al-'awrā' (ugly word). In sacred law, it is that which it is obligatory to cover during prayer. And this definition of the 'awrah that we have mentioned is the 'zāhir al-riwāyah'. And it was said: its beginning is from the navel, and its proponent is Abū 'Ismah. And it was said: its beginning is from the pubic hairline, and its proponent is Muhammad ibn al-Fadl, as in al-Dirāyah.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage defines the 'awrah of a man (whether free or slave) as the area between the navel and the knee, including the knee but not the navel. The primary evidence is a hadith: 'The 'awrah of a man is what is between his navel and his knee.' There is another narration that says 'below his navel until it passes the knee.' The author explains that the word 'to' (ilā) is interpreted as 'with' (ma'a) to include the knee, consistent with another hadith: 'The knee is part of the 'awrah.' The passage then gives a linguistic analysis of the word 'awrah, deriving it from deficiency and ugliness. The legal definition in the Hanafi school is that which must be covered during prayer. The author emphasizes that this definition is the 'zāhir al-riwāyah' (the well-known transmission from the founding Imams). However, there are two other opinions mentioned: one by Abū 'Ismah that the 'awrah begins from the navel (thus including the navel), and another by Muhammad ibn al-Fadl that it begins from the pubic hairline (thus excluding the navel and the area above the pubes). The relied-upon (muftā bihī) position is the first: from below the navel to below the knee, with the knee included.

Key Terms
عورة ('awrah): In sacred law, that which must be covered during prayer; for a man, between navel and knee.
ظاهر الرواية (zāhir al-riwāyah): The well-known and authoritative transmission from Imam Muhammad in the six core books (Zahir al-Riwayah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The knee

D) Neither the navel nor the knee

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi for a man's 'awrah is from below the navel to below the knee, with the navel excluded and the knee included, as established by the zāhir al-riwāyah.

Additional 'Awrah of a Slave Woman
States the additional 'awrah of slave women beyond that of a man

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's position on the additional 'awrah of a slave woman and explain the illa (effective cause) of slavery that justifies the ruling.

Core Idea
A slave woman's 'awrah includes her abdomen and back beyond a man's, due to the presence of slavery.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling regarding the 'awrah (parts that must be covered) of a slave woman (amah) according to Imam Abu Hanifa. While a man's 'awrah is between the navel and knee, a slave woman must additionally cover her abdomen and back. The passage provides the legal reasoning (ta'lil) for this distinction: the presence of slavery (riqq). This ruling illustrates how social status influences fiqh rulings and highlights an intra-Hanafi difference with the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is covering the 'awrah during salah. The ruling is that a slave woman must cover her abdomen and back in addition to the man's 'awrah. Identify the hukm level: wajib.
Covering the 'awrah is a condition for the validity of salah.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The text provides the illa: 'due to the presence of slavery' (li wujūd al-riqq). This indicates that the ruling is derived by qiyas (analogy) or direct consideration of the attribute. The dalil is the illa itself, not a specific text from Quran or Sunnah.
The proof is not naqli but 'aqli based on the meaning of slavery.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The presence of slavery reduces the woman's honor/status in matters of covering, making her 'awrah intermediate between a man and a free woman. The illa is 'slavery' which necessitates covering more than a man but less than a free woman.
Other schools use different illa, e.g., likelihood of fitnah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) hold that a slave woman's 'awrah is the same as a man's (navel to knee). They may rely on the principle that the ‘awrah is determined by desire, which is less for a slave due to her low status.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The muftā bihī (operative) position in later Hanafi fatwa is often the view of the Sahibayn for practical ease, but the text here presents Abu Hanifa's view as the primary teaching.
The choice may depend on context and custom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَتَزيدُ عَلَيْهِ) أي: على الرجل (الأمةُ) (٣) القنّة، وأم الولد)، والمدبرة، والمكاتبة)، والمستسعاة ) عند أبي حنيفة لوجـود الـرق (البطن، والظَّهْرَ)؛
(And it is added to it) i.e., to the man (the female slave) — the qinnah, the umm walad, the mudabbara, the mukatabah, and the mustas'ah — according to Abu Hanifa, due to the presence of slavery, (the abdomen and the back).
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage states the ruling regarding the 'awrah of a slave woman (amah). According to Abu Hanifa, a slave woman, regardless of her specific status (qinnah: fully owned, umm walad: mother of her master's child, mudabbara: freed upon master's death, mukatabah: contracted to purchase freedom, mustas'ah: partially freed and working to free the rest), has more 'awrah than a man. In addition to covering the same area as a man (between navel and knee), she must also cover her abdomen (al-baṭn) and back (al-ẓahr). The reason given is 'due to the presence of slavery' (li wujūd al-riqq). The underlying principle is that a slave woman is not treated like a free woman in terms of covering; her 'awrah is less than that of a free woman (which covers the entire body) but more than that of a man. The abdomen and back are specifically mentioned. Note: This is the position of Abu Hanifa; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) may differ, holding that the slave woman's 'awrah is the same as a man's. The muftā bihī position in later Hanafi fatwa is often the more protective view, but the text here presents Abu Hanifa's view as the one to follow (as indicated by the structure of the text).

Key Terms
الأمة (al-amah): A female slave; includes various types such as qinnah (fully owned), umm walad (mother of master's child), mudabbara (freed upon death), mukatabah (contracting freedom), mustas'ah (working for freedom).
الرق (al-riqq): Slavery; the legal status of being owned as property.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa rules that a slave woman's 'awrah includes the abdomen and back beyond a man's, based on the illa of slavery, but this is contested within the Hanafi school.

Free Woman's 'Awrah: Face, Hands, and Feet Excluded
Defines the 'awrah of a free woman and provides evidence from Quran and Hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the 'awrah of a free woman, identify the Quranic verse and hadith used as proof, and explain the ikhtilaf regarding the feet.

Core Idea
A free woman's 'awrah is all except face, hands, and feet — proven by Quran, Hadith, and Companion practice.

This lesson defines the 'awrah of a free woman (ḥurrah) according to the Hanafi school. The ruling is derived from the Quranic verse (al-Nur 31) and a hadith forbidding the woman in ihrām from wearing gloves and niqāb. The text also discusses an internal ikhtilaf regarding whether the feet are 'awrah. Understanding this ruling is essential for correct performance of salah and proper covering in front of non-mahram men.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Extract from the source the exact statement: 'All of the body of a free woman is 'awrah except her face, her two hands, and her two feet.' Note that this is the general rule.
The exception includes the face, the palms and back of the hands (kuffān), and the feet (qadamayn).
2
Locate the Quranic proof
The text cites Quran 24:31: 'and not to reveal their adornment except that which is apparent thereof.' The Companions Ibn 'Abbās and Ibn 'Umar interpreted 'that which is apparent' as the face and hands.
This verse is the primary dalil for the exception.
3
Identify the Hadith proof
The Prophet (PBUH) forbade a woman in ihrām from wearing gloves (qafāzayn) and the niqāb. The Hanafi argument: if the face and hands were 'awrah, covering them would be obligatory even in ihrām, but the prohibition shows they are not 'awrah.
This is a proof by implication (dalālah al-iltizām).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on feet
The text states that there are two narrations regarding the feet. The more correct (aṣaḥ) is that the feet are not 'awrah. This difference affects the ruling for covering feet during prayer and in public.
The muftā bihī position is that feet are not 'awrah.
5
Understand the distinction between free and slave women
The text contrasts the 'awrah of a free woman with that of a slave woman. The primary evidence for the free woman's 'awrah is from the Quran and Sunnah, while slave women have a less restrictive 'awrah (similar to a man's, with additional covering of the back and abdomen).
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school among the four major madhāhib.

Source Text

And all of the body of a free woman is 'awrah except her face, her two hands, and her two feet. Because they have a distinction (attractiveness) and looking at them is a cause of fitna. And other than that of her is not 'awrah, because 'Umar used to strike slave women to make them cover their heads and say: 'Take off your khimar, O Daffār, you are imitating free women.' And his saying: 'Sharaqa ṣadra al-qanāti bi al-dam' and another poet: 'When the news of the vizier came, the city walls and the humble mountains lowered themselves.' As in al-Mustasfā. And His saying: 'that delight the onlookers' (al-Tatfif 69) as in al-Mi'rāj. (Except her face, her two hands, and her two feet) due to His saying: 'and not to reveal their adornment except that which is apparent thereof' (al-Nur 31), and the intended meaning is the place of adornment and what is apparent of it is the face and two palms, said by Ibn 'Abbās and Ibn 'Umar: due to the necessity of showing it; and because the Prophet, peace be upon him, forbade the woman in ihrām from wearing gloves and the niqāb. If the face and hands were 'awrah, he would not have forbidden covering them with sewn garments. And regarding the foot, there are two narrations, and the more correct of the two is that it is not 'awrah.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage defines the 'awrah of a free woman (ḥurrah) as her entire body except her face, hands, and feet. The primary evidence is the Quranic verse (al-Nur 31): '...and not to reveal their adornment except that which is apparent thereof.' The Companions Ibn 'Abbās and Ibn 'Umar interpreted 'that which is apparent' as the face and hands. A secondary proof is that the Prophet forbade a woman in ihrām from wearing gloves (qafāzayn) and the face-veil (niqāb); if the face and hands were 'awrah, she would not be forbidden to cover them, since covering 'awrah is obligatory even in ihrām. The text also discusses the exception for feet: there are two narrations in the Hanafi school; the more correct (aṣaḥ) is that the feet are not 'awrah. The passage includes linguistic notes and historical reports about 'Umar's practice with slave women to argue that slave women have a different 'awrah (only abdomen and back additional to man's). This reinforces the distinction between free and slave women. The ruling for free women is that they must cover everything except the face, hands, and feet during prayer and in front of non-mahram men (with conditions regarding fitna).

Key Terms
الحرة (al-ḥurrah): A free woman (not a slave).
الكفان (al-kuffān): The two hands (palms and back, up to the wrist).
القدمين (al-qadamayn): The two feet.
القفازين (al-qafāzayn): Gloves worn by a woman in ihram.
النقاب (al-niqāb): Face veil covering the nose and mouth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Quranic evidence cited for the exception of face and hands from the 'awrah of a free woman?
A) Surah al-Nur 31: 'and not to reveal their adornment except that which is apparent thereof.'
B) Surah al-Ahzab 59: 'draw their cloaks over themselves.'
C) Surah al-Nur 30: 'lower their gaze.'
D) Surah al-Maidah 6: 'wash your faces and hands.'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that a free woman's 'awrah is her entire body except the face, hands, and feet, based on Quran 24:31, the ihram hadith, and Companion interpretation.

The Quarter-Limb Rule for 'Awrah Exposure in Prayer
States the ruling that exposing a quarter of an 'awrah limb invalidates prayer and discusses conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that exposure of a quarter of any 'awrah limb for one rukn invalidates prayer and distinguish between valid and invalid exposure scenarios.

Core Idea
Exposing a quarter of any 'awrah limb for one rukn invalidates prayer; less is forgiven.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah establishes a key rule in Hanafi fiqh: the invalidation of prayer due to 'awrah exposure begins at a quarter of a limb. The text also clarifies how to measure scattered exposure and what constitutes a single limb for this purpose. Understanding this threshold is essential for knowing when a prayer becomes invalid and when an imperfection is excused.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Covering the 'awrah is wajib in prayer; deliberate exposure of a quarter or more invalidates the prayer if conditions are met.
The ruling is specific to prayer; outside prayer, covering 'awrah is fard but exposure does not invalidate an act of worship.
2
Determine the threshold
The minimum amount that invalidates is exposure of a quarter of any single 'awrah limb. Less than a quarter is excused due to necessity.
The quarter is measured of the limb itself, not of the body.
3
Check the conditions
For invalidation, three conditions must be met: a cover is available, the exposure lasts for the duration of one rukn (e.g., time to say subhanallah three times), and the person is aware of the exposure.
If no cover is available (e.g., lost clothing), one prays as is and the prayer is valid.
4
Handle scattered exposure
If exposure is on multiple limbs, sum the exposed areas. If the total equals a quarter of the smallest exposed limb, the prayer invalidates.
This applies only when the exposure is scattered; if one limb has a quarter, it invalidates directly.
5
Apply the limb definitions
The text specifies which body parts are considered one limb for measurement (e.g., knee and thigh together, ear alone). Use these definitions to calculate the quarter.
Al-Karhki's estimation using dirham is rejected; the quarter rule is the relied-upon view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكشف ربع عُضو من أعضاء العورة يمنعُ صحةَ الصَّلاةِ. ولو تفرق الانكشاف على أعضاء من العورة، وكان جُمْلَةُ، ما تفرق يبلغ ربع أصغرِ الأعضاء المنكشفةِ مَنَع.
تنبيه: كل عضو هو عورة من المرأة إذا انفصل منها، في النظر إليه روايتان أحدهما: يجوز كما يجوز النظر إلى ريقها ودمها، والثانية: لا يجوز وهو الأصح، وكذا الذَّكر المقطوع من الرجل، وشعر عانته إذا حلق، الصحيح أنه لا يجوز. تنبيه آخر في ( النوازل ) نغمة المرأة عورة، وتعلمها القرآن من المرأة أحب، قــال عـلـيـه الصـلاة
والسلام: « التسبيح للرجال والتصفيق للنّساءِ» (۱) فلا يحسن أن يسمعها الرجل انتهى. قال الكمال: وعلى هذا لو قيل: إذا جهرت بالقراءة في الصلاة فسدت كان متجهاً ولهذا منـعـهـا عـلـيـه الصـلاة والسلام من التسبيح بالصوت لإعلام الإمام بسهوه إلى التصفيق انتهى. وذكر الإمام «أبو العباس القرطبي في كتابه في السماع : ولا يظن من لا فطنة عنده أنا إذا قلنا : صوت المرأة عورة أنـا نريد بذلك كلامها؛ لأن ذلك ليس بصحيح فإنا نجيز الكلام مع النساء الأجانب ومحاورتهـن عنـد الحاجة إلى ذلك، ولا نجيز لهن رفع أصواتهن ولا تمطيطها ولا تليينها وتقطيعها؛ لما في ذلــك مـن استمالة الرجال إليهن وتحريك الشهوات منهم، ومن هنا لم يجز أن تؤذن المرأة انتهى. كذا بخـط العلامة المقدسي رحمه الله. وكشفُ رُبْعِ عُضو مِنْ أَعْضَاءِ العَوْرَةِ) الغليظة أو الخفيفة مـــن الـرجــل والمرأة ( يمنعُ صِحةَ الصَّلاةِ) إن وجد ما يستره ومكث مكشوفاً قدر أداء ركن، وقيدنا بالربع؛ لأن ما دونه لا يمنع الصحة للضرورة؛ وبوجدان الساتر لأن فاقده يصلي عارياً، وبالمكث قدر أداء ركــن لأن الانكشاف الكثير في الزمن اليسير ،عفو، كما لو هبت ريح ف فكشفت جميع عورتـه فسترها من فوره لا يضر، كالانكشاف القليل في الزمن الطويل، وتقدير ( الكرخي » المانع من العورة الغليظة بالدرهم، ومن المخففة بالربع اعتباراً بالنجاسة الغليظة والخفيفة مردود، والركبة مع الفخذ عضو واحد في الأصح، وكعب المرأة مع ساقها، وأذنها بانفرادها، وثديها المنكسر، فإن كانت ناهداً فهو تبع لصدرها، والذكر بانفراده، والأنثيين (۳) بلا ضمهما إليه في الصحيح، ومـا بـيـن الـســرة والـعـانـة عضو كامل بجميع جوانب البدن. وكل ألية عورة والدبر ثالثهما في الصحيح، (ولو تفرق الانكشاف على أعضاء من العورة، وكان جُمْلَةُ، ما تفرق يبلغ ربع أصغر الأعضاء المنكشفة) يعني: التي انكشفت بعضها (مَنَعَ) صحة الصلاة إن طال زمن الانكشاف بقدر أداء ركن كما ذكرنا،
(1) أخرجه البخاري في العمل في الصلاة، باب التصفيق للنساء (۱۲۰۳)، ومسلم في الصلاة، باب: تسبيح الرجل وتصفيق المرأة (٤٢٢). (۲) أي: الخصيتان. معجم لغة الفقهاء / أنثيان /.
- YO-
Exposure of a quarter of a limb from the limbs of the 'awrah prevents the validity of prayer. And if the exposure is scattered over limbs of the 'awrah, and the total of what is scattered amounts to a quarter of the smallest exposed limb, it prevents.
Note: Every limb that is 'awrah from a woman, if it is separated from her, there are two narrations regarding looking at it: one is that it is permissible, just as it is permissible to look at her saliva and blood; the second is that it is not permissible, and that is the correct view. Similarly, the severed penis of a man, and his pubic hair if shaved, the correct view is that it is not permissible.
Another note in (al-Nawazil): The melodious voice of a woman is 'awrah, and teaching her the Quran by a woman is more beloved. The Prophet (peace and salutations upon him) said: 'Tasbih is for men, clapping for women.' So it is not proper for a man to hear her, end. Al-Kamal said: Based on this, if it were said: if she recites loudly in prayer, her prayer becomes invalid, that would be appropriate. That is why the Prophet (peace and salutations upon him) prevented her from tasbih with the voice to inform the imam of his forgetfulness, pointing to clapping, end. Imam Abu al-Abbas al-Qurtubi mentioned in his book on listening: Let not one lacking intellect think that when we say the woman's voice is 'awrah, we mean her speech; that is not correct, for we permit speaking with foreign women and conversing with them when needed. But we do not permit them to raise their voices, nor to elongate them, nor to soften them or break them, because that attracts men to them and arouses desires. Hence, a woman is not permitted to give the adhan, end. So in the handwriting of al-Maqdisi, may Allah have mercy on him. And exposure of a quarter of a limb from the limbs of the thick or thin 'awrah of a man and woman prevents the validity of prayer, provided that something to cover it is available and it remains uncovered for the duration of performing one rukn. We restricted it to a quarter because less than that does not prevent validity due to necessity; and to the availability of a cover because one without it prays naked; and to the duration of one rukn because much exposure in a short time is forgiven, just as if a wind blew and exposed all of his 'awrah and he covers it immediately, it does not harm, unlike small exposure over a long time. The estimation of al-Karhki that the restrictor for thick 'awrah is a dirham and for thin is a quarter, by analogy to thick and thin impurity, is rejected. The knee with the thigh is one limb according to the correct view, the woman's ankle with her shank, her ear alone, her breast if it is sagging - if it is prominent then it follows her chest; the penis alone, the testicles without including them to it according to the correct view; what is between the navel and the pubic area is one complete limb including all sides of the body. Every buttock is 'awrah, and the anus is the third of them according to the correct view. And if the exposure is scattered over limbs of the 'awrah, and the total of what is scattered amounts to a quarter of the smallest exposed limbs, meaning those that have been partially exposed, it prevents the validity of prayer if the duration of exposure is lengthy to the extent of performing one rukn, as we mentioned.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the invalidation of prayer by exposure of the 'awrah. It first states that exposing a quarter of an 'awrah limb invalidates prayer, and if the exposure is scattered over multiple limbs, the total must reach a quarter of the smallest limb. Then two notes: first, regarding a detached 'awrah limb - the correct view is that looking at it is not permissible, contrary to saliva and blood. Second, the woman's voice is 'awrah; she should not recite loudly in prayer, as the hadith says men should do tasbih and women clap when correcting the imam. Al-Qurtubi clarifies that speech is not 'awrah, but raising the voice or softening it is. The passage then revisits the quarter-limb rule with more conditions: a cover must be available, and the exposure must last the duration of one rukn (e.g., one prostration or bowing). Less than a quarter is forgiven; quick exposure is forgiven; small exposure over a long time is not. The estimation of Al-Karhki (dirham for thick, quarter for thin) is rejected. It then defines which parts constitute a single limb for the purpose of calculating the quarter: knee and thigh, woman's ankle and shank, ear alone, sagging breast (prominent breast follows chest), penis alone, testicles alone, area between navel and pubic area as one limb, buttocks and anus as two.

Key Terms
عورة ('awrah): Parts of the body that must be covered in prayer; exposure of a quarter or more invalidates it.
ربع عضو (rub' 'udw): One quarter of a limb; the threshold for invalidation of prayer due to exposure.
نغمة (naghama): Melodious voice; considered 'awrah in the sense that it may attract men.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a man's thigh (which is 'awrah) is exposed for the duration of one complete ruku', and the exposed area is exactly one quarter of the thigh, what is the ruling on his prayer?
A) His prayer is valid because he covered it after ruku'.
B) His prayer is invalid.
C) His prayer is valid if he was unaware.
D) His prayer is invalid only if the exposure lasted longer than one rukn.

Key Takeaway
Exposure of a quarter of any 'awrah limb for one rukn invalidates prayer; less than that is excused.

The 'Awrah of the Woman's Voice and Detached Limbs
Discusses the 'awrah of the woman's voice and detached limbs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that a woman's melodious voice is considered 'awrah in contexts that may attract men, and distinguish between permissible speech and forbidden vocal modulation.

Core Idea
A woman's voice is not forbidden speech, but its melodious use is 'awrah because it may attract men.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah addresses two important issues beyond the quarter-limb rule: the status of detached 'awrah limbs and the woman's voice. It clarifies that a severed limb remains 'awrah in terms of looking, and that a woman's voice is considered 'awrah only when she modulates it in a way that attracts men. The hadith 'Tasbih is for men, clapping for women' is cited to show that women should not raise their voices in prayer to alert the imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two notes in the passage
The passage contains two تنبيه (notes): one on detached limbs, another on the woman's voice. Focus on each separately.
The notes are subsidiary to the main ruling but are important for comprehensive understanding.
2
Analyze the ruling on detached limbs
For a detached 'awrah limb (e.g., severed hand), there are two narrations: one allows looking at it (like looking at saliva or blood), the other forbids. The correct view (الأصح) is that it is not permissible to look.
This applies to both the woman's severed limb and the man's severed penis and shaved pubic hair.
3
Understand the concept of 'naghama'
The term 'naghama' refers to a melodious voice. The passage states that the melodious voice of a woman is 'awrah. This is a specific ruling from al-Nawazil.
This does not mean all speech of a woman is 'awrah.
4
Examine the hadith and its application
The hadith 'التسبيح للرجال والتصفيق للنساء' indicates that women should clap rather than speak when alerting the imam to a mistake. This is used to support the idea that a woman's voice should not be raised in prayer.
Al-Kamal ibn al-Humam suggests that if a woman recites loudly in prayer, her prayer may become invalid because her voice is 'awrah.
5
Differentiate between speech and voice
Imam al-Qurtubi clarifies: when we say the woman's voice is 'awrah, we do not mean her speech. Speech is permissible when needed. It is the raising, elongating, softening, or breaking of the voice that is forbidden because it attracts men.
This distinction is crucial to avoid misunderstanding.

Source Text

Al-Qurtubi clarifies that speech is not 'awrah, but raising the voice or softening it is. The passage then revisits the quarter-limb rule with more conditions: a cover must be available, and the exposure must last the duration of one rukn (e.g., one prostration or bowing). Less than a quarter is forgiven; quick exposure is forgiven; small exposure over a long time is not. The estimation of Al-Karhki (dirham for thick, quarter for thin) is rejected. It then defines which parts constitute a single limb for the purpose of calculating the quarter: knee and thigh, woman's ankle and shank, ear alone, sagging breast (prominent breast follows chest), penis alone, testicles alone, area between navel and pubic area as one limb, buttocks and anus as two.

Key Terms
عورة ('awrah): Parts of the body that must be covered in prayer; also metaphorically applied to a woman's melodious voice.
نغمة (naghama): Melodious voice; considered 'awrah in the sense that it may attract men.
التسبيح للرجال والتصفيق للنّساءِ (al-tasbih lil-rijal wa al-tasfiq lil-nisa'): Hadith: men should say tasbih (subhanallah) to alert the imam, women should clap.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does Imam al-Qurtubi say the woman's voice is 'awrah?
A) Because all speech of women is forbidden
B) Because raising, softening, or elongating the voice attracts men
C) Because women should not pray aloud
D) Because the hadith says so without nuance

Key Takeaway
A woman's speech is not 'awrah, but her melodious voice is, due to its potential to attract men.

Salah — Prayer
beginner

The Ruling of Exposure During Prayer: Quarter and Conditions
Core ruling with conditions on exposure of awrah during prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions under which exposure of a private part invalidates prayer and apply the quarter-threshold rule to multiple limbs.

Core Idea
A prayer is invalid only if a quarter of a private part is exposed for the duration of one rukn.

In this lesson we examine the Hanafi ruling on covering the private parts during prayer. The author specifies that not all exposure invalidates; there is a precise threshold of one quarter of a limb and a minimum duration. We will break down the conditions and see how they apply in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is covering the private parts during prayer. The ruling: exposure of a quarter of a limb of the private part prevents the validity of prayer (makes it invalid).
The ruling applies to both thick and light private parts, for men and women.
2
List the three conditions for invalidation
The text states three conditions: (1) The person must have something to cover with (if not, he prays naked and it is valid). (2) The uncovered area must equal at least a quarter of that limb. (3) The exposure must last for the duration of performing one integral (rukn) of prayer, e.g., the time for one rukn like one tasbih.
If any condition is missing, the prayer is not invalidated.
3
Distinguish between thick and light private parts
The Hanafi school distinguishes between thick private parts (e.g., genitals, anus) and light private parts (e.g., thighs for women, but the text uses thick and light broadly). The quarter rule applies to both. The text mentions al-Karkhi's estimation (a dirham for thick, quarter for light) but rejects it, affirming the quarter rule for all.
Other schools may use different measures; this is a Hanafi specific threshold.
4
Apply the rule for exposure spread over multiple limbs
If the exposure is spread over several private parts, add the total uncovered area. If the sum equals a quarter of the smallest limb among those exposed, it invalidates. This prevents someone from circumventing the rule by exposing small portions of different limbs.
The smallest limb is used as the benchmark to avoid injustice.
5
Note the exceptions for brief exposure and lack of covering
A large exposure that is immediately covered (e.g., wind uncovers all, then covered instantly) does not invalidate. Similarly, a small amount of exposure (less than quarter) over a long time is also excused due to necessity, as poor people’s clothes often have small tears.
The ruling is based on ease and removing hardship.

تنبيه: كل عضو هو عورة من المرأة إذا انفصل منها، في النظر إليه روايتان أحدهما: يجوز كما يجوز النظر إلى ريقها ودمها، والثانية: لا يجوز وهو الأصح، وكذا الذَّكر المقطوع من الرجل، وشعر عانته إذا حلق، الصحيح أنه لا يجوز. تنبيه آخر في ( النوازل ) نغمة المرأة عورة، وتعلمها القرآن من المرأة أحب، قــال عـلـيـه الصـلاة والسلام: « التسبيح للرجال والتصفيق للنّساءِ» (۱) فلا يحسن أن يسمعها الرجل انتهى. قال الكمال: وعلى هذا لو قيل: إذا جهرت بالقراءة في الصلاة فسدت كان متجهاً ولهذا مـنـعـهـا عـلـيـه الصـلاة والسلام من التسبيح بالصوت لإعلام الإمام بسهوه إلى التصفيق انتهى. وذكر الإمام «أبو العباس القرطبي في كتابه في السماع : ولا يظن من لا فطنة عنده أنا إذا قلنا : صوت المرأة عورة أنــا نريد بذلك كلامها؛ لأن ذلك ليس بصحيح فإنا نجيز الكلام مع النساء الأجانب ومحاورتهـن عنـد الحاجة إلى ذلك، ولا نجيز لهن رفع أصواتهن ولا تمطيطها ولا تليينها وتقطيعها؛ لما في ذلــك مـن استمالة الرجال إليهن وتحريك الشهوات منهم، ومن هنا لم يجز أن تؤذن المرأة انتهى. كذا بخـط العلامة المقدسي رحمه الله. وكشفُ رُبْعِ عُضو مِنْ أَعْضَاءِ العَوْرَةِ) الغليظة أو الخفيفة مـــن الــرجــل والمرأة ( يمنعُ صِحةَ الصَّلاةِ) إن وجد ما يستره ومكث مكشوفاً قدر أداء ركن، وقيدنا بالربع؛ لأن ما دونه لا يمنع الصحة للضرورة؛ وبوجدان الساتر لأن فاقده يصلي عارياً، وبالمكث قدر أداء ركــن لأن انكشاف الكثير في الزمن اليسير عفو، كما لو هبت ريح فكشفت جميع عورتـه فسترها من فوره لا يضر، كالانكشاف القليل في الزمن الطويل، وتقدير ( الكرخي » المانع من العورة الغليظة بالدرهم، ومن المخففة بالربع اعتباراً بالنجاسة الغليظة والخفيفة مردود، والركبة مع الفخذ عضو واحد في الأصح، وكعب المرأة مع ساقها، وأذنها بانفرادها، وثديها المنكسر، فإن كانت ناهداً فهو تبع لصدرها، والذكر بانفراده، والأنثيين (۳) بلا ضمهما إليه في الصحيح، ومـا بـيـن الـســرة والـعـانـة عضو كامل بجميع جوانب البدن. وكل ألية عورة والدبر ثالثهما في الصحيح، (ولو تفرق الانكشاف على أعضاء من العورة، وكان جُمْلَةُ، ما تفرق يبلغ ربع أصغر الأعضاء المنكشفة) يعني: التي انكشفت بعضها (مَنَعَ) صحة الصلاة إن طال زمن الانكشاف بقدر أداء ركن كما ذكرنا، وإلا فلا.
( وإلأ ) أي : وإن لم يبلغ ربع أصغرها، أو بلغ ولم يطل زمن الانكشاف، (فلا) يمنع الصحة لأن قليل الانكشاف عفو عندنا للضرورة، فإن ثياب الفقراء لا تخلو عن قليل خرق كالنجاسة القليلة، وعم الحكم الفقير وغيره رفقاً بالكل لأصل الضرورة.
And the uncovering of a quarter of a limb from the limbs of the private part prevents the validity of prayer. And if the uncovering is spread over limbs of the private part, and the total of what is spread reaches a quarter of the smallest of the uncovered limbs, it prevents. Notice: Every limb that is a private part of a woman if separated from her, regarding looking at it there are two narrations: one: it is permissible as it is permissible to look at her saliva and blood, and the second: it is not permissible, and it is the more correct. Likewise, the male organ cut from a man, and his pubic hair if shaved, the correct view is that it is not permissible. Another notice in (al-Nawazil): The tone of a woman is a private part, and it is more beloved for her to learn the Quran from a woman. The Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم said: 'Tasbih is for men and clapping is for women.' So it is not good for a man to hear her. End. Al-Kamal said: Based on this, if it were said: If she raises her voice in recitation in prayer, it becomes invalid, it would be appropriate, and because of this the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم prevented her from using tasbih out loud to inform the imam of his forgetfulness, instead using clapping. End. And Imam Abu al-Abbas al-Qurtubi mentioned in his book on listening: And let the one without understanding not think that when we say 'the voice of a woman is a private part' we mean her speech; because that is not correct, for we permit speech with foreign women and conversing with them when needed, and we do not permit them to raise their voices, nor extend them, nor soften them, nor break them, because that attracts men to them and stirs desires from them. Hence, it is not permissible for a woman to give adhan. End. So in the handwriting of al-Allamah al-Maqdisi, may Allah have mercy on him. And the uncovering of a quarter of a limb from the limbs of the private part (the thick or light private part of the man and woman) prevents the validity of prayer (if he finds something to cover it and remains uncovered for the duration of performing a pillar. And we restricted it to a quarter because less than that does not prevent validity due to necessity; and to finding a cover because the one without it prays naked; and to remaining uncovered for the duration of performing a pillar because a large uncovering in a short time is excused, as if the wind blows and uncovers all his private part and he covers it immediately, it does not harm, like a small uncovering over a long time. And the knee with the thigh is one limb in the correct view, and the ankle of the woman with her leg, and her ear by itself, and her hanging breast, but if it is erect, it follows her chest, and the male organ by itself, and the testicles without including it in the correct view, and what is between the navel and the pubis is a complete limb from all sides of the body. And every buttock is a private part, and the anus is the third of them in the correct view. (And if the uncovering is spread over limbs of the private part, and the total of what is uncovered reaches a quarter of the smallest of the uncovered limbs) meaning those parts of which some were uncovered (it prevents) the validity of prayer if the time of uncovering is long enough for performing a pillar as we mentioned, and otherwise not. (And otherwise) i.e., if it does not reach a quarter of the smallest of them, or it reaches but the time of uncovering is not long, (then it does not) prevent validity, because a small uncovering is excused according to us due to necessity, for the clothes of the poor are not free from a small tear, like a small impurity, and the ruling applies universally to the poor and others out of kindness for all due to the principle of necessity.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah is a commentary on Nur al-Idah, presenting the ruling on exposure of the private parts during prayer. The author states that uncovering a quarter of any private part (whether thick or light, for man or woman) invalidates the prayer, provided three conditions: (1) the person has something to cover with (otherwise he prays naked), (2) the exposure lasts for the duration of performing one integral (rukn) of prayer, and (3) the uncovered area is at least a quarter of that limb. If the exposure is spread over multiple private parts, it is assessed together: if the total uncovered area equals a quarter of the smallest limb among those exposed, it invalidates. Small exposures (less than a quarter) are excused due to necessity, as poor people's clothes often have small tears. Similarly, a large exposure that is immediately covered (like wind revealing the whole body) is excused. The author also discusses what constitutes a private part, including definitions for women (e.g., voice, hair, separated limbs) and men, and notes that the estimation of al-Karkhi (comparing to impurity) is rejected. The commentary follows the Hanafi school, emphasizing that the ruling is based on ease and necessity.

Key Terms
الربع (al-rub‘): One quarter of a limb; the minimum threshold for exposure that invalidates prayer.
الانكشاف (al-inkishāf): The uncovering of a private part; if it occurs for the duration of one rukn and covers a quarter or more, prayer is invalid.
الركن (al-ruk'n): An integral of prayer, such as a prostration or standing; used as the minimum time unit for exposure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum amount of exposure of a private part that invalidates prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) Any amount
B) One quarter of a limb
C) Half of a limb
D) One dirham area

Key Takeaway
Exposure of a quarter of a private part for one rukn invalidates prayer; less than that is excused.

Defining the Private Parts (Awrah) in Hanafi Fiqh
Expansion on the definition of awrah for men and women, including voice and body parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which body parts constitute the awrah for men and women during prayer, and explain the status of the woman's voice and separated limbs.

Core Idea
The awrah is precisely defined; even the voice can be considered awrah in certain contexts.

This lesson explores the detailed definitions of what must be covered during prayer. The text provides specific rulings on various body parts, including the knee, ankle, ear, breast, and even the woman's voice. Understanding these definitions is essential to correctly applying the rules of sartorial covering in prayer.

Guided Path
1
List the default awrah for men and women
According to the Hanafi school, a man's awrah is from the navel to the knees (including the navel and knees). A woman's awrah is her entire body except the face, hands, and feet. The passage elaborates on specific parts.
These are the minimal requirements for prayer.
2
Examine special cases: woman's voice, hair, separated limbs
The text states that a woman's voice (tone) is considered awrah in the sense that it should not be raised enticingly. Separated limbs (e.g., a cut hand) are subject to different rulings on looking. Shaved pubic hair is also discussed.
The voice ruling is from al-Nawazil and al-Qurtubi, and is a matter of dispute within the school.
3
Understand the difference between thick and light awrah
The Hanafi school makes a distinction between 'thick' awrah (e.g., genitals, anus) and 'light' awrah (e.g., thighs for women). This distinction affects the threshold for uncleanliness (najasa) but not for the quarter rule in prayer.
Al-Karkhi's estimation using dirham and quarter is rejected; the text affirms a unified quarter rule.
4
Note the rulings on specific body parts
The text specifies: the knee is part of the thigh (one limb), the ankle is part of the leg, the ear is an independent limb, the hanging breast is part of the chest but the erect breast follows the chest, the male organ and testicles are separate limbs, the area between navel and pubis is one complete limb, and the buttocks and anus are separate private parts.
These definitions affect the calculation of the quarter threshold.
5
Consider the practical implications for prayer and interaction
Knowing these definitions helps determine if exposure during prayer requires repetition. Outside prayer, it affects rules of looking and social interaction, e.g., hearing a woman's voice.
The passage ends by emphasizing that small exposures are excused due to necessity, applying to all people.

The author states that uncovering a quarter of any private part (whether thick or light, for man or woman) invalidates the prayer, provided three conditions: (1) the person has something to cover with (otherwise he prays naked), (2) the exposure lasts for the duration of performing one integral (rukn) of prayer, and (3) the uncovered area is at least a quarter of that limb. The author also discusses what constitutes a private part, including definitions for women (e.g., voice, hair, separated limbs) and men, and notes that the estimation of al-Karkhi (comparing to impurity) is rejected. The commentary follows the Hanafi school, emphasizing that the ruling is based on ease and necessity.

Key Terms
العورة (al-‘awrah): Parts of the body that must be covered during prayer; includes thick and light private parts for both genders.
النغمة (al-naghama): The tone or timbre of the voice, considered awrah for a woman in terms of modesty and attracting non-mahram men.
الركبة (al-rukbah): The knee; considered part of the thigh (one limb) for the purpose of awrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school in this passage, which of the following is NOT considered part of the woman's awrah for prayer?
A) Her ear
B) Her face
C) Her voice (tone)
D) Her hanging breast

Key Takeaway
The awrah includes defined body parts and, in some contexts, the woman's voice; knowing these definitions is key to proper covering and prayer validity.

Exemption from Facing the Qibla When Unable
Explains exemptions from facing qibla due to inability and the ikhtilaf on ability through others.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a person is exempted from facing the qibla in prayer and identify the intra-Hanafi difference regarding ability through others.

Core Idea
Facing the qibla is a condition that drops when genuinely unable—prayer is valid in any direction of safety or ability.

Facing the qibla is a key requirement for prayer, but the Hanafi school recognizes exemptions for genuine inability. This lesson examines the scenarios of illness, fear, and being on a mount that prevent facing the qibla, and explains the underlying principle that the condition falls away due to necessity. It also presents a key difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions on whether being able through others counts as ability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the excuses
List the specific excuses mentioned: illness, inability to dismount from a moving mount, fear of enemy (human or beast), and severe harm.
These constitute 'ajz (inability).
2
Understand the condition dropping
Facing qibla is a shart za'id (additional condition) that drops when 'ajz is realized. The prayer is valid facing any direction of ability or safety.
The rationale: Kaaba is not worshipped in itself; it is a test.
3
Analyze the rationale from al-Diraya
The worshipper serves Allah, who is free from direction. The command to face Kaaba is a test; when unable, the test is fulfilled by facing any direction.
4
Explore the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa: one who is able through another's ability is not considered able. Sahibayn: they are considered able. This affects whether a sick person with help must face qibla.
The text follows Abu Hanifa's view.
5
Note the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's: the person prays as unable even if help is available.
No dispute when no helper exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنْ عَجَزَ عن استقبالِ القِبلة لمرض، أو عَجَزَ عن النزولِ عنْ دابَتِهِ، أَوْ خاف عدواً، فَقِبْلَتُهُ جَهَهُ قدرته وأمنه، ومن اشتبهت عليه القبلة، ولم يكن عنده مُخبر، ولا مِحْرَابٌ تَحَرّى..
( وإلأ ) أي : وإن لم يبلغ ربع أصغرها، أو بلغ ولم يطل زمن الانكشاف، (فلا) يمنع الصحة لأن قليل الانكشاف عفو عندنا للضرورة، فإن ثياب الفقراء لا تخلو عن قليل خرق كالنجاسة القليلة، وعم الحكم الفقير وغيره رفقاً بالكل لأصل الضرورة. (ومن عَجَزَ عن استقبال القبلة) بنفسه (لِمَرَض)، أو كان على خشبة في البحر، بحيث لو استقبل ينزل عنها، فيغرق، أو يحصل له ضرر شديد (أو عَجَزَ عنِ النُّزولِ) بنفسه (عَنْ دَابَّتِهِ) وهي سائرة، أو كانت جموحاً لو نزل لا يمكنه الركوب إلا بمعين، أو كان شيخاً كبيراً لا يمكنه الركوب إلا بمعين (أَوْ خَافَ عَدُوَّا) آدمياً، أو سبعاً، سواء خاف على نفسه، أو دابته أو ماله، أو أمانته، أو اشتد الخوف في حال القتال، أو هرب من عَدُوٌّ راكباً، فقِبْلَتُهُ جِهَهُ قُدْرَتِهِ) أي: العاجز عن الاستقبال بعذر، (وَ) قبلة الخائف جهة (أَمْنِهِ)، وإنما سقط عنه استقبال جهة القبلة وأجزأه الاستقبال لغيرها؛ لأن استقبال القبلة شرط زائد يسقط عند العجز، قال في ( الدراية» : والفقه فيه أن المصلي يخدم الله تعالى فلابد من الإقبال علـى مـن يخدمه، والله تعالى منزّه عن الجهة فابتلاه أي كلَّفه بالتَّوجه إلى الكعبة لا أن العبادة للكعبة، حتى لو سجد للكعبة يكفر، فَلمَّا عَراهُ الخوف والعجز تحقق العذر، فأشبه حالة الاشتباه في تحقق العذر، فيتوجه إلى أي جهةٍ قدر؛ لأن الكعبة لم تعتبر لعينها، بل للابتلاء فيتحقق المقصود بالتوجه إلى أي جهة قدر. انتهى. ولو خاف أن يراه العدو إن قعد صلـى مضطجعاً بالإيماء إلى جهة أمنه، وقيدنا بالعجز عن الاستقبال والنزول بنفسه لأن القادر بقدرة الغير ليس بقـادر عند أبي حنيفة، خلافاً لهما، وقدمنا في التيمم تفصيلاً في المسألة وإذا لم يجد العاجز أحـداً فـلا خـلاف في الصحة. ومَنِ اسْتَبَهَتْ عَلَيْهِ) جهة ( القبلة، ولم يكن عنده مُخْبِر) من أهل المحلة ولا من غيرها ممن له علم أو كان وسأله فلم يخبره (وَلا) بالمحل (مِحْرَابٌ تَحَرَّى ) أي: اجتهد وهـو : بذل المجهود لنيل المقصود، كما في «المستصفى وقال في الدراية » و « التبيين» و «الفتح»: لا يجوز التحري مع المحاريب لأن وضعها في الأصل بحق وفي ( المحيط ) : دخل مصراً وعاين المحاريب لا يتحرى، وقيدنا بكون المخبر من أهل المحلة أو العلم؛ لأنه لو كان غيرهما من المسافرين فأخبره اثنان منهم لا يلتفت إلى قولهما؛ لأنهما يقولان بالاجتهاد، فلا يترك اجتهاده باجتهاد غيره، وإن كانا من أهل ذلك الموضع لزمه الأخذ بقولهما؛ لأن الخبر في كونه حجة فوق الاجتهاد، كما في « التجنيس )
And whoever is unable to face the qibla due to illness, or unable to dismount from his mount, or fears an enemy, then his qibla is the direction of his ability and safety. And whoever is confused about the qibla, and he does not have an informer nor a mihrab, he makes an estimation. (And otherwise) i.e., if it does not reach a quarter of the smallest of them, or it reaches but the time is not long, (then it) does not prevent validity because a small uncovering is excused among us due to necessity, for the clothes of the poor are not free from a small tear, like a small impurity, and the ruling applies universally to the poor and others out of kindness for all due to the principle of necessity. (And whoever is unable to face the qibla) himself (due to illness), or was on a plank in the sea, such that if he faces it he would descend from it and drown, or severe harm would befall him, (or is unable to dismount) himself (from his mount) while it is moving, or it is unruly such that if he dismounts he cannot mount except with help, or he is an old man who cannot mount except with help, (or fears an enemy) human or beast, whether he fears for himself, his mount, his property, or his trust, or fear intensifies during battle, or he flees from an enemy while riding, then his qibla is the direction of his ability (i.e., the one unable to face due to an excuse) and the qibla of the fearful is the direction of his safety. And the condition of facing the direction of the qibla is dropped from him and facing other than it suffices, because facing the qibla is an additional condition that drops when unable. He said in al-Diraya: The fiqh of it is that the worshipper serves Allah Almighty, so he must turn towards the One he serves, and Allah Almighty is free from direction, so He tests him by requiring him to turn towards the Kaaba, not that worship is for the Kaaba, such that if he prostrates to the Kaaba he disbelieves. So when fear and inability occur, the excuse is realized, similar to the state of confusion in realizing the excuse, so he faces whatever direction he is able; because the Kaaba is not considered for itself, but for the test, so the purpose is achieved by facing whatever direction he can. End. And if he fears that the enemy will see him if he sits, he prays lying down with gestures towards his safe direction. And we restricted it to being unable to face and dismount himself because the one who is able through another's ability is not considered able according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And we previously presented details in the chapter on tayammum. And if the one unable does not find anyone, then there is no dispute about validity. And whoever is confused about (the direction of) the qibla, and he does not have an informer from the people of the neighborhood nor from elsewhere who has knowledge, or he asked and he did not inform him, and there is no mihrab in the place, then he makes an estimation (ijtihad). That is: exerting effort to attain the goal, as in al-Mustasfa. And it is said in al-Diraya, al-Tabyin, and al-Fath: Estimation is not permissible when there are mihrabs, because their placement is originally based on truth. And in al-Muhit: If he enters a city and sees the mihrabs, he does not estimate. And we restricted it to the informer being from the people of the neighborhood or knowledge, because if they are others from travelers and two of them inform him, their statement is not considered, because they speak by ijtihad, so his ijtihad is not abandoned for the ijtihad of others. But if they are from that place, he must accept their statement, because news in being a proof is above ijtihad, as in al-Tajnis.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This section of Imdad al-Fattah covers exemptions from facing the qibla in prayer. The text explains that if a person is unable to face the qibla due to illness, being on a moving mount, or fear of an enemy (human or beast), then they may pray facing any direction they are able or that ensures safety. The ruling is based on the principle that facing the qibla is a condition that falls away when one is genuinely unable. The commentary cites al-Diraya explaining that the Kaaba is not worshipped in itself but as a test; therefore, when unable, the purpose is fulfilled by facing any direction. The text also addresses the case where one is uncertain about the qibla direction: if no reliable informer or mihrab exists, one must perform ijtihad (estimation). However, if there is a mihrab, ijtihad is not allowed. There is an ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding whether a person who can be helped by others is considered able—Abu Hanifa says no, so they pray as unable. The commentary emphasizes that the ruling applies only when the person themselves is unable, not if someone else can help.

Key Terms
عجز (‘ajz): Inability to perform an action oneself; here, inability to face qibla due to illness, fear, or being on a mount.
شرط زائد (shart za'id): An additional condition that is not intrinsic to the act; here, facing qibla is a condition that drops when unable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when is a person permitted to pray without facing the qibla?
A) Only when sick
B) When unable due to illness, fear, or inability to dismount
C) Only when confused about direction
D) Never

Key Takeaway
Facing the qibla is a condition that drops when one is genuinely unable due to illness, fear, or in a moving mount; the prayer is valid facing any direction of ability or safety.

Determining the Qibla Through Estimation (Taharri)
Rules for determining qibla direction when uncertain, focusing on the role of mihrab and informers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a person must perform ijtihad (taharri) for qibla direction and identify when it is not allowed (due to mihrab or reliable informer).

Core Idea
When uncertain about qibla and no reliable indicator exists, you must exert ijtihad; the existence of a mihrab or trustworthy informer removes the need for estimation.

Uncertainty about the qibla direction is a common challenge, especially when traveling. The Hanafi school provides clear guidelines: if there is a mihrab in a mosque, or a reliable informer from the locality, you must follow that. Only when these are absent does personal ijtihad (taharri) become obligatory. This lesson explains the process and the hierarchy of evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for taharri
Taharri is required when a person is confused about the qibla direction and does not have a reliable informer or a mihrab.
Confusion (ishtibah) is the key trigger.
2
Understand the prohibition of taharri with mihrab
If a mihrab exists, taharri is not allowed because mihrabs are accurately placed based on correct knowledge.
This is a general rule: mihrabs are trusted.
3
Distinguish between informers
An informer from the locality or someone with knowledge is a proof (hujja) above ijtihad. Informers who are travelers (outside the locality) are not accepted because they speak from their own ijtihad.
Two travelers' statements are not taken; one local informer is sufficient.
4
Apply the hierarchy
When entering a city with mihrabs, follow them. If no mihrab, seek a local informer. If no informer, perform ijtihad.
The maxim: 'al-khabar hujja fawqa al-ijtihad'.
5
Note the outcome
After proper ijtihad, the person prays facing his best estimate; the prayer is valid even if later found wrong (provided ijtihad was sincere).
This is implied by the permissibility of taharri.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Key Terms
تحري (taḥarrī): Estimation or ijtihad to determine the qibla direction when uncertain.
محراب (miḥrāb): Prayer niche indicating the direction of qibla in a mosque; its presence removes the need for estimation.
مخبر (mukhbir): Informer who can reliably indicate the qibla direction.

Rulings on Qibla Uncertainty: Effort and Error
Commentary on matn: rulings for qibla uncertainty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a mutaharrī who errs in qibla, explain the proofs (Quran, hadith, and qiyas), and apply the distinction from taharrī in purity.

Core Idea
No repeat is required for one who prays with effort (taharrī) and later discovers error, because obligation is limited by capacity.

When the qibla is uncertain, the Hanafi school permits one to exert effort (taharrī) to determine the correct direction. If after prayer the person realizes he faced the wrong direction, does he need to repeat? The answer is no, based on clear proofs and a key distinction from similar cases in purity. This lesson unpacks the reasoning, including a famous hadith, a qiyas argument, and practical scenarios like a blind person or someone who prayed without any effort.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is performing prayer with taharrī for qibla when the direction is uncertain. The ruling (stated at the beginning of the passage) is: if one later discovers error, there is no repeat required. Confirm the Arabic phrase 'ولا إعادة عليه لو أخطأ'.
This is the core ruling that the rest of the passage supports.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author cites the hadith of 'Amir ibn Rabī'a where the Companions prayed each in his own direction on a dark night, and the verse 2:115 was revealed. Also the Prophet's statement: 'The qibla of the mutaharrī is the direction he intends.' Identify these as the primary textual proofs.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for a ruling of this nature.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal implication)
The verse 'Wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah' indicates that after sincere effort, any direction is acceptable. The hadith shows the Prophet's approval of the Companions' actions without requiring a repeat. Understand how these prove the ruling.
This step links the text to the fiqh ruling: the implication of the evidence.
4
Analyse the qiyas objection and response
An objection is raised: why does taharrī in purity (vessels/clothes) require a repeat if mistaken, but not here? The answer distinguishes qibla as changeable (abrogated from Jerusalem to Ka'ba) whereas purity is not. Also, one has more capacity to verify purity. Work through the qiyas panel to see the illa (effective cause).
This shows the Hanafi method of istidlal: using qiyas to answer objections.
5
Apply to edge cases
The passage covers several applications: (a) blind person – valid as imam if no informant; (b) turning (istidāra) during prayer if error discovered; (c) one who prays without taharrī and later finds correctness – valid. Review these to solidify the principle.
These sub-rulings demonstrate the scope of the core rule.
