ولا إعادة عليه لو أخطأ.
وفي قولنا ولم يكن عنده مخبر إشارة إلى أنه ليس عليه طلب من يسأله عند الاشتباه، كما في «معراج الدراية». وقال في الفتاوى الخانية»: صلى في المسجد في ليلة مظلمة بالتحري، فتبين أنه صلى إلى غير القبلة جازت صلاته، لأنه ليس له أن يقرع أبواب الناس للسؤال عن القبلة، ولا تعرف القبلة بمس الجدران والحيطان للاشتباه، وعسى يكون ثمة مؤذية أي من الحشرات فجاز له التحري انتهى. تنبيه: يجوز للأعمى التحري كغيره ، ولا يلزمه مس الجدران لما ذكرنا، ولذا قال في « التجنيس والمزيد » : الأعمى إذا صلى ركعة إلى غير القبلة فجاء رجل وسواه وأقامه إلى القبلة واقتدى به فهذا على وجهين، أما إن وجد عند الافتتاح إنساناً يسأله أو لم يجد ففي الوجه الأول لا تجوز صلاته ولا الاقتداء به؛ لأنه قادر على أداء الصَّلاة إلى جهة الكعبة، وفي الوجه الثاني: تجوز صلاة الإمام أي: الأعمى لأنه عاجز ولا تجوز صلاة المقتدي لأن عنده صلاة إمامه على الخطأ. ثم قال: إذا دخل المسجد وهو مظلم وصلى المغرب، فلما فرغ من الصلاة جيء بالسراج فإذا هو صلى إلى غير القبلة إن صلاها بالتحري جاز ولا إعادة عليه، وفيه إشكال وهو : أنه قادر على إصابة القبلة بالاستدلال بالمحاريب المنصوبة والسؤال من أهل المحلة قالوا في الجواب عنه: أما السؤال فذلـك عنـد حضرتهم وخروجهم من المنازل؛ لأن من القبيح أن يستخرجهم من المنازل يسألهم عن قبلتهم، وأما المحاريب فالاستدلال بها عند النظر إليها عياناً والوقف عليها جهاراً فأما لمس الجدران حين أظلم المسجد فلا يكلف بذلك؛ لأنه قد تقع يده على بعض الهوام اللاسعة وفي ذلــك ضرراً، ويكون في بعض الزوايا طاقات (۱) توهم أنها المحراب فيشتبه الأمر، أو يكون المحراب منقوشاً معلماً بالخطوط دون الطاق الداخلة في الحائط ولا يعرف ذلك إلا بالرؤية ، قال : وهذه فائدة جليلة نبه عليها الشيخ الإمام نجم الدين عمر بن محمد النسفي رحمه الله تعالى عن أستاذه شيخ الإسلام عن السيد الإمام أبي شجاع ) انتهى. ولا إعَادَةَ عَلَيْهِ لَوْ) علم بعد الفراغ من صلاته متحريـاً أنـه أخطأ) الجهة لما روي عن عامر بن ربيعة، أنه قال: « كُنَّا مَعَ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي لَيْلَةٍ مُظْلِمَةٍ فَلْمٍ نَدْرِ أين القبلةُ فَصَلَّى كُلُّ رجلٍ مِنَّا على حِيالِهِ فَلَمَّا أَصْبَحْنَا ذكرنا ذلك لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فنزلت: فَأَيْنَمَا تُوَلُّوا فَتَمَ وَجْهُ اللَّهُ إِنَّ ) [البقرة : ١١٥] وقال عليه : قبلة المتحري جهة قصده (۳) ولأن التكليف
مقيد بالوسع فإن قيل: إذا تحرى في الأواني التي أكثرها طاهر، أو الثياب مطلقاً، ثم ظهر أنه أخطأ، يجب الإعادة فهلا وجبت هنا قلنا: الأصل أن ما يحتمل الانتقال بعد الثبوت لا تجـب فيـه الإعــادة، وأمر القبلة بهذه الصفة، ألا يرى أنها حولت من بيت المقدس إلى الكعبة ) ، ثم منها إلى جهتها، وما لا يحتمل الانتقال بعد الثبوت يلزم فيه الإعادة، وطهارة الأواني والثياب لا تحتمل الانتقال؛ ولأن في وسعه إصابة الطاهر لأنه كان يقدر على تطهيره حقيقة، وإنما خفي لنسيانه الطاهر منها، وكذا في الماء في وسعه الاستخبار عن طهارته ممن له علم به، وإن لم يكن في وسعه كان في وسعه إراقته والتيمم الذي يخلفه بلا شبهة، وأما علمه بجهة الكعبة فمما غاب عنه ولا يدرك حقيقته باستقصائه إلا بالنظر في النجم ونحوه ومن يخبره يعتمد على ذلك، فإذا خفي عنهما عجزا عن الاستدلال لعارض الغيم ونحوه، وذلك من قبل الله فسقط به خطابه (وإنْ عَلِمَ بِخَطَئِهِ فِي صَلَاتِهِ اسْتَدَارَ) وكيفية الاستدارة أن يبدأ من الجانب الأيمن لا من الأيسر، كما في «معراج الدراية» وكذا إذا تبدل اجتهاده إلى جهة أخرى استدار (وَبَنَى) على ما صلى إلى الجهة الأولى، ثم إن تحول إلى أخرى يتحول إليها، وهكذا كذلك إلى أن يتممها، واختلف المتأخرون فيما إذا تحول رأيه إلى الجهة الأولى بالتحري، فمنهم من قال : يتمها ومنهم من قال : يستقبل، وإذا تحول إلى جهة أخرى فتذكر سجدة مــن الركعة الأولى فسدت صلاته (۳) ، ويتحرى لسجدة التلاوة كالصلاة، وبعد علمه بخطئه في تحريه واستدارته بني على ما صلى، لأن تبدل الاجتهاد بمنزلة تبدل النسخ، وما شرع فيه بالتحري لا يبطل الخطأ، وأهل قباء لما بلغهم نسخ القبلة استداروا في الصلاة إلى الكعبة، واستحسنه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وهذا لأن اليقين حادث وليس بمناقض، فصار كنص ترك على خلاف اجتهاد أو إجماع انعقد بعد إمضاء حكم الاجتهاد بخلافه، (وَإِنْ شَرَعَ من اشتبهت عليه القبلة في صلاته شـــاكـاً في الجهة (بـلا تَحر)، كان مبنى أمره على الفساد، لكن غير محتم، فإذا أتمها (فعلم بعد فراغِهِ) من الصلاة (أنَّه أصابَ، صحت) لأنه تبين الصواب بطل الحكم باستصحاب الحال (۳)، وثبـت الجـواز مــن الأصل، بظهور ا
And there is no repeat upon him if he made a mistake. And in our statement 'and he has no informant' is an indication that he is not required to seek someone to ask when uncertain, as in 'Miraj al-Diraya'. And it is stated in 'al-Fatawa al-Khaniyya': He prayed in the mosque on a dark night with taharrī, and it turned out that he prayed to a direction other than the qibla; his prayer is permissible, because he is not allowed to knock on people's doors to ask about the qibla, nor is the qibla known by touching walls and partitions due to confusion, and perhaps there is a harmful insect there, so taharrī is permissible for him. End. A note: it is permissible for a blind person to perform taharrī like others, and he is not required to touch walls for what we mentioned. Hence it is said in 'al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd': A blind person who prays one rak'ah to a direction other than the qibla, then a man comes and corrects him and makes him face the qibla, and the blind person follows him — this is of two aspects: either he found at the beginning a person to ask or he did not find. In the first aspect, his prayer is not valid and neither is following him, because he is able to perform prayer towards the Ka'ba. In the second aspect: the prayer of the imam, i.e., the blind person, is valid because he is incapable, and the prayer of the follower is not valid because he has the prayer of his imam in error. Then he said: If he entered the mosque in darkness and prayed Maghrib, and when he finished the prayer a lamp was brought and it turned out he prayed to a direction other than the qibla — if he prayed with taharrī, it is permissible and there is no repeat upon him. There is a difficulty: that he is able to hit the qibla by deducing from the installed mihrabs and by asking the people of the neighborhood. They responded: As for asking, that is when they are present and coming out of their homes, because it is improper to bring them out of their homes to ask them about their qibla. As for the mihrabs, deducing by them is by looking at them directly and standing on them openly. As for touching walls when the mosque is dark, he is not obliged to do that because his hand might fall on some stinging insects, and there is harm in that. And in some corners there are archways (1) that might be mistaken for the mihrab, so the matter is confusing, or the mihrab might be decorated and marked with lines without the arch being set into the wall, and that is not known except by sight. He said: This is a great benefit that the Shaykh al-Imam Najm al-Din 'Umar ibn Muhammad al-Nasafi, may Allah have mercy on him, pointed out from his teacher Shaykh al-Islam from al-Sayyid al-Imam Abu Shuja'. End. And there is no repeat upon him if he learns after finishing his prayer, having performed taharrī, that he erred in the direction, because of what is narrated from 'Amir ibn Rabī'a who said: 'We were with the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) on a dark night and we did not know where the qibla was, so each man prayed in his own direction. When morning came, we mentioned that to the Messenger of Allah, and the verse was revealed: 'Wherever you turn, there is the face of Allah' [Al-Baqara: 115]. And he (peace be upon him) said: 'The qibla of the mutaharrī is the direction he intends.' (3) And because obligation is limited by capacity. If it is said: When one performs taharrī about vessels most of which are pure, or clothes absolutely, then it becomes clear he erred, he must repeat. So why is it not required here? We say: The principle is that what can be altered after establishment does not require repetition. The matter of qibla has this quality; do you not see that it was changed from Jerusalem to the Ka'ba, then to its direction? And what cannot be altered after establishment requires repetition. Purity of vessels and clothes cannot be altered. And because he is able to hit the pure one by actually being able to purify it, but it was hidden from him due to his forgetting the pure one among them. Similarly with water, he is able to inquire about its purity from one who knows about it. And if he is not able to do that, he is able to pour it out and perform tayammum which substitutes it without doubt. As for his knowledge of the direction of the Ka'ba, it is something hidden from him and cannot be grasped by thorough investigation except by looking at the stars and the like, and whoever informs him relies on that. So if it is hidden from both, they are incapable of deduction due to an obstacle like clouds and the like, and that is from Allah, so His address falls away. (And if he knows of his error during his prayer, he turns.) And the manner of turning is that he starts from the right side, not the left, as in 'Miraj al-Diraya'. Likewise, if his ijtihad changes to another direction, he turns (and builds) upon what he prayed towards the first direction. Then if he changes to another, he turns to it, and so on until he completes it. The later scholars differed regarding when his opinion changes to the first direction by taharrī: some said he completes it, and some said he resumes facing it. If he changes to another direction and then remembers a sajdah from the first rak'ah, his prayer is invalidated (3). And he performs taharrī for the sajdah of tilawah like for prayer. After he knows his error in his taharrī and turns, he builds upon what he prayed, because change of ijtihad is like change of abrogation. And what is begun with taharrī is not invalidated by error. The people of Quba', when the abrogation of the qibla reached them, turned in prayer towards the Ka'ba, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) approved of that. This is because certainty is new and not contradictory. So it becomes like a text that is abandoned contrary to ijtihad, or an ijma' that occurred after the implementation of the ruling of ijtihad contrary to it. (And if one who is uncertain about the qibla begins his prayer (while in doubt about the direction without taharrī), his matter is based on corruption, but it is not certain. So if he completes it (and knows after finishing it) that he was correct, it is valid because the correct judgment becomes clear, the ruling of presuming continuity (istishab al-hal) is nullified (3), and permissibility is established from the beginning, by the appearance of...
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a matn concerning the rulings for one who prays with uncertainty about the qibla. It opens with the ruling that if a person performs taharrī (exerting effort to determine the correct direction) and later discovers he prayed to the wrong direction, there is no requirement to repeat the prayer. The commentator explains the reasoning: the one performing taharrī is not obligated to seek out someone to ask when uncertain, as this would cause hardship. He supports this by quoting from al-Fatawa al-Khaniyya, giving the example of a person praying in a dark mosque with taharrī; even if he later finds he faced the wrong direction, his prayer is valid. The commentator then addresses the specific case of a blind person, stating that a blind person may also perform taharrī and is not required to touch walls. He relates two scenarios from al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd: if the blind person found someone to ask at the start, his prayer is not valid; if he did not, his prayer as imam is valid but the follower's prayer is not valid. The commentator then provides a proof from the hadith of 'Amir ibn Rabī'a, where the Companions prayed in different directions on a dark night, and the verse 2:115 was revealed, and the Prophet said, 'The qibla of the mutaharrī is the direction he intends.' The ruling is based on the principle that obligation is limited by capacity. An objection is raised: why is it that in cases of taharrī regarding the purity of vessels or clothes, one must repeat if mistaken, whereas here no repeat is required? The response is that the qibla was changed by divine decree, so it is a matter that can be altered after establishment; purity of vessels and clothes cannot be altered. Additionally, one has the capacity to determine purity by inquiry or by using alternatives like tayammum, while determining the qibla direction through the stars is uncertain and subject to obstacles like clouds, so it is beyond one's capacity. The commentator then explains the ruling if one realizes the error during the prayer: he should turn from the right side and build upon what he has already prayed. This is based on the precedent of the people of Quba' when the qibla was changed to the Ka'ba. The later scholars differed on whether to complete or restart if the ijtihad changes back to the original direction. Finally, the passage covers the case of one who prays without any taharrī (i.e., in doubt) and later discovers he was correct: his prayer is valid because the error in presumption is corrected by the appearance of the truth. This commentary systematically explains the matn's rulings, providing proofs, answering objections, and covering edge cases.

Key Terms
تحري (taharrī): Exerting effort to determine the correct direction of the qibla when it is not clear
قبلة (qibla): The direction of the Ka'ba in Mecca that Muslims face during prayer
استدارة (istidāra): Turning from the right side towards the correct qibla direction during prayer when realizing error

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for one who performs taharrī for qibla and later discovers after finishing prayer that he faced the wrong direction?
A) He must repeat the prayer
B) He does not need to repeat the prayer
C) He must repeat only if it was a fard prayer
D) He must make up the prayer with a prostration of forgetfulness

Key Takeaway
No repeat is required for a mutaharrī who errs in qibla; the prayer is valid due to the limitation of obligation by capacity and the principle that what is subject to change does not require repetition.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Correcting Qibla Error During Prayer and Starting Without Ijtihad
Explanation of two rulings: turning during prayer upon discovering error, and validity of prayer started without ijtihad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi rulings for a person uncertain of the qibla: the rule of turning and building during prayer when error is known, and the rule of validity when starting without ijtihad and later learning correctness, and explain the proof from the hadith of the people of Quba.

Core Idea
If you discover qibla error during prayer, turn and continue; if you started without ijtihad and were correct, prayer is valid within capacity.

When a person is uncertain of the qibla, Hanafi fiqh provides specific rulings that preserve the validity of the prayer while respecting the obligation to face the qibla. This lesson examines two key scenarios: discovering error during prayer, and starting prayer without performing ijtihad (taharrī). The rulings are based on the principle that the qibla obligation can change, reminiscent of the abrogation from Jerusalem to the Kaaba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The passage presents two distinct rulings: (a) knowing error during prayer, (b) starting without taharrī and later learning correctness.
These are separate issues with different conditions.
2
State the Hanafi ruling for each case
For (a): the person turns from the right side and builds on what he has prayed. For (b): the prayer is valid if the person was within capacity (i.e., genuinely unable to determine qibla).
The manner of turning and the condition of capacity are crucial.
3
Analyze the dalil (proof)
The proof is the hadith of the people of Quba: when the qibla abrogation reached them, they turned towards the Kaaba during prayer, and the Prophet ﷺ approved. This indicates that building is permissible when the qibla changes, analogically to knowing error.
The approval (taqrīr) of the Prophet is a valid source of Sunnah.
4
Differentiate from similar cases
The passage contrasts the qibla case with errors in purity of vessels or clothes. In those cases, if error is discovered later, repetition is required because those rulings cannot change after establishment. The qibla ruling can change (as seen with abrogation), so no repetition is needed.
This distinction highlights the principle of 'ma yahtamil al-intiqāl' (can undergo change).
5
Note the practical manner of turning
When turning during prayer, one should begin from the right side. If ijtihad changes to another direction, he turns similarly. Later scholars differed on what to do if his opinion returns to the original direction: some say continue, some say face anew.
This shows that ijtihad changes are analogous to abrogation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن علم بخطئِهِ في صلاته استدار وبنى، وإنْ شَرَعَ بلا تَحَرِّ، فعلم بعدَ فراغِهِ أَنَّه أَصابَ، صحت، مقيد بالوسع فإن قيل: إذا تحرى في الأواني التي أكثرها طاهر، أو الثياب مطلقاً، ثم ظهر أنه أخطأ، يجب الإعادة فهلا وجبت هنا قلنا: الأصل أن ما يحتمل الانتقال بعد الثبوت لا تجـب فيـه الإعــادة، وأمر القبلة بهذه الصفة، ألا يرى أنها حولت من بيت المقدس إلى الكعبة ) ، ثم منها إلى جهتها، وما لا يحتمل الانتقال بعد الثبوت يلزم فيه الإعادة، وطهارة الأواني والثياب لا تحتمل الانتقال؛ ولأن في وسعه إصابة الطاهر لأنه كان يقدر على تطهيره حقيقة، وإنما خفي لنسيانه الطاهر منها، وكذا في الماء في وسعه الاستخبار عن طهارته ممن له علم به، وإن لم يكن في وسعه كان في وسعه إراقته والتيمم الذي يخلفه بلا شبهة، وأما علمه بجهة الكعبة فمما غاب عنه ولا يدرك حقيقته باستقصائه إلا بالنظر في النجم ونحوه ومن يخبره يعتمد على ذلك، فإذا خفي عنهما عجزا عن الاستدلال لعارض الغيم ونحوه، وذلك من قبل الله فسقط به خطابه (وإنْ عَلِمَ بِخَطَئِهِ فِي صَلَاتِهِ اسْتَدَارَ) وكيفية الاستدارة أن يبدأ من الجانب الأيمن لا من الأيسر، كما في «معراج الدراية» وكذا إذا تبدل اجتهاده إلى جهة أخرى استدار (وَبَنَى) على ما صلى إلى الجهة الأولى، ثم إن تحول إلى أخرى يتحول إليها، وهكذا كذلك إلى أن يتممها، واختلف المتأخرون فيما إذا تحول رأيه إلى الجهة الأولى بالتحري، فمنهم من قال : يتمها ومنهم من قال : يستقبل، وإذا تحول إلى جهة أخرى فتذكر سجدة مــن الركعة الأولى فسدت صلاته (۳) ، ويتحرى لسجدة التلاوة كالصلاة، وبعد علمه بخطئه في تحريه واستدارته بني على ما صلى، لأن تبدل الاجتهاد بمنزلة تبدل النسخ، وما شرع فيه بالتحري لا يبطل الخطأ، وأهل قباء لما بلغهم نسخ القبلة استداروا في الصلاة إلى الكعبة، واستحسنه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وهذا لأن اليقين حادث وليس بمناقض، فصار كنص ترك على خلاف اجتهاد أو إجماع انعقد بعد إمضاء حكم الاجتهاد بخلافه
And if he knows his error in his prayer, he turns and builds; and if he begins without taharrī, then after his completion he knows that he was correct, it is valid, restricted by capacity. For if it is said: When he makes ijtihad regarding vessels most of which are pure, or clothes absolutely, then it appears that he erred, he must repeat; so why is it not required here? We say: The principle is that which can undergo change after establishment does not require repetition, and the matter of qibla is of this description. Do you not see that it was changed from Jerusalem to the Kaaba, then to its direction? And what cannot change after establishment requires repetition. The purity of vessels and clothes cannot undergo change. And because he has the capacity to hit upon what is pure since he was able to purify it actually, but it was hidden due to his forgetting the pure among them. Similarly with water, he has the capacity to inquire about its purity from someone who knows. If he did not have the capacity, he had the capacity to pour it out and perform tayammum which substitutes for it without doubt. As for his knowledge of the direction of the Kaaba, it is something hidden from him, and he cannot know its reality through investigation except by looking at the stars and the like, and whoever informs him relies on that. So if it is hidden from both, they are unable to deduce due to an obstacle like clouds and the like, and that is from Allah, so his obligation falls. (And if he knows his error in his prayer, he turns around.) The manner of turning is that he begins from the right side, not the left, as in 'Mi'raj al-Diraya'. Similarly, if his ijtihad changes to another direction, he turns and builds on what he prayed towards the first direction. Then if he turns to another, he turns to it, and so on until he completes it. The later scholars disagreed when his opinion changes to the first direction by taharrī: some said he completes it, some said he faces anew. If he turns to another direction and then remembers a sajdah from the first rakah, his prayer becomes invalid. And he makes ijtihad for the sajdah of tilawah like the prayer. After knowing his error in his ijtihad and his turning, he builds on what he prayed, because change of ijtihad is like change of abrogation, and what he began with taharrī is not invalidated by error. The people of Quba when the abrogation of the qibla reached them, they turned in prayer towards the Kaaba, and the Prophet ﷺ approved of that. This is because certainty is newly occurring and not contradictory, so it becomes like an explicit text that abandons contrary ijtihad or like an ijma that occurs after execution of a ruling contrary to it.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains two rulings for someone uncertain of the qibla. First: if during prayer he realizes his direction was wrong, he turns to the correct direction and continues building on what he has already prayed. Turning should start from the right side. This building is permissible because the qibla ruling can change, like when it was abrogated from Jerusalem to the Kaaba. Second: if he begins praying without making ijtihad (taharrī) and after finishing learns he was facing correctly, his prayer is valid, but only if he was within his capacity (i.e., he could not determine the qibla due to genuine inability). The author distinguishes this from cases of impure vessels or clothes where repeating is required, because those cannot change once established, while qibla can. The proof is the hadith of the people of Quba who turned during prayer upon learning of the abrogation, and the Prophet approved. The method of turning and differences among later scholars regarding changes in ijtihad are also detailed.

Key Terms
تحرّ (taharrī): Making ijtihad to determine the correct direction of the qibla when uncertain.
استدار (istadāra): To turn towards the correct qibla during prayer by moving the feet from the right side.
مقيد بالوسع (muqayyad bil-wus'): Restricted by capacity, meaning the ruling applies only if the person was genuinely unable to determine the qibla.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a person uncertain of the qibla knows his error during prayer, what is the correct action according to the Hanafi school?
A) He must stop and repeat the entire prayer.
B) He turns from the left side and continues.
C) He turns from the right side and builds on what he prayed.
D) He continues without turning and repeats later.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school preserves the validity of prayer for the uncertain person by allowing turning and building upon discovery of error, and by accepting prayer started without ijtihad if the person was correct within capacity.

Invalidity of Prayer When One Knows Correct Qibla During Prayer Without Taharrī
Ruling on invalidity when knowledge of qibla arrives during prayer without taharrī

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a person gains knowledge of correct qibla during prayer without prior ijtihad, and explain the reasoning based on the principle that the strong cannot be built upon the weak.

Core Idea
Knowledge during prayer cannot cure a deficient beginning: the strong cannot be built on the weak.

This lesson examines a specific case in Hanafi fiqh: a person begins praying without determining the qibla (taharrī) while uncertain, then during prayer becomes certain he is facing correctly. According to the majority of the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), the prayer becomes invalid immediately. We will explore the legal reasoning behind this ruling and contrast it with the minority view of Abu Yusuf, who allows building upon the later knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is: a person starts praying without performing taharrī (ijtihad to find qibla) while in doubt, then during prayer becomes certain or strongly presumes he is facing correctly. The ruling stated is that the prayer becomes invalid (fasid).
The ruling applies whether certainty or strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann) is achieved.
2
Trace the dalil (proof)
The primary proof is the principle: 'Building the strong upon the weak is not permissible.' The initial state was weak (no taharrī, uncertainty), and the later knowledge introduces strength; thus the prayer cannot be built on a deficient foundation.
This is a rational (aqli) proof, analogous to other cases in fiqh.
3
Understand the qiyas (analogy)
The text analogizes to two cases: (1) an illiterate person (ummi) who learns a surah during prayer — the prayer invalidates; (2) a person who gestures (mumi) due to inability and then becomes able to perform physical pillars — the prayer invalidates. In both, the deficiency at the start cannot be remedied mid-prayer.
The underlying illa (effective cause) is that a strong element (knowledge, ability) appears during the act, but the foundation was weak, so building is impermissible.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf dissents: he holds that the person should 'build' (i.e., continue the prayer and it remains valid), analogizing to the case where one changes qibla during prayer due to revelation (where the prayer remains valid).
The text responds that in the qibla-change case, the initial state was strong (based on ijtihad or divine command), whereas here it was weak.
5
Determine the tarjih and mufta bihi
The author sides with Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the prayer invalidates. The principle of istishab al-hal (presumption of continuation of the original state) also supports invalidity, as the original deficiency is not removed by evidence.
The ruling is settled in authoritative Hanafi works such as al-Bada'i', al-Tabyin, and al-Fath.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنْ عَلِمَ بإصابتِهِ فِيْهَا ) يقيناً، أو بأكبر رأيه (فَسَدَتْ)؛ لأن حالته قويت بالعلم، وبناء القوي علـى الضعيف لا يجوز، وعند أبي يوسف يبني لما ذكرنا، قلنا: هو كالأمي إذا تعلم ســـورة، والمومـي إذا قدر على الأركان فيها تفسد، وبعدها تصح لقوة ما بقي وضعف الماضي، فلا يُبنـى قـوي عـلـى ضعيف، (كَمَا ) فسدت فيما لو لم يعلم إصابته أصلاً وقد شرع فيها شاكاً بلا تحر؛ لأن الأصل هو الفساد وهو ثابت باستصحاب الحال، ولم يرتفع بدليل)، فتقرر الفساد لعدم حصول المشروط لا حقيقة ولا حكماً (۳)، كما في ( البدائع»، و«التبيين»، و«الفتح».
And if he knows his correctness during it — with certainty or by strong presumption — it becomes invalid, because his state is strengthened by knowledge, and building the strong upon the weak is not permissible. According to Abu Yusuf, he builds due to what we mentioned. We say: He is like the illiterate person who learns a surah, or the one who gestures who becomes able to perform the pillars — during the act it becomes invalid, and after it, it becomes valid due to the strength of what remains and the weakness of the past. So the strong cannot be built upon the weak. (Just as) it became invalid if he had not known his correctness at all and had started in doubt without taharrī, because the original is invalidity, and it is established by istishab al-hal, and is not removed by evidence. So invalidity is settled due to the non-attainment of the condition, neither in reality nor legally, as in al-Bada'i', al-Tabyin, and al-Fath.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage clarifies that if a person begins praying without taharrī (ijtihad) while uncertain of the qibla, and then during the prayer he becomes certain or strongly presumes he is facing the correct direction, the prayer becomes invalid. The reason is that the initial state of the prayer was weak (due to lack of taharrī), and now knowledge introduces strength. In Hanafi law, a strong act cannot be built upon a weak foundation, just as if an illiterate person learns a surah during prayer or a disabled person gains ability to perform physical pillars — the prayer invalidates because the basis was deficient. Abu Yusuf opposed, saying one can build, but the relied-upon position (of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the prayer invalidates. Supporting evidence is that if he had never known correctness, the prayer would be invalid by default (istishab), and since knowledge during prayer does not remove that initial deficiency, the invalidity stands.

Key Terms
الأمي (al-ummī): An illiterate person who cannot recite Quran properly; analogy in this text for someone with deficient prayer
المومي (al-mūmī): One who gestures during prayer due to inability to perform physical pillars
استصحاب الحال (istishāb al-ḥāl): Presumption of the continuation of the existing state (here, the presumption of invalidity)

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated
C) He should continue and it is valid if he finishes
D) He may choose to continue or restart

Key Takeaway
If a person begins prayer without proper determination of qibla (taharrī), even later certainty of correct direction does not validate the prayer; it invalidates.

The Binding Nature of Taharrī: When Your Ijtihad Becomes Your Qibla
Summary of three scenarios and the intra-Hanafi dispute when one does taharrī but prays elsewhere

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a person does taharrī but prays to a different direction, and explain why the relied-upon position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) differs from Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
The direction indicated by your ijtihad becomes your kaaba — abandoning it invalidates your prayer even if you face the real Kaaba.

The previous discussion established that making ijtihad (taharrī) for the qibla is obligatory when the direction is uncertain. But what happens if you perform ijtihad, your reasoning points to one direction, yet you deliberately choose to pray towards another — even if that other direction is actually correct? Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad hold that your prayer is invalid, because your ijtihad result is legally binding for you. Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees, finding the prayer valid if you hit the true qibla. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the practical consequence of this intra-Hanafi dispute.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Describe the situation: a person makes taharrī to determine the qibla. His ijtihad points to direction X, but he deliberately prays towards direction Y. After prayer, he learns that Y was actually the true qibla.
2
State the majority Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad)
The prayer is invalid regardless of whether he was actually correct. Because the direction of ijtihad becomes like the Kaaba for him, leaving it is impermissible. Moreover, he believed his act invalid from the start.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position
The prayer is valid if he was actually correct. His proof: the objective (facing the qibla) was achieved, analogous to taharrī for vessels where deviating to a clean source suffices.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The majority distinguishes: in the vessel case, the person had certainty in his intention and the water was pure. Here, the person believed his act invalid from the start, so his intention is defective.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and thamarah
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: the prayer is invalid. Practical effect: the person must repeat his prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه علم مما ذكرناه ثلاث صور من مسائل التحري : ١- صحة الصلاة مع الشك، ٢- والتحري ولو علم بالخطأ وهو في أثنائها، كما لو علم بالخطأ بعد فراغه، ٣ - وصحتها لا مع شك ولا تحر، حتَّى إذا صلّى في ليلة مظلمة من غير تحرّ ولاشك فهو على الجواز، حتّى يظهر خطؤه بيقين، أو بأكبر رأيه ولو بعد الفراغ فيلزمه الإعادة، وصحتها مع الشك وترك التحري، والشرط في هذه الصور للصحة: أن يعلم بعد فراغه أنه أصاب إذ لم يجزم بفسادها في ابتدائها، فإن لم يعلم حاله لا فيها ولا بعدها، أو علم الخطأ فيها أو بعدها، أو علم الإصابة وهو فيها، فسدت في هذه الأقسام الأربع من هذه الصورة، وبقي صورة من صور التحري، وهي ما لو تحرى ووقـع تحريـه إلى جهة فصلي إلى جهة أخرى، وفي هذه لا تجزئه أصاب أو لم يصب؛ أما إذا لم يصيب فظاهر، وأما إذا أصاب فلتركه ما هو مخاطب به من الاستقبال بالاجتهاد واعتقاده الفساد، لأن الجهة التي أدّى إليها اجتهاده صارت قائمة مقام الكعبة في حقه، فلا يجوز له تركها، وهذا على قولهما، وقال أبو يوسف تصح إذا ظهر صوابه لأن المقصود قد حصل كما لو تحرى في الأواني وعدل عن تحريـه إلى آخــر فظهر طهارته صحت صلاته. وعند أبي حنيفة ومحمد لا تصح؛ مؤاخذة له باعتقاده فسادها، فلا تنقلب صحيحة لو ظهر إصابته بعده، وعلى هذا لو صلى في ثوب وعنده أنه نجس، ثم ظهر أنه طاهر، أو صلى وعنده أنه محدث فظهر أنه متوضئ أو صلى الفرض وعنده أن الوقت لم يدخل فظهر أنه قد دخل، لا يجزئه لأن الشرط وإن تبين وجوده لكن هنا شرط آخر، وهو: أن لا يحكم بفساد فعله ابتداء؛ لأنه حينئذ لا تكون نيته صحيحة، لعدم الجزم، وفي الماء الذي عدل إليه وجـد الجـزم بالنية والطهارة حقيقة ،فصحت انتهى من «الدراية»، و«الفتح»، و« التبيين»، وغيرها.
A note: Know from what we have mentioned three scenarios from the issues of taharrī: 1- Validity of prayer with doubt, 2- With taharrī even if he knows error during it, just as if he knows error after completion, 3- Its validity not with doubt nor taharrī, such that if he prayed on a dark night without taharrī and no doubt, then it is permissible until his error appears with certainty or strong presumption, even after completion, in which case he must repeat. And its validity with doubt and leaving taharrī. The condition in these scenarios for validity is that he knows after completion that he was correct, since he did not judge its invalidity at the beginning. For if he does not know his state either during or after, or knows error during or after, or knows correctness during it, then it becomes invalid in these four subdivisions of this picture. And there remains a picture from the pictures of taharrī: that he makes taharrī and his taharrī directs to one direction, but he prays to another direction. In this, it does not suffice him whether he is correct or not. As for if he is not correct, it is obvious. As for if he is correct, it is because he abandoned what he was obligated with: facing by ijtihad, and his belief in its invalidity. Because the direction to which his ijtihad led became standing in place of the Kaaba for him, so it is not permissible for him to leave it. This is according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said: It is valid if his correctness appears, because the objective was achieved, just as if he makes ijtihad regarding vessels and deviates from his ijtihad to another and its purity appears, his prayer is valid. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, it is not valid; he is held responsible for his belief in its invalidity, so it does not become valid even if his correctness appears afterwards. And upon this, if he prays in a garment thinking it impure, then it appears pure, or prays thinking he is in hadath and then appears to have wudu, or prays fard thinking the time has not entered and then appears that it had entered, it does not suffice him, because even if the condition appears in existence, there is another condition: that he does not judge his act invalid at the beginning, because then his intention is not correct for lack of certainty. In the case of water to which he deviated, there was certainty in intention and actual purity, so it was valid. End from al-Diraya, al-Fath, al-Tabyin, and others.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage summarizes three scenarios related to taharrī (ijtihad for qibla) derived from the previous discussion. The first scenario: prayer with doubt (shakk) but without taharrī is valid only if after completion he learns he was correct; otherwise invalid. The second: with taharrī, even if error is discovered during or after prayer, the prayer is valid (as per the earlier building ruling). The third: prayer without either doubt or taharrī (e.g., praying confidently on a dark night) is conditionally valid until error is certain, then redoing is required. The condition for validity in all these is that he does not know the state during prayer but learns correctness after. If he knows error or correctness during, it invalidates. Then the passage discusses a dispute: if one does taharrī but deliberately prays to a different direction, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two) say the prayer is absolutely invalid, whether he was actually correct or not, because his ijtihad has made that direction the qibla for him. Abu Yusuf says it is valid if he was correct, analogy to taharrī for vessels where deviation to a clean source suffices. The Hanafi response uses examples of praying in a garment thought impure, etc., to show that belief in invalidity nullifies the act even if reality differs. The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Key Terms
التحري (al-taharrī): Making ijtihad to determine the qibla direction
اجتهاد (ijtihād): Scholarly effort to deduce the correct direction, here for qibla
قائمة مقام الكعبة (qā'imatan maqām al-ka'bah): The direction indicated by ijtihad stands in place of the actual Kaaba for that person

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The prayer is valid because he faced the true qibla
B) The prayer is invalid because he abandoned his ijtihad
C) The prayer is valid according to Abu Yusuf's opinion

Key Takeaway
The direction indicated by one's ijtihad becomes legally equivalent to the Kaaba; abandoning it invalidates the prayer even if one accidentally faces the true Qibla.

Knowledge of Correct Qibla During Prayer Invalidates It
Ruling on knowledge of correct qibla during prayer — intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a person who began prayer with taharrī becomes certain of the qibla during the prayer, and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad from Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
If you become certain of the qibla during prayer, your prayer breaks—strong cannot be built on weak.

This lesson examines a subtle situation: a person begins prayer with taharrī (estimation of qibla) and then, during the prayer, becomes certain or strongly believes he is facing the correct direction. How does this knowledge affect the validity of the prayer? The Hanafi school, through a famous intra-madhhab dispute, addresses this with a principle of legal analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its initial state
The person started prayer with taharrī (weak state of uncertainty). This is the foundation upon which the prayer is built.
Taharrī is a zanni (speculative) method; the prayer is valid only if later proven correct.
2
State the disputed ruling
When knowledge of correctness occurs during the prayer, the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) rule the prayer invalid (fasid). Abu Yusuf rules it valid.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf recorded in zahir al-riwayah.
3
Examine the majority's proof
The proof is an analogy (qiyas khafiy): like an illiterate who learns a surah during prayer – his prior recitation becomes invalid; like a gesture-prayer who becomes able to perform pillars – the strong cannot be built on the weak.
The illa (effective cause) is the inability to build a strong state on a weak foundation.
4
Examine Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf argues that the condition of taharrī was fulfilled, so the prayer should continue; knowledge does not disrupt it.
His proof is based on istishab al-hal (presumption of continuity).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is the majority view: the prayer becomes invalid and must be restarted.
If one follows Abu Yusuf, the prayer continues; but the fatwa is on the majority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنْ عَلِمَ بإصابتِهِ فيها فَسَدَتْ، كما لو لم يعلم إصابتَهُ أصلاً . ( وإنْ عَلِمَ بإصابتِهِ فِيْهَا ) يقيناً، أو بأكبر رأيه (فَسَدَتْ)؛ لأن حالته قويت بالعلم، وبناء القوي علـى الضعيف لا يجوز، وعند أبي يوسف يبني لما ذكرنا، قلنا: هو كالأمي إذا تعلم ســـورة، والمومـي إذا قدر على الأركان فيها تفسد، وبعدها تصح لقوة ما بقي وضعف الماضي، فلا يُبنـى قـوي عـلـى ضعيف، (كَمَا ) فسدت فيما لو لم يعلم إصابته أصلاً وقد شرع فيها شاكاً بلا تحر؛ لأن الأصل هو الفساد وهو ثابت باستصحاب الحال، ولم يرتفع بدليل)، فتقرر الفساد لعدم حصول المشروط لا حقيقة ولا حكماً (۳)، كما في ( البدائع»، و«التبيين»، و«الفتح». تنبيه علم مما ذكرناه ثلاث صور من مسائل التحري : ١- صحة الصلاة مع الشك، ٢- والتحري ولو علم بالخطأ وهو في أثنائها، كما لو علم بالخطأ بعد فراغه، ٣ - وصحتها لا مع شك ولا تحر، حتَّى إذا صلّى في ليلة مظلمة من غير تحرّ ولاشك فهو على الجواز، حتّى يظهر خطؤه بيقين، أو بأكبر رأيه ولو بعد الفراغ فيلزمه الإعادة، وصحتها مع الشك وترك التحري، والشرط في هذه الصور للصحة: أن يعلم بعد فراغه أنه أصاب إذ لم يجزم بفسادها في ابتدائها، فإن لم يعلم حاله لا فيها ولا بعدها، أو علم الخطأ فيها أو بعدها، أو علم الإصابة وهو فيها، فسدت في هذه الأقسام الأربع من هذه الصورة
And if he knows that he has hit the direction during it, it becomes invalid, just as if he did not know his hitting at all. (And if he knows with certainty of his hitting during it), or with his preponderant opinion, (it becomes invalid) because his state has strengthened by knowledge, and building the strong upon the weak is not permissible. According to Abu Yusuf, he builds upon it for what we have mentioned. We said: He is like the illiterate person when he learns a surah, and the one who gestures when he is able to perform the pillars during it—it becomes invalid, and after it becomes valid due to the strength of what remains and the weakness of the past, so the strong is not built upon the weak. (Just as) it became invalid when he did not know his hitting at all and began it in doubt without estimation, because the original rule is invalidity and it is established by istishab al-hal, and it is not removed by evidence. So invalidity is established due to the non-attainment of the condition neither in reality nor by legal fiction (hukman). As in al-Bada'i, al-Tabyin, and al-Fath. Note: You learn from what we have mentioned three types of cases of estimation: 1- Validity of prayer with doubt, 2- And estimation even if he knows the error during it, just as if he knows the error after his completion, 3- And its validity without doubt and without estimation, such that if he prays on a dark night without estimation and without doubt, it is permissible until his error becomes apparent with certainty or with his preponderant opinion, even if after completion, then he must repeat. And its validity with doubt and abandonment of estimation, and the condition in these types for validity: that he knows after his completion that he hit the direction, since he did not deem it invalid at its beginning. If he does not know his state during it nor after it, or he knows the error during it or after it, or he knows the hitting during it, then it becomes invalid in these four divisions of this type.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah deals with the ruling on one who begins prayer with taharrī (estimation of qibla) and then, during the prayer, becomes certain or strongly believes that he is facing the correct direction. The text rules that such knowledge invalidates the prayer, as the initial weak foundation (taharrī) cannot support the strong certainty. A key intra-Hanafi dispute is reported: Abu Yusuf holds that he may continue building on his initial prayer, while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad rule it invalid. The author supports the majority view with an analogy: just as an illiterate person who learns a surah mid-prayer invalidates what he recited and starts anew, or a person who gestures (mumī) but becomes able to perform actual pillars — the strong cannot be built on the weak. The text then lists three images (صور) of taharrī cases: (1) validity if he prayed with doubt but later knew he hit direction; (2) validity if he made taharrī and later learned error during prayer (same as after completion); (3) validity if he prayed without any taharrī or doubt — but must repeat if error becomes apparent. The condition for validity in all three is that he only knows he was correct after completion. If he knows error or correctness during prayer, or remains ignorant, the prayer is invalid. The summary categorizes four scenarios where prayer is invalidated.

Key Terms
تحري (taharrī): Effort to determine the direction of qibla by reasoning and signs when the direction is unknown.
استصحاب الحال (istishāb al-ḥāl): Presumption that a previous state of affairs (here, the invalidity of prayer due to uncertainty) continues until evidence to the contrary.
فسدت (fasadat): The prayer becomes invalid (fasid) and must be repeated; not necessarily sinful if done with valid excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if a person who began prayer with taharrī becomes certain he is facing the qibla during the prayer, what is the ruling?
A) Valid, continue.
B) Invalid, must restart.
C) Valid only if he is certain.
D) Invalid only if he was wrong.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi majority holds that if knowledge of correct qibla occurs during prayer, the prayer becomes invalid and must be restarted.

Praying to a Different Direction After Taharrī
Intra-Hanafi dispute on prayer validity after taharrī deviation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of prayer when one prays to a different direction than his ijtihad indicated, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Believing your act invalid at the start voids the prayer, even if it later meets conditions—intention requires certainty.

This passage examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a person who makes taharrī to determine the qibla but then prays in a different direction. The key question is whether accidentally facing the correct qibla can validate an otherwise invalid intention. The Hanafi school splits on this, with the majority ruling that the subjective belief of invalidity at the time of prayer renders it void.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, the prayer is invalid whether he hits the qibla or not. The reason: he abandoned his ijtihad, which made that direction binding, and he believed his prayer invalid at the start.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Abu Yusuf says the prayer is valid if it becomes apparent that he faced the true qibla, because the objective (facing the Kaaba) was achieved.
This is a legitimate intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Abu Yusuf analogizes to the case of estimating pure vessels: if one deviates from his estimation but the vessel he uses turns out pure, the act is valid.
The analogy is based on the principle that the objective (purity) was attained.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The majority distinguish: in the vessel case, the person had certainty of intention (he believed the vessel pure). In the qibla case, he believed his act invalid, so intention lacked certainty (jazzm).
Thus, the analogy fails because the key condition (certainty of intention) is missing.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, Abu Yusuf would validate the prayer if the qibla was hit, so no repetition; the majority require repetition. The mufta bihi position is the majority view.
This affects real-life fatwa: one must repeat the prayer according to the relied-upon ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبقي صورة من صور التحري، وهي ما لو تحرى ووقع تحريه إلى جهة فصلى إلى جهة أخرى، وفي هذه لا تجزئه أصاب أو لم يصب؛ أما إذا لم يصيب فظاهر، وأما إذا أصاب فلتركه ما هو مخاطب به من الاستقبال بالاجتهاد واعتقاده الفساد، لأن الجهة التي أدّى إليها اجتهاده صارت قائمة مقام الكعبة في حقه، فلا يجوز له تركها، وهذا على قولهما، وقال أبو يوسف تصح إذا ظهر صوابه لأن المقصود قد حصل كما لو تحرى في الأواني وعدل عن تحريه إلى آخر فظهر طهارته صحت صلاته. وعند أبي حنيفة ومحمد لا تصح؛ مؤاخذة له باعتقاده فسادها، فلا تنقلب صحيحة لو ظهر إصابته بعده، وعلى هذا لو صلى في ثوب وعنده أنه نجس، ثم ظهر أنه طاهر، أو صلى وعنده أنه محدث فظهر أنه متوضئ أو صلى الفرض وعنده أن الوقت لم يدخل فظهر أنه قد دخل، لا يجزئه لأن الشرط وإن تبين وجوده لكن هنا شرط آخر، وهو: أن لا يحكم بفساد فعله ابتداء؛ لأنه حينئذ لا تكون نيته صحيحة، لعدم الجزم، وفي الماء الذي عدل إليه وجد الجزم بالنية والطهارة حقيقة ،فصحت انتهى من «الدراية»، و«الفتح»، و« التبيين»، وغيرها.
And a remaining type of the types of estimation: that he estimates and his estimation falls upon one direction, but he prays to another direction. In this, it does not suffice him whether he hit or missed. As for if he missed, it is obvious. As for if he hit, it is because he abandoned what he was obligated to do: facing the qibla through his ijtihad, and his belief of its invalidity. Because the direction to which his ijtihad led him has become in his right like the Kaaba, so it is not permissible for him to abandon it. And this is according to their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's?) saying. Abu Yusuf said: It is valid if his correctness becomes apparent because the objective has been attained, just as if he estimated regarding vessels and deviated from his estimation to another and its purity appeared, his prayer is valid. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, it is not valid; because he is taken to task for his belief in its invalidity, so it does not become valid even if his hitting appears afterward. And upon this, if he prays in a garment thinking it is najis, then it appears that it is tahir, or prays thinking he is hadith then appears that he has wudu, or prays fard thinking the time has not entered then appears that it has entered, it does not suffice him because the condition (even if it is found to exist) but here there is another condition: that he does not judge his act as invalid at the beginning; because then his intention is not valid due to lack of certainty. In the water he deviated to, there was certainty of intention and actual purity, so it was valid. End from al-Dirayah, al-Fath, al-Tabyin, and others.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a person who, after making taharrī and determining a specific direction, actually prays facing a different direction. The text states that according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, such a prayer is invalid whether he accidentally faces the correct qibla or not. The reason is that he abandoned his own ijtihad, which had made that direction sacred for him, and his own belief at the time was that his prayer was invalid (since he prayed in a direction other than his estimated one). Abu Yusuf, however, argues that if it later becomes apparent that he did face the true qibla, the prayer is valid because the objective (facing the Kaaba) was achieved, similar to a case where one estimates about vessels containing water and then drinks from a different vessel that turns out to be pure. The text then extends the principle to other analogous situations: praying in a garment thought to be najis (impure) that later proves pure, or praying thinking one is in a state of impurity when actually pure, or praying before the thought entry of time that actually entered. In all these, the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) rule that the prayer is invalid because the person initially believed it invalid, which vitiates the intention (niyyah) due to lack of certainty (jazzm). The key distinction is that in the vessel analogy of Abu Yusuf, the person had certainty of intention and purity at the time, so it is valid. The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): Intention, which must be present and certain for an act of worship to be valid.
اجتهاد (ijtihād): The effort to determine the correct qibla through signs and reasoning.
لا تجزئه (lā tujzī’uhu): It does not suffice him; the act is not valid and must be repeated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which condition does the text identify as necessary for the validity of prayer when one initially believed it invalid?
A) The actual conditions (qibla, purity, time) must be met.
B) The person must not judge his act as invalid at the beginning.
C) The person must make taharrī again.
D) The person must have certainty after completion.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the subjective belief of invalidity at the time of prayer renders the prayer invalid, even if objective conditions are later met—intention (niyyah) requires certainty (jazzm).

Ruling on Congregation Facing Different Directions Due to Ignorance of Imam's Qibla
Ruling on validity of prayer when followers independently determine qibla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which followers praying behind an imam in different qibla directions due to ijtihad have a valid prayer, and identify the exceptions that invalidate it.

Core Idea
If followers independently determine the qibla, their prayer is valid as long as they are ignorant of the imam's error and not ahead of him.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah addresses a situation where the qibla is unclear, and followers perform ijtihad individually. The default ruling is that their prayer is valid even if they face different directions, analogous to praying inside the Kaaba. However, two exceptions invalidate the prayer: knowledge that the imam is facing the wrong qibla, or knowledge of being ahead of the imam. Understanding these nuances prevents unnecessary invalidation of prayers in challenging circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize the context: followers in darkness or other conditions where the qibla is unclear, each performing ijtihad to determine direction.
The key is that they are ignorant of the imam's own direction.
2
State the default ruling
The prayer is valid (sahih) even though followers face different directions. This is because each direction is the qibla for the one who made ijtihad.
3
Understand the analogy
The ruling is analogous to prayer inside the Kaaba with a congregation, where everyone faces different interior walls but the prayer is valid.
The essence is that the obligation of facing the qibla is fulfilled through ijtihad.
4
Identify the exceptions
Two cases invalidate the prayer: 1) The follower knows that the imam is facing the wrong qibla. 2) The follower knows that he is standing ahead of the imam.
In the first case, the follower believes the imam's prayer is invalid, so he cannot follow him. In the second, he abandons the obligation of standing behind the imam.
5
Distinguish the exceptions
In the first exception, the follower did his best in ijtihad and had no capacity to correct the imam. In the second, he had knowledge and ability to stand behind, so his prayer is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو تحرى قوم جهات، وجهلوا حال إمامهم تجزيهم. (ولو تحرّى قوم جهات) في ظلمة (وجهلوا حال إمامهم) في توجهه (تُجْزِيهُمْ) تحريـهـم إذا كانوا خلف الإمام، لوجود الاستقبال؛ لأن كل جهة منها قبلة في حق الذي تحرى إليها، ولا يضرهـم هـذا الاختلاف، كالصلاة في جوف الكعبة بجماعة، أما من علم في حال اقتدائه مخالفة إمامه، فقد اقتدى بمن يعتقد بطلان صلاته بالنسبة إليه لاعتقاده خطأه في توجهه، ومن علم تقدمـه عـلـى إمامه، لا تصح صلاته؛ لتركه فرض المقام، سواء علم حال الاقتداء أو بعده، والفرق بين علمه بمخالفته جهة إمامه، وعلمه بتقدمه عليه بعد الفراغ، أنه في الأول : أتى بما في وسعه في حق الجهة بالتحري فأجزأه، وفي الثانية: ترك ما في قدرته وهو العلم بالوقوف خلف الإمام وفي وسعه علمه بذلك، ففسدت به صلاته.
And if a group of people independently determine [the qibla] directions, and they are ignorant of the state of their imam [regarding his direction], it suffices them. (And if a group independently determine directions) in darkness (and they are ignorant of the state of their imam) in his facing direction, (it suffices them) their ijtihad when they are behind the imam, due to the existence of facing the qibla; because each direction is the qibla for the one who made ijtihad towards it, and this difference does not harm them, like the prayer inside the Kaaba with a congregation. However, the one who knows during his following that he is contradicting his imam, he has followed someone whom he believes his prayer is invalid relative to him due to his belief that the imam is wrong in his direction. And the one who knows that he is ahead of his imam, his prayer is not valid because he leaves the obligation of station, whether he knows at the time of following or after. And the difference between his knowledge of contradicting the imam's direction and his knowledge of being ahead of him after completion is that in the first, he did what was within his capacity regarding the direction by ijtihad, so it sufficed him; in the second, he left what was within his power, which is the knowledge of standing behind the imam, and within his capacity was knowledge of that, so his prayer became invalid.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling for a congregation when followers are uncertain about the qibla direction of their imam. The scenario is darkness or similar conditions where each follower performs ijtihad (independent reasoning) to determine the qibla. Their prayer is valid even if they face different directions because each direction is considered the correct qibla for the individual who made ijtihad. This is analogous to praying inside the Kaaba with a congregation, where everyone faces a different part of the interior but the prayer is valid. However, there are two exceptions. First, if a follower knows that the imam is facing the wrong direction, then his own prayer is invalid because he believes the imam's prayer is invalid, and one cannot follow someone whose prayer is invalid in one's own belief. Second, if a follower knows that he is standing ahead of the imam (i.e., closer to the qibla), then his prayer is invalid because he has abandoned the obligation of standing behind the imam. The key distinction is between these two cases: in the first case, the follower did his best in ijtihad and cannot be blamed; in the second, he had knowledge that he was ahead and could have corrected his position, so his prayer is invalid.

Key Terms
تحرى (taharra): To exercise ijtihad to determine the qibla direction when it is unclear.
جهة (jihah): Direction, specifically the qibla direction as determined by ijtihad.
فرض المقام (fard al-maqam): The obligation of standing behind the imam in congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The follower faces a different direction from the imam but is unaware of the imam's direction.
B) The follower knows during the prayer that the imam is facing the wrong qibla.
C) The follower is uncertain about the qibla and prays without ijtihad.
D) The follower stands behind the imam but faces the same direction.

Key Takeaway
The validity of congregational prayer when followers independently determine qibla depends on ignorance of the imam's direction and not being ahead of him; knowledge of the imam's error or being ahead invalidates the prayer.

Definition of Wajib and the First Two Wajibat: Fatiha and Adding a Surah
Defining wajib and specifying first two wajibat of prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define wajib in Hanafi fiqh and explain why reciting al-Fatiha and adding a surah are classified as wajib rather than fard.

Core Idea
Wajib is distinct from fard: it is proven by probable evidence and leaving it does not invalidate the prayer.

This lesson introduces the Hanafi concept of wajib (obligatory) in prayer, which is a category between fard and sunnah. We will examine the definition of wajib, the types of evidence that establish it, and the first two rulings in this category: reciting Surah al-Fatiha and adding another surah. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly assessing the validity and deficiency of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Define wajib linguistically and technically
Identify the linguistic meanings (binding, falling, agitation) and the technical definition: 'what is binding upon us through evidence containing doubt'. Note that this distinguishes wajib from fard.
Think of shubha as probabilistic evidence, e.g., khabar wahid.
2
Classify scriptural evidences
Learn the four types of evidence based on thubut (transmission certainty) and dalala (meaning certainty). Understand that fard requires qat'i thubut and qat'i dalala, while wajib can be established by zanni thubut or zanni dalala.
Focus on types 2 and 3: qat'i thubut + zanni dalala and zanni thubut + qat'i dalala both yield wujub.
3
Apply to reciting al-Fatiha
The hadith 'La salata liman lam yaqra' bi-Fatiha al-Kitab' is khabar wahid (zanni thubut) but its meaning is qat'i (negation of prayer). Therefore it establishes wujub, not fard. The Quranic general command 'faqra'u ma tayassara' supports permissibility of other recitation.
Hanafis interpret the negation as negation of perfection.
4
Apply to adding a surah
Similarly, the hadith combining Fatiha and a surah is also khabar wahid, so adding a surah is wajib. This applies to two unspecified rak'ahs of obligatory prayers.
Two unspecific rak'ahs are the first two in four- or three-rak'ah prayers.
5
Identify consequences of omission
Leaving a wajib intentionally: sin, must repeat prayer. Forgetfully: sajda al-sahw is wajib. Not compensating leaves the fard deficient.
This contrasts with omitting a sunnah (no sin, no compensation) or a rukn (prayer invalid).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان واجب الصلاة
وهو ثمانية عشر شيئاً قراءة الفاتحة، وضم سورة، أو ثلاث آيات في ركعتين غير متعينتين من الفرض،
الواجب في اللغة يجيء بمعنى اللزوم وبمعنى السقوط وبمعنى الاضطراب، وفي الشرع اسم لما لزمنا بدليل فيه شبهة. قال فخر الإسلام وإنما سمي به إما لكونه ساقطاً عنا علماً، أو لكونه ساقطاً علينا عملاً، أو لكونه مضطرباً ما بين الفرض والسنة، أو بين اللزوم وعدم اللزوم، فإنه يلزمنا عملاً لا علماً، واعلم أن الأدلة السمعية أنواع أربعة قطعي الثبوت والدلالة كالنصوص المتواترة، وقطعي الثبوت ظني الدلالة كالآيات المؤولة، وظني الثبوت قطعي الدلالة كأخبار الآحاد التي مفهومها قطعي، وظني الثبوت والدلالة كأخبار الآحاد التي مفهومها ظني، فبالأول يثبت الفرض وبالثاني والثالث يثبت الوجوب، وبالرابع تثبت السنة والاستحباب؛ ليكون ثبوت الحكم بقدر دليله كذا في « التبيين ، واعلم أن الواجبات شرعت لإكمال الفرائض، والسنن شرعت لإكمال الواجبات، والأدب شرع لإكمال السنن؛ ليكون كل منها حصناً لما شرع لتكميله، وحكم الواجب استحقاق العقاب بتركه ، وعدم إكفار جاحده، والثواب بفعله، وحكمه في الصلاة دخول النقص فيها بتركه، ووجوب سجود السهو بتركه سهواً، وإعادتها بتركه عمداً، وسقوط الفرض ناقصاً إن لم يسجد ولم يعد الصلاة في تركه عمداً أو سهواً، وقدمنا تعريف الفرض والسنة والأدب. (وَهُوَ) أي: الواجب ( ثمانية عشَرَ شيئاً). يجب (قِرَاءةُ الفَاتِحَةِ) المواظبته عليها ولقوله : « لا صلاة لمن لم يقرأ بفاتحة الكتاب » وهو خبر آحاد فأوجب العمل، فتكره الصلاة بتركها تحريماً، ولا تفسد بترك الفاتحة لو قرأ غيرها؛ لإطلاق قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاقْرَهُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ﴾ [الم : ٢٠] ولا يقيد بالخبر المذكور لأنه نسخ، ولا يجوز بخبر الواحد. (وَ) يجب (ضم سُورةٍ) قصيرة، (أو ثلاث آيات) قصار، لقوله : لا صلاةَ لِمَنْ لَمْ يَقْرَأَ بِالْحَمْدُ وَسُورَةٍ فِي فَريضَةِ أَوْ غَيْرهَا )) رواه الترمذي، والكلام عليه كما في حديث الفاتحة، فيجب قراءة الفاتحة وضم سورة (في ركعتين غيرِ مُتَعَينتين من ركعات ( الفَرْضِ) الرباعي والثلاثي، لأنه الأصل، وحكم الركعة الثانية كالأولى، كما قدمنــا فـي الأمــر
Section on explaining the obligatory (wajib) of prayer. And it is eighteen things: recitation of al-Fatiha, and adding a surah or three verses in two unspecified rak'ahs of the obligatory prayer. Wajib linguistically means binding, falling, and agitation. In sacred law it is a name for what is binding upon us through evidence containing doubt. Fakhr al-Islam said: It is named so either because it is falling from us in knowledge, or because it is falling upon us in action, or because it is agitated between fard and sunnah, or between binding and non-binding; for it binds us in action not in knowledge. Know that scriptural evidences are four types: definitive in transmission and meaning like recurrent texts; definitive in transmission but probable in meaning like interpretable verses; probable in transmission but definitive in meaning like solitary hadith whose meaning is definitive; probable in transmission and meaning like solitary hadith whose meaning is probable. By the first, fard is established; by the second and third, wujub is established; by the fourth, sunnah and recommendation are established; so that the establishment of the ruling is according to its evidence, as in al-Tabyin. Know that wajibat are legislated to complete the fara'id, sunan to complete the wajibat, and adab to complete the sunan; so that each is a fortress for what it is legislated to complete. The ruling of wajib is: deserving punishment for leaving it, not deeming its denier a disbeliever, reward for performing it; and its ruling in prayer: the occurrence of deficiency in it by leaving it, obligation of sajda al-sahw for leaving it forgetfully, repetition if left intentionally, and the falling of the fard deficient if he does not prostrate and does not repeat the prayer, whether leaving it intentionally or forgetfully. We have previously defined fard, sunnah, and adab. (And it) i.e., the wajib (is eighteen things). Recitation of al-Fatiha is obligatory (must be adhered to) and because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'No prayer for one who does not recite the Fatiha of the Book' – it is a solitary hadith, so it necessitates action. Thus, prayer is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahriman) by leaving it, but the prayer is not invalidated by leaving al-Fatiha if one recites something else, due to the general meaning of Allah's saying: 'So recite what is easy [of the Quran]' (al-Muzzammil:20) and it is not restricted by the mentioned hadith because it is abrogated, and abrogation by solitary hadith is not permissible. (And) it is obligatory (to add a surah), short, (or three verses) short, because of his saying: 'No prayer for one who does not recite al-Hamd and a surah in an obligatory prayer or other' – narrated by al-Tirmidhi, and the discussion on it is like the hadith of al-Fatiha. So it is obligatory to recite al-Fatiha and add a surah (in two unspecified rak'ahs of the obligatory) four-rak'ah and three-rak'ah prayer, because that is the original, and the ruling of the second rak'ah is like the first, as we have mentioned in the command.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage opens a new section on the obligatory (wajib) elements of prayer. The author first gives a linguistic and technical definition of wajib in Hanafi fiqh. Linguistically, it can mean binding, falling, or agitation. Technically, it is what is binding upon us through evidence that contains some doubt (shubha). This is a key Hanafi distinction: fard is established by qat'i evidence (Quran or mutawatir hadith), while wajib is established by zanni evidence (khabar wahid). The author then categorizes scriptural evidences into four types based on certainty of transmission (thubut) and meaning (dalala). Fard is proven by the first type, wujub by the second and third, and sunnah/istihbab by the fourth. The author explains that wajibat complete the fara'id, sunan complete the wajibat, and adab complete the sunan. The consequences of leaving a wajib: sin, sajda al-sahw if forgetful, repeating the prayer if intentional, and deficiency in the fard if not compensated. The author then lists the first two of the eighteen wajibat: reciting Surah al-Fatiha and adding another surah (or three short verses) in two rak'ahs of an obligatory prayer (the first two rak'ahs in four- or three-rak'ah prayers). He provides evidence from hadith (khabar wahid) but clarifies that these are wajib, not fard, because the hadith is solitary and cannot abrogate the general Quranic command to recite what is easy. Therefore, leaving al-Fatiha intentionally makes the prayer deficient but not invalid; one must perform sajda al-sahw or repeat the prayer. This is the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
الواجب (al-wajib): In Hanafi fiqh, what is binding by evidence that contains doubt (shubha), between fard and sunnah; leaving it incurs sin but the prayer is not invalidated.
خبر آحاد (khabar wahid): A solitary hadith, which is zanni al-thubut (probable in transmission) and thus cannot establish fard or abrogate Quran.
سجود السهو (sajda al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness, wajib when a wajib is omitted or delayed in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why is reciting Surah al-Fatiha in prayer considered wajib rather than fard?
A) Because it is proven by a solitary hadith (khabar wahid).
B) Because it is proven by a mutawatir hadith.
C) Because the Quran explicitly commands it.
D) Because the Prophet always did it.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, reciting al-Fatiha and adding a surah are wajib, not fard, because they are proven by solitary hadith; omitting them invalidates the perfection of prayer, not the prayer itself.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Concept of Wajib and the First Seven Wajibat of Salah
Defining the category of wajib and explaining the first seven wajibat of salah with dalil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of wajib, distinguish it from fard based on evidence certainty, and apply the ruling that omitting a wajib requires sajdah sahw but does not invalidate the prayer.

Core Idea
A wajib is proven by zanni evidence; its omission requires sajdah sahw, not repetition.

In the Hanafi school, not every obligatory act is a fard. Some acts are wajib—binding but established by evidence that contains some uncertainty. This lesson unpacks the definition of wajib, the four-fold classification of revealed evidence, and the first seven wajibat of prayer with their proofs. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for correctly evaluating the consequences of omission in salah.

Guided Path
1
Define wajib in Hanafi fiqh
Start with the linguistic and terminological definition. Note that wajib binds in action but not in knowledge (itmam al-ilm). Its proof contains shubha (uncertainty).
The text gives four possible reasons for the name 'wajib'.
2
Classify the four types of revealed evidence
Identify the categories: qat'i thubut & qat'i dalala (fard), qat'i thubut & zanni dalala (wajib), zanni thubut & qat'i dalala (wajib), zanni thubut & zanni dalala (sunnah/mustahabb).
This explains why some rulings are fard and others wajib.
3
List the first seven wajibat of salah
From the text: (1) recitation of al-Fatihah, (2) adding a short surah or three verses in two rak'ahs of fard and all of witr/nafl, (3) specifying recitation in first two rak'ahs of fard, (4) giving precedence to Fatihah over the surah, (5) pressing the nose with the forehead in sajdah, (6) performing the second sajdah before moving to another action, (7) tranquility (itminan) in the pillars.
Each is supported by a hadith or constant practice.
4
Analyze the dispute on itminan
Note that Abu Yusuf considers itminan fard, while the majority (Abu Hanifah, Muhammad) consider it wajib. The mufta bihi is that it is wajib.
The hadith of the 'Musi' salatuh' is cited by Abu Yusuf.
5
Apply the consequence of omitting a wajib
If a wajib is omitted forgetfully, sajdah sahw is required. If omitted deliberately, the prayer is still valid but sinful, and sajdah sahw is still needed. The prayer becomes deficient but is not invalidated.
This contrasts with omission of a rukn, which invalidates the prayer.

Source Text
