فصل في بيان واجب الصلاة
الواجب في اللغة يجيء بمعنى اللزوم وبمعنى السقوط وبمعنى الاضطراب، وفي الشرع اسم لما لزمنا بدليل فيه شبهة. قال فخر الإسلام وإنما سمي به إما لكونه ساقطاً عنا علماً، أو لكونه ساقطاً علينا عملاً، أو لكونه مضطرباً ما بين الفرض والسنة، أو بين اللزوم وعدم اللزوم، فإنه يلزمنا عملاً لا علماً، واعلم أن الأدلة السمعية أنواع أربعة قطعي الثبوت والدلالة كالنصوص المتواترة، وقطعي الثبوت ظني الدلالة كالآيات المؤولة، وظني الثبوت قطعي الدلالة كأخبار الآحاد التي مفهومها قطعي، وظني الثبوت والدلالة كأخبار الآحاد التي مفهومها ظني، فبالأول يثبت الفرض وبالثاني والثالث يثبت الوجوب، وبالرابع تثبت السنة والاستحباب؛ ليكون ثبوت الحكم بقدر دليله كذا في « التبيين »، واعلم أن الواجبات شرعت لإكمال الفرائض، والسنن شرعت لإكمال الواجبات، والأدب شرع لإكمال السنن؛ ليكون كل منها حصناً لما شرع لتكميله، وحكم الواجب استحقاق العقاب بتركه، وعدم إكفار جاحده، والثواب بفعله، وحكمه في الصلاة دخول النقص فيها بتركه، ووجوب سجود السهو بتركه سهواً، وإعادتها بتركه عمداً، وسقوط الفرض ناقصاً إن لم يسجد ولم يعد الصلاة في تركه عمداً أو سهواً، وقدمنا تعريف الفرض والسنة والأدب. (وهو) أي: الواجب (ثمانية عشر شيئاً). يجب (قراءة الفاتحة) المواظبة عليها ولقوله : « لا صلاة لمن لم يقرأ بفاتحة الكتاب » وهو خبر آحاد فأوجب العمل، فتكره الصلاة بتركها تحريماً، ولا تفسد بترك الفاتحة لو قرأ غيرها؛ لإطلاق قوله تعالى: « فَاقْرَؤُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ » [المزمل: ٢٠] ولا يقيد بالخبر المذكور لأنه نسخ، ولا يجوز بخبر الواحد. (و) يجب (ضم سورة) قصيرة، (أو ثلاث آيات) قصار، لقوله : « لا صلاة لمن لم يقرأ بالحمد وسورة في فريضة أو غيرها » رواه الترمذي، والكلام عليه كما في حديث الفاتحة، فيجب قراءة الفاتحة وضم سورة (في ركعتين غير متعينتين من ركعات الفرض الرباعي والثلاثي، لأنه الأصل، وحكم الركعة الثانية كالأولى، كما قدمنا في الأمر. وفي جميع ركعات الوتر والنفل. وتجب قراءة الفاتحة (و) ضم سورة (في جميع ركعات الوتر)، (و) جميع ركعات (النفل) لما روينا، ولأن كل ركعتين من النافلة صلاة على حدة، فلذا خالفت الفرض والوتر مشابهة للنفل. (و) يجب (تعيين القراءة) أي: قراءة الفاتحة وسورة (في الأوليين) من الفرض؛ لمواظبة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم على القراءة فيهما، ولما روي أن عمر ترك القراءة في ركعة من المغرب فقضاها في الثالثة، ولم تجب في الأخريين لقول علي : « القراءة في الأوليين قراءة في الأخريين »، وعن ابن مسعود وعائشة التخيير في الأخريين « إن شاء قرأ، وإن شاء سبح » (و) يجب (تقديم الفاتحة على قراءة السورة)؛ لمواظبة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم على ذلك، حتى لو قرأ من السورة ابتداء فتذكر يقرأ الفاتحة ثم يقرأ السورة ويسجد للسهو، كما لو كرر الفاتحة قبل قراءة السورة (و) يجب (ضم الأنف) أي: ما صلب منه للجبهة في السجود) للمواظبة عليه، ولا يجوز الاقتصار على الأنف في السجود على الصحيح كما قدمناه. (و) تجب مراعاة الترتيب فيما بين السجدتين، وهو (الإتيان بالسجدة الثانية في كل ركعة) من الفرض وغيره (قبل الانتقال لغيرها) أي: لغير السجدة من باقي أفعال الصلاة للمواظبة على ذلك، ولما قدمناه في بيان الفرائض، حتى لو نسي سجدة من الركعة الأولى، أو غيرها أو تركها عمداً، فقضاها في آخر صلاته صحت وسجد للسهو وأثم في العمد. (و) يجب (الاطمئنان) وهو التعديل (في الأركان) بتسكين الجوارح في الركوع والسجود، حتى تطمئن مفاصله، وهو الصحيح؛ لأنه شرع لتكميل الركن فكان واجباً كقراءة الفاتحة لا ركنا ولا سنة، كما قال الجرجاني: يسن سنة مؤكدة وأدناه مقدار تسبيحة، وقال أبو يوسف: هو فرض لقوله : « لمن خفف الصلاة، ويقال له المسيء صلاته:
Section on explaining the obligatory acts of prayer. The wajib linguistically means necessity, falling, or agitation. In Shari'ah, it is a name for what is binding upon us by evidence containing ambiguity. Fakhr al-Islam said it is named thus either because it is 'falling' from us knowledge-wise, or because it is 'falling' upon us action-wise, or because it is unsettled between fard and sunnah, or between necessity and non-necessity: it binds us in action, not knowledge. Know that the revealed evidences are four types: qat'i thubut and dalala, like mutawatir texts; qat'i thubut and zanni dalala, like interpreted verses; zanni thubut and qat'i dalala, like ahad hadith whose meaning is definitive; zanni thubut and dalala, like ahad hadith whose meaning is probable. By the first, fard is established; by the second and third, wujub is established; by the fourth, sunnah and mustahabb are established, so that the ruling's establishment is according to its evidence, as in al-Tabyin. Know that the wajibat are prescribed to complete the fara'id, the sunan to complete the wajibat, and the adab to complete the sunan, so that each is a fortress for what it completes. The ruling of the wajib is: deserving punishment for its omission, not deeming its denier a disbeliever, reward for its performance. Its ruling in prayer is: deficiency enters into it by its omission, the obligation of sajdah sahw if omitted forgetfully, and repetition if omitted deliberately, and the fall of the fard deficient if he does not prostrate and does not repeat the prayer, whether omitted deliberately or forgetfully. We have already given the definition of fard, sunnah, and adab. (And it), i.e., the wajib, (is eighteen things). (Recitation of al-Fatihah) is obligatory, due to the Prophet's constant practice and his saying: 'There is no prayer for one who does not recite the Fatihah of the Book.' It is a khabar wahid, so it necessitates action. Therefore, prayer without it is makruh tahrimi, but it is not invalidated if he recites something else, due to the generality of His saying: 'So recite what is easy [of the Quran]' (73:20), and it is not restricted by the aforementioned hadith because it is abrogated, and it is not permissible to abrogate with a khabar wahid. (And) (adding a surah) short, or three short verses, is obligatory, due to his saying: 'There is no prayer for one who does not recite al-Hamd and a surah in a fard or other prayer' narrated by al-Tirmidhi. The ruling is as in the hadith of al-Fatihah. So recitation of al-Fatihah and adding a surah is obligatory in two non-specific rak'ahs of the four- and three-rak'ah fard prayers, because that is the original, and the ruling of the second rak'ah is like the first, as we mentioned earlier. And in all rak'ahs of witr and nafl. Recitation of al-Fatihah and adding a surah is obligatory in all rak'ahs of witr and all rak'ahs of nafl due to what we narrated, and because every two rak'ahs of nafl constitute a separate prayer, so they differ from fard, and witr resembles nafl. (And) (specification of recitation), i.e., recitation of al-Fatihah and surah, is obligatory in the first two rak'ahs of fard due to the Prophet's constant practice of recitation in them, and due to the report that 'Umar omitted recitation in a rakah of maghrib and made it up in the third. It is not obligatory in the last two because of 'Ali's saying: 'Recitation in the first two is recitation in the last two,' and from Ibn Mas'ud and 'A'ishah there is choice in the last two: 'If he wishes, he recites; if he wishes, he glorifies.' (And) (giving precedence to al-Fatihah over the surah) is obligatory due to the Prophet's constant practice, so that if he begins with the surah and then remembers, he recites al-Fatihah and then the surah and performs sajdah sahw, as if he repeated al-Fatihah before the surah. (And) (pressing the nose), i.e., its hard part, to the forehead in prostration, is obligatory due to constant practice, and it is not permissible to limit to the nose in prostration according to the correct view, as we mentioned. (And) observing order between the two prostrations is obligatory, i.e., (performing the second prostration in every rak'ah) of fard or other (before moving to something else), i.e., to other than the prostration from the remaining actions of the prayer, due to constant practice and what we mentioned in the explanation of the fara'id. Thus if he forgets a prostration from the first rak'ah or other, or omits it deliberately, and then makes it up at the end of his prayer, it is valid, and he performs sajdah sahw, and he sins in the deliberate omission. (And) (tranquility), i.e., settling (in the pillars) by calming the limbs in ruku' and sujud until his joints are tranquil, is obligatory, and it is the correct view because it is prescribed to complete the pillar, so it is wajib like recitation of al-Fatihah, not a rukn nor a sunnah. As al-Jurjani said: it is sunnah mu'akkadah, and its minimum is the measure of a tasbihah. Abu Yusuf said it is fard due to his saying: 'to the one who makes the prayer quickly, and he is called the one who prays badly'
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Nur al-Idah begins by defining the concept of 'wajib' both linguistically and terminologically in the Hanafi school. It emphasizes that a wajib is proven by evidence that is not absolutely definitive (zanni), such as a khabar wahid or a verse that can be interpreted. The text then classifies the four types of revealed evidence based on certainty of transmission (thubut) and meaning (dalala), establishing that the first type (qat'i thubut and dalala) proves fard, while the second and third types prove wujub, and the fourth proves sunnah or mustahabb. This classification is foundational for understanding the hierarchy of obligations in Hanafi fiqh. After this theoretical introduction, the text lists the first seven of the eighteen wajibat of salah: recitation of Surah al-Fatihah, adding a short surah or equivalent in the first two rak'ahs of fard and all rak'ahs of witr and nafl, specifying the recitation in the first two rak'ahs of fard, giving precedence to Fatihah over the surah, pressing the nose with the forehead in prostration, performing the second prostration before moving to another action, and maintaining tranquility (itminan) in the pillars. For each, the author provides a hadith or evidence from the Prophet's practice and addresses potential objections. A significant intra-Hanafi dispute is noted regarding itminan: Abu Yusuf considers it fard based on the hadith of the 'Musi' salatuh,' while the majority (Abu Hanifah and Muhammad) deem it wajib. The text confirms the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) that itminan is wajib, not fard. The overall theme is that these wajibat complement the fara'id; their omission requires sajdah sahw but does not invalidate the prayer, unlike a rukn. The passage is a clear exposition of Hanafi methodology linking evidence to ruling.

Key Terms
الواجب (al-wajib): An act whose obligation is established by a proof containing shubha (uncertainty); its omission incurs sin but does not entail disbelief in its rejecter.
الاطمئنان (al-itminan): Tranquility in the pillars of prayer, such as pausing until the joints settle in ruku' and sujud.
خبر آحاد (khabar ahad): A hadith that does not reach the level of tawatur; its transmission is zanni.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated
B) Sajdah sahw is required and the prayer is valid
C) No action is needed; the prayer is complete
D) The prayer is valid but must be repeated later

Key Takeaway
Wajibat of salah are proven by zanni evidence; their omission requires sajdah sahw but does not invalidate the prayer, emphasizing the Hanafi hierarchy of obligations.

Salah — Prayer

Wajibat of Recitation in Salah
Enumeration of recitation-related wajibat with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting Fatiha and a surah in witr and nafl, specify the requirement in the first two rak'ahs of fard, and apply the order of Fatiha before surah.

Core Idea
Recitation in every rak'ah of witr and nafl is obligatory; in fard, it is only wajib in the first two rak'ahs.

This lesson covers the wajibat related to recitation in salah. You will learn when the Fatiha and a surah must be recited, the evidence from the Prophet's constancy (muwazabah) and companion practice, and the consequence of violating the order.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate each ruling in the text: recitation in witr/nafl (obligatory in every rak'ah), recitation in first two of fard (wajib), and the order of Fatiha before surah (wajib).
2
Examine the evidence
The text cites the Prophet's constancy (muwazabah) as proof. For the first two rak'ahs, it also mentions the hadith of 'Umar making up recitation. For the last two, the option from Ibn Mas'ud and 'A'isha.
The hadith of 'Umar is a dalil for wajib in first two; the option shows it is not wajib in the last two.
3
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider someone who recites a surah before the Fatiha in a rak'ah. According to the text, they must recite the Fatiha then the surah again and perform sajdah al-sahw.
4
Distinguish from fard and sunnah
Note that these are wajib, not fard. Omission requires sajdah al-sahw and is sinful if intentional, but the prayer is still valid.
This is a key Hanafi distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي جميع ركعات الوثرِ والنَّفْلِ. وتَعْيِينُ القراءة في الأُولَيَيْنِ، وتقديم الفاتحة على السورة، وضم الأنف للجبهة في السجود، والإتيان بالسجدة الثانية في كلِّ ركعة، قبل الانتقال لغيرها، والاطمئنان في الأركان
بالقراءة في الأولى بالعبارة وفي الثانية بدلالة النص، وتجب قراءة الفاتحة (و) ضــم ســورة (في جميع ركعات الوثر)، (وَ) جميع ركعات (النَّفْل ) لما روينا ، ولأن كل ركعتين من النافلة صلاة على حدة، فلذا خالفت الفرض والوتر مشابهة للنفل . (وَ) يجب ( تَعْيِينُ القراءة) أي: قراءة الفاتحة وسورة (في الأُولَييْن) من الفرض؛ لمواظبة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم على القراءة فيهما، ولما روي أن عمـــره تــرك القراءة في ركعة من المغرب فقضاها في الثالثة، ولم تجب في الأخريين لقول علي ه: « القـــراءة في الأولِيَّيْنِ قَراءَةٌ في الأُخريين ) (، وعن ابن مسعود وعائشة التخيير في الأخريين « إِنْ شَاءَ قَرَأ، وإِنْ شَاءَ سَبَّحَ » ( و ) يجب ( تقديم الفاتحة على قراءة ( السُّورة)؛ لمواظبة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم على ذلك، حتى لو قرأ من السورة ابتداء فتذكر يقرأ الفاتحة ثم يقرأ السورة ويسجد للسهو، كما لو كـرر الفاتحة قبل قراءة السورة (وَ) يجب (ضَمُّ الأَنْفِ) أي: ما صلب منه للجبهة في السجودِ) للمواظبة عليه، ولا يجوز الاقتصار على الأنف في السجود على الصحيح كما قدمناه . (و) تجب مراعاة الترتيب فيما بين السجدتين، وهو (الإتيانُ بالسجدة الثانية في كلِّ ركعة) من الفرض وغيره (قَبْلَ الانْتِقَالِ لِغَيْرِهَا أي: لغير السجدة من باقي أفعال الصلاة للمواظبة على ذلك، ولما قدمناه في بيان الفرائض، حتى لو نسي سجدة من الركعة الأولى، أو غيرها أو تركها عمداً، فقضاها في آخــر صلاته صحت وسجد للسهو ) وأثم في العمد. (وَ) يجب ( الاطْمِثْنَانُ) وهو التعديل (في الأركان) بتسكين الجوارح في الركوع والسجود، حتى تطمئن مفاصله، وهو الصحيح؛ لأنـه شـرع لتكميل الركن فكان واجباً كقراءة الفاتحة لا ركنا ولا سنة، كما قال ( الجرجاني » : يسن سنة مؤكدة وأدناه مقدار تسبيحة، وقال أبو يوسف: هو فرض لقوله : « لِمَنْ خَفَّفَ الصَّلاةَ، وَيُقَالُ لَهُ: الْمَسِيء صَلَاتَه: صَلِّ فَإِنَّكَ لَمْ تُصَلِّ ). وسئل محمد رحمه الله عن ترك الطمأنينة فقال: إني أخاف أن لا تجوز. وعن أبي حنيفة فيمن لم يتم ركوعه وسجوده، ولم يقم صلبه فقال: أخشى أن لا تجوز صلاته، وقيدنــا بالطمأنينة في الأركان لأن الطمأنينة في القومة والجلسة سنة عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد، ومقتضى الدليل وجوب الطمأنينة في الأربعة، ووجوب نفس الرفع من الركوع والجلوس بين السجدتين، للمواظبة على ذلك كله وللأمر في حديث المسيء صلاته، وإليه ذهب المحقق « الكمال بن الهمام»، وتبعه تلميذه ابن أمير حاج وقال: إنه الصواب فليتنبه له. (وَ) يجب ( القُعود الأوّلُ) في الصحيح وقيل: يسن، وقلنا بالوجوب المواظبة النبي عليه وسجوده للسهو لما تركــه وقــام سـاهياً، والمراد بالأول الأول ولو حكماً، فيشمل قعود المسبوق فيما يقضيه، فيجب وإن وجد منه حقيقة مع الإمام. (و) يجب ( قِرَاءةُ التَّشَهْدِ فِيهِ) أي: في القعود الأول وسنذكر لفظه ( إن شاء الله تعالى وقوله (في الصحيح) متعلق بكل من القعود الأول وتشهده، وهو احتراز عن القول بسنيتها أو بسنية التشهد وحده، وجه القول بالوجوب مواظبته ولم يكن فرضاً لما قدمناه من حديث ابن مسعوده: « إذا قلت هذا .... إلخ » (وَ) تجب (قِرَاءتُهُ) أي: التشهد في الجلوس الأخير) أيضـاً لـمـا ذكـرنـاه. (و) يجب (القيام إلى) الركعة (الثالثة، منْ غيرِ تراخ بَعْدَ) قراءة (التَّشَهدِ)، حتـى لـو زاد عليـه بـمـقـدار أداء ركن ساهياً يسجد للسهو لتأخير واجب القيام للثالثة. (و) يجب (لَفْظُ السّلام) مرتين في اليمين واليسار، للمواظبة عليه، وسيأتي)، حكم الالتفات به في السنن، ولم يكن فرضاً لما قدمناه من حديث ابن مسعود، دُونَ عَلَيْكُمْ إذ يحصل المقصود بلفظ السلام دون متعلقه، ويتجه الوجوب بالمواظبة عليه. (و) يجب قراءة (قُنوتُ الوِتْرِ ) عند أبي حنيفة، وكذا تكبيرة القنــوت كـمـا في «الجوهرة» ، ويسن صلاته عندهما، واستدل لوجوبه بأنه يضاف للصلاة فيقال: قنوت الوتر، فدل على أن من خصائصها هو إما بالفرض وهو منتف، أو بالواجب وهو متعين بخلاف التسبيح ونحوه فإنه يضاف إلى الركوع فقط، فلا يجب الجابر بتركه بخلاف القنوت. (وَ) يجب (تَكْبِيرَاتُ العِيدَيْنِ) كلها، وكل واحدة منها واجبة يجب بتركها سجود السهو، وتسمى الزوائد، وهي: ثلاث في كل ركعة، وجه الوجوب الإضافة إلى الصلاة كما ذكرنا.
And in all rak'ahs of witr and supererogatory prayer. And specifying the recitation in the first two rak'ahs, and presenting the Fatiha before the Surah, and joining the nose to the forehead in prostration, and performing the second prostration in every rak'ah before moving to something else, and tranquility in the pillars. By recitation in the first [two] by explicit statement and in the second by implication of the text. And the recitation of the Fatiha and a Surah is obligatory in all rak'ahs of witr and all rak'ahs of supererogatory prayer due to what we have narrated, and because every two rak'ahs of supererogatory prayer are a separate prayer, therefore they differ from obligatory prayer, and witr resembles supererogatory prayer. And specifying the recitation, i.e., reciting the Fatiha and a Surah, in the first two [rak'ahs] of obligatory prayer is obligatory due to the Prophet's constancy in reciting in them, and because it is narrated that 'Umar left recitation in a rak'ah of Maghrib and made it up in the third. And it is not obligatory in the last two [rak'ahs] due to the statement of 'Ali: 'Recitation in the first two is recitation in the last two,' and from Ibn Mas'ud and 'A'isha there is the option in the last two: 'If he wishes, he recites, and if he wishes, he glorifies.' And presenting the Fatiha before reciting the Surah is obligatory due to the Prophet's constancy in that, to the extent that if he begins reading from a Surah and then remembers, he recites the Fatiha then the Surah and performs the prostration of forgetfulness, just as if he repeated the Fatiha before reciting the Surah. And joining the nose, i.e., its hard part, to the forehead in prostration is obligatory due to constancy in it, and it is not permissible to confine [prostration] to the nose according to the correct view as we have mentioned. And observing order between the two prostrations is obligatory, which is performing the second prostration in every rak'ah, obligatory and otherwise, before moving to something else, i.e., other than the prostration from the remaining acts of the prayer, due to constancy in that and due to what we have mentioned in explaining the obligatory [pillars]. So if he forgets a prostration from the first rak'ah or others, or leaves it intentionally, and makes it up at the end of his prayer, his prayer is valid and he performs the prostration of forgetfulness, and he sins in the case of intent. And tranquility, which is composure, is obligatory in the pillars, by stilling the limbs in bowing and prostration until his joints are at rest, and that is the correct [view]; because it was legislated to complete the pillar, so it is obligatory like reciting the Fatiha, not a pillar nor a sunnah, as said by al-Jurjani: 'It is a highly recommended sunnah, and its minimum is the measure of one glorification.' And Abu Yusuf said: 'It is obligatory,' due to his statement to the one who shortened the prayer, who is called the one who prayed badly: 'Pray, for you have not prayed.' And Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, was asked about leaving tranquility and said: 'I fear that it is not valid.' And from Abu Hanifa regarding one who did not complete his bowing and prostration and did not straighten his back, he said: 'I fear that his prayer is not valid.' And we restricted [the obligation] to tranquility in the pillars because tranquility in standing up and sitting is sunnah according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And the implication of the evidence is the obligation of tranquility in the four [pillars], and the obligation of the raising from bowing and sitting between the two prostrations, due to constancy in all of that and due to the command in the hadith of the one who prayed badly. And to this went the verifier Kamal ibn al-Humam, and his student Ibn Amir Hajj followed him and said: 'It is correct, so let one pay attention to it.' And the first sitting is obligatory according to the correct [view], and it is said: it is sunnah. And we said it is obligatory due to the Prophet's constancy and his prostration of forgetfulness when he left it and stood up forgetfully. And 'first' means the first even if by consideration, so it includes the sitting of a latecomer in what he makes up, so it is obligatory even if he actually performs it with the imam. And recitation of the tashahhud in it, i.e., in the first sitting, is obligatory, and we will mention its wording, Allah willing. And his statement 'according to the correct [view]' pertains to both the first sitting and its tashahhud, and it is a precaution against the statement that they are sunnah or that the tashahhud alone is sunnah. The basis for the statement of obligation is his constancy and it was not obligatory due to what we have mentioned from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'When you say this... etc.' And recitation of it, i.e., the tashahhud, in the last sitting is obligatory as well, due to what we have mentioned. And standing for the third rak'ah without delay after the tashahhud is obligatory, so if he adds to it by the measure of performing a pillar forgetfully, he performs the prostration of forgetfulness for delaying the obligation of standing for the third. And the wording of the salutation twice, to the right and left, is obligatory due to constancy, and the ruling of turning during it will come in the sunan, and it was not obligatory due to what we have mentioned from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, [and it is] without 'alaikum, because the purpose is achieved by the word of salutation without its complement, and the obligation is established by constancy. And recitation of the qunut of witr is obligatory according to Abu Hanifa, and likewise the takbir of qunut as in al-Jawhara, and according to [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] its prayer is sunnah. And evidence for its obligation is that it is attributed to the prayer, so it is said 'qunut of witr', indicating that it is among its specific characteristics; it is either obligatory (which is negated) or wajib (which is established), unlike glorification and the like, which are attributed only to bowing, so the compensator is not required for leaving it, unlike qunut. And all the takbirs of the two 'Eids are obligatory, and each one of them is wajib, requiring the prostration of forgetfulness for leaving it, and they are called the additional [takbirs]; they are three in every rak'ah, and the basis for obligation is the attribution to the prayer as we have mentioned.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Nur al-Idah enumerates the wajibat (obligatory acts) of salah according to the Hanafi school. The author, Shaykh al-Imam, presents each wajib with its evidence (dalil), primarily from the Prophet's constant practice (muwazabah) and from hadith. The structure follows the order of the original matn, expanding each point. The passage begins with recitation in witr and nafl, explaining that every two rak'ahs of nafl are an independent prayer, thus requiring recitation in each. For fard prayers, recitation is wajib only in the first two rak'ahs; the last two are optional between recitation and tasbih. The order of Fatiha before surah is wajib; if reversed, one must recite Fatiha and repeat the surah, then perform sajdah al-sahw. Including the nose in sujud is wajib; confining to the nose alone is invalid. The second sajdah must be performed before moving to the next action; if missed, it must be made up later with sajdah al-sahw. Tranquility (itminan) in the four pillars (bow and prostration principally) is wajib according to the relied-upon view, though there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf considers it fard, while the text affirms it as wajib, citing the hadith of the man who prayed badly. The first sitting (qa'dah) and its tashahhud are wajib, as is the tashahhud in the last sitting. Standing for the third rak'ah must occur immediately after the tashahhud; delaying causes sajdah al-sahw. The wording of the salam is wajib twice, but without 'alaikum; the essential is the word 'salam'. Qunut in witr is wajib according to Abu Hanifa, while the two disciples consider it sunnah; the evidence is its attribution to the prayer. Finally, the additional takbirs of 'Eid prayers are wajib; each of the three per rak'ah requires sajdah al-sahw if omitted. This passage illustrates the Hanafi methodology of deriving wajib from the Prophet's constant practice and distinguishing it from fard and sunnah. The mufta bihi position is that these acts are all wajib, not fard nor sunnah, and their omission necessitates sajdah al-sahw.

Key Terms
المواظبة (al-muwazabah): The Prophet's constant practice; in Hanafi usul, it indicates wujub (obligation) unless there is evidence otherwise.
سجود السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed at the end of salah to compensate for unintentional omissions or additions of wajibat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on reciting a surah after al-Fatiha in the third rak'ah of an obligatory prayer?
A) It is fard.
B) It is wajib.
C) It is sunnah; one may either recite or glorify Allah.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, recitation of Fatiha and surah is wajib in every rak'ah of witr and nafl, but in fard it is wajib only in the first two rak'ahs; the order of Fatiha before surah must be observed.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Wajibat of Posture: Nose in Sujud, Second Sajdah, and Tranquility
Enumeration of posture-related wajibat and the tranquility dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi wajibat related to sujud (including nose placement, order of sajdahs, and tranquility) and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on tranquility.

Core Idea
Tranquility in the pillars is wajib; including the nose in sujud is wajib; the second sajdah must be performed immediately after the first.

This lesson deals with three posture-related wajibat: placing the nose on the ground during sujud, performing the second prostration before moving to the next action, and maintaining tranquility (itminan) in all pillars. Special attention is given to the dispute on whether tranquility is fard or wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three wajibat
From the text, list: (1) ضم الأنف للجبهة في السجود (joining the nose to the forehead), (2) الإتيان بالسجدة الثانية قبل الانتقال لغيرها (performing the second sajdah before moving to another action), (3) الاطمئنان في الأركان (tranquility in the pillars).
2
Analyze the evidence for each
The text cites 'المولظة' (constancy) as the proof for all three. For tranquility, it also quotes the hadith of the man who prayed badly: 'صَلِّ فَإِنَّكَ لَمْ تُصَلِّ'.
The hadith provides additional support for tranquility.
3
Compare the views on tranquility
Note that Abu Yusuf considers it fard, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider it wajib, and some early scholars like al-Jurjani consider it sunnah mu'akkadah. The text sides with wajib as the correct view.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) is wajib.
4
Apply to practical scenarios
Consider someone who prostrates without lowering their nose to the ground: they must repeat the sajdah and perform sajdah al-sahw. If they forget the second sajdah and stand up, they must return and perform it, then do sajdah al-sahw. If they rush through the pillars without pausing, they must perform sajdah al-sahw for lack of tranquility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي جميع ركعات الوثرِ والنَّفْلِ. وتَعْيِينُ القراءة في الأُولَيَيْنِ، وتقديم الفاتحة على السورة، وضم الأنف للجبهة في السجود، والإتيان بالسجدة الثانية في كلِّ ركعة، قبل الانتقال لغيرها، والاطمئنان في الأركان
بالقراءة في الأولى بالعبارة وفي الثانية بدلالة النص، وتجب قراءة الفاتحة (و) ضــم ســورة (في جميع ركعات الوثر)، (وَ) جميع ركعات (النَّفْل ) لما روينا ، ولأن كل ركعتين من النافلة صلاة على حدة، فلذا خالفت الفرض والوتر مشابهة للنفل . (وَ) يجب ( تَعْيِينُ القراءة) أي: قراءة الفاتحة وسورة (في الأُولَييْن) من الفرض؛ لمواظبة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم على القراءة فيهما، ولما روي أن عمـــره تــرك القراءة في ركعة من المغرب فقضاها في الثالثة، ولم تجب في الأخريين لقول علي ه: « القـــراءة في الأولِيَّيْنِ قَراءَةٌ في الأُخريين ) (، وعن ابن مسعود وعائشة التخيير في الأخريين « إِنْ شَاءَ قَرَأ، وإِنْ شَاءَ سَبَّحَ » ( و ) يجب ( تقديم الفاتحة على قراءة ( السُّورة)؛ لمواظبة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم على ذلك، حتى لو قرأ من السورة ابتداء فتذكر يقرأ الفاتحة ثم يقرأ السورة ويسجد للسهو، كما لو كـرر الفاتحة قبل قراءة السورة (وَ) يجب (ضَمُّ الأَنْفِ) أي: ما صلب منه للجبهة في السجودِ) للمواظبة عليه، ولا يجوز الاقتصار على الأنف في السجود على الصحيح كما قدمناه . (و) تجب مراعاة الترتيب فيما بين السجدتين، وهو (الإتيانُ بالسجدة الثانية في كلِّ ركعة) من الفرض وغيره (قَبْلَ الانْتِقَالِ لِغَيْرِهَا أي: لغير السجدة من باقي أفعال الصلاة للمواظبة على ذلك، ولما قدمناه في بيان الفرائض، حتى لو نسي سجدة من الركعة الأولى، أو غيرها أو تركها عمداً، فقضاها في آخــر صلاته صحت وسجد للسهو ) وأثم في العمد. (وَ) يجب ( الاطْمِثْنَانُ) وهو التعديل (في الأركان) بتسكين الجوارح في الركوع والسجود، حتى تطمئن مفاصله، وهو الصحيح؛ لأنـه شـرع لتكميل الركن فكان واجباً كقراءة الفاتحة لا ركنا ولا سنة، كما قال ( الجرجاني » : يسن سنة مؤكدة وأدناه مقدار تسبيحة، وقال أبو يوسف: هو فرض لقوله : « لِمَنْ خَفَّفَ الصَّلاةَ، وَيُقَالُ لَهُ: الْمَسِيء صَلَاتَه: صَلِّ فَإِنَّكَ لَمْ تُصَلِّ ). وسئل محمد رحمه الله عن ترك الطمأنينة فقال: إني أخاف أن لا تجوز. وعن أبي حنيفة فيمن لم يتم ركوعه وسجوده، ولم يقم صلبه فقال: أخشى أن لا تجوز صلاته، وقيدنــا بالطمأنينة في الأركان لأن الطمأنينة في القومة والجلسة سنة عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد، ومقتضى الدليل وجوب الطمأنينة في الأربعة، ووجوب نفس الرفع من الركوع والجلوس بين السجدتين، للمواظبة على ذلك كله وللأمر في حديث المسيء صلاته، وإليه ذهب المحقق « الكمال بن الهمام»، وتبعه تلميذه ابن أمير حاج وقال: إنه الصواب فليتنبه له. (وَ) يجب ( القُعود الأوّلُ) في الصحيح وقيل: يسن، وقلنا بالوجوب المواظبة النبي عليه وسجوده للسهو لما تركــه وقــام سـاهياً، والمراد بالأول الأول ولو حكماً، فيشمل قعود المسبوق فيما يقضيه، فيجب وإن وجد منه حقيقة مع الإمام. (و) يجب ( قِرَاءةُ التَّشَهْدِ فِيهِ) أي: في القعود الأول وسنذكر لفظه ( إن شاء الله تعالى وقوله (في الصحيح) متعلق بكل من القعود الأول وتشهده، وهو احتراز عن القول بسنيتها أو بسنية التشهد وحده، وجه القول بالوجوب مواظبته ولم يكن فرضاً لما قدمناه من حديث ابن مسعوده: « إذا قلت هذا .... إلخ » (وَ) تجب (قِرَاءتُهُ) أي: التشهد في الجلوس الأخير) أيضـاً لـمـا ذكـرنـاه. (و) يجب (القيام إلى) الركعة (الثالثة، منْ غيرِ تراخ بَعْدَ) قراءة (التَّشَهدِ)، حتـى لـو زاد عليـه بـمـقـدار أداء ركن ساهياً يسجد للسهو لتأخير واجب القيام للثالثة. (و) يجب (لَفْظُ السّلام) مرتين في اليمين واليسار، للمواظبة عليه، وسيأتي)، حكم الالتفات به في السنن، ولم يكن فرضاً لما قدمناه من حديث ابن مسعود، دُونَ عَلَيْكُمْ إذ يحصل المقصود بلفظ السلام دون متعلقه، ويتجه الوجوب بالمواظبة عليه. (و) يجب قراءة (قُنوتُ الوِتْرِ ) عند أبي حنيفة، وكذا تكبيرة القنــوت كـمـا في «الجوهرة» ، ويسن صلاته عندهما، واستدل لوجوبه بأنه يضاف للصلاة فيقال: قنوت الوتر، فدل على أن من خصائصها هو إما بالفرض وهو منتف، أو بالواجب وهو متعين بخلاف التسبيح ونحوه فإنه يضاف إلى الركوع فقط، فلا يجب الجابر بتركه بخلاف القنوت. (وَ) يجب (تَكْبِيرَاتُ العِيدَيْنِ) كلها، وكل واحدة منها واجبة يجب بتركها سجود السهو، وتسمى الزوائد، وهي: ثلاث في كل ركعة، وجه الوجوب الإضافة إلى الصلاة كما ذكرنا.
And in all rak'ahs of witr and supererogatory prayer. And specifying the recitation in the first two rak'ahs, and presenting the Fatiha before the Surah, and joining the nose to the forehead in prostration, and performing the second prostration in every rak'ah before moving to something else, and tranquility in the pillars. By recitation in the first [two] by explicit statement and in the second by implication of the text. And the recitation of the Fatiha and a Surah is obligatory in all rak'ahs of witr and all rak'ahs of supererogatory prayer due to what we have narrated, and because every two rak'ahs of supererogatory prayer are a separate prayer, therefore they differ from obligatory prayer, and witr resembles supererogatory prayer. And specifying the recitation, i.e., reciting the Fatiha and a Surah, in the first two [rak'ahs] of obligatory prayer is obligatory due to the Prophet's constancy in reciting in them, and because it is narrated that 'Umar left recitation in a rak'ah of Maghrib and made it up in the third. And it is not obligatory in the last two [rak'ahs] due to the statement of 'Ali: 'Recitation in the first two is recitation in the last two,' and from Ibn Mas'ud and 'A'isha there is the option in the last two: 'If he wishes, he recites, and if he wishes, he glorifies.' And presenting the Fatiha before reciting the Surah is obligatory due to the Prophet's constancy in that, to the extent that if he begins reading from a Surah and then remembers, he recites the Fatiha then the Surah and performs the prostration of forgetfulness, just as if he repeated the Fatiha before reciting the Surah. And joining the nose, i.e., its hard part, to the forehead in prostration is obligatory due to constancy in it, and it is not permissible to confine [prostration] to the nose according to the correct view as we have mentioned. And observing order between the two prostrations is obligatory, which is performing the second prostration in every rak'ah, obligatory and otherwise, before moving to something else, i.e., other than the prostration from the remaining acts of the prayer, due to constancy in that and due to what we have mentioned in explaining the obligatory [pillars]. So if he forgets a prostration from the first rak'ah or others, or leaves it intentionally, and makes it up at the end of his prayer, his prayer is valid and he performs the prostration of forgetfulness, and he sins in the case of intent. And tranquility, which is composure, is obligatory in the pillars, by stilling the limbs in bowing and prostration until his joints are at rest, and that is the correct [view]; because it was legislated to complete the pillar, so it is obligatory like reciting the Fatiha, not a pillar nor a sunnah, as said by al-Jurjani: 'It is a highly recommended sunnah, and its minimum is the measure of one glorification.' And Abu Yusuf said: 'It is obligatory,' due to his statement to the one who shortened the prayer, who is called the one who prayed badly: 'Pray, for you have not prayed.' And Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, was asked about leaving tranquility and said: 'I fear that it is not valid.' And from Abu Hanifa regarding one who did not complete his bowing and prostration and did not straighten his back, he said: 'I fear that his prayer is not valid.' And we restricted [the obligation] to tranquility in the pillars because tranquility in standing up and sitting is sunnah according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And the implication of the evidence is the obligation of tranquility in the four [pillars], and the obligation of the raising from bowing and sitting between the two prostrations, due to constancy in all of that and due to the command in the hadith of the one who prayed badly. And to this went the verifier Kamal ibn al-Humam, and his student Ibn Amir Hajj followed him and said: 'It is correct, so let one pay attention to it.' And the first sitting is obligatory according to the correct [view], and it is said: it is sunnah. And we said it is obligatory due to the Prophet's constancy and his prostration of forgetfulness when he left it and stood up forgetfully. And 'first' means the first even if by consideration, so it includes the sitting of a latecomer in what he makes up, so it is obligatory even if he actually performs it with the imam. And recitation of the tashahhud in it, i.e., in the first sitting, is obligatory, and we will mention its wording, Allah willing. And his statement 'according to the correct [view]' pertains to both the first sitting and its tashahhud, and it is a precaution against the statement that they are sunnah or that the tashahhud alone is sunnah. The basis for the statement of obligation is his constancy and it was not obligatory due to what we have mentioned from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'When you say this... etc.' And recitation of it, i.e., the tashahhud, in the last sitting is obligatory as well, due to what we have mentioned. And standing for the third rak'ah without delay after the tashahhud is obligatory, so if he adds to it by the measure of performing a pillar forgetfully, he performs the prostration of forgetfulness for delaying the obligation of standing for the third. And the wording of the salutation twice, to the right and left, is obligatory due to constancy, and the ruling of turning during it will come in the sunan, and it was not obligatory due to what we have mentioned from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, [and it is] without 'alaikum, because the purpose is achieved by the word of salutation without its complement, and the obligation is established by constancy. And recitation of the qunut of witr is obligatory according to Abu Hanifa, and likewise the takbir of qunut as in al-Jawhara, and according to [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] its prayer is sunnah. And evidence for its obligation is that it is attributed to the prayer, so it is said 'qunut of witr', indicating that it is among its specific characteristics; it is either obligatory (which is negated) or wajib (which is established), unlike glorification and the like, which are attributed only to bowing, so the compensator is not required for leaving it, unlike qunut. And all the takbirs of the two 'Eids are obligatory, and each one of them is wajib, requiring the prostration of forgetfulness for leaving it, and they are called the additional [takbirs]; they are three in every rak'ah, and the basis for obligation is the attribution to the prayer as we have mentioned.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Nur al-Idah enumerates the wajibat (obligatory acts) of salah according to the Hanafi school. The author, Shaykh al-Imam, presents each wajib with its evidence (dalil), primarily from the Prophet's constant practice (muwazabah) and from hadith. The structure follows the order of the original matn, expanding each point. The passage begins with recitation in witr and nafl, explaining that every two rak'ahs of nafl are an independent prayer, thus requiring recitation in each. For fard prayers, recitation is wajib only in the first two rak'ahs; the last two are optional between recitation and tasbih. The order of Fatiha before surah is wajib; if reversed, one must recite Fatiha and repeat the surah, then perform sajdah al-sahw. Including the nose in sujud is wajib; confining to the nose alone is invalid. The second sajdah must be performed before moving to the next action; if missed, it must be made up later with sajdah al-sahw. Tranquility (itminan) in the four pillars (bow and prostration principally) is wajib according to the relied-upon view, though there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf considers it fard, while the text affirms it as wajib, citing the hadith of the man who prayed badly. The first sitting (qa'dah) and its tashahhud are wajib, as is the tashahhud in the last sitting. Standing for the third rak'ah must occur immediately after the tashahhud; delaying causes sajdah al-sahw. The wording of the salam is wajib twice, but without 'alaikum; the essential is the word 'salam'. Qunut in witr is wajib according to Abu Hanifa, while the two disciples consider it sunnah; the evidence is its attribution to the prayer. Finally, the additional takbirs of 'Eid prayers are wajib; each of the three per rak'ah requires sajdah al-sahw if omitted. This passage illustrates the Hanafi methodology of deriving wajib from the Prophet's constant practice and distinguishing it from fard and sunnah. The mufta bihi position is that these acts are all wajib, not fard nor sunnah, and their omission necessitates sajdah al-sahw.

Key Terms
الاطمئنان (al-itminan): Composure and stillness of the limbs in the pillars of salah until each joint settles.
السجدة الثانية (al-sajdat al-thaniyah): The second prostration in each rak'ah, which must be performed immediately after the first, before any other action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on placing the nose on the ground during sujud?
A) It is fard; sujud is invalid without it.
B) It is wajib; omitting it requires sajdah al-sahw.
C) It is sunnah; omitting it is not sinful and no compensation needed.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, tranquility, including the nose in sujud, and the order of sajdahs are all wajibat; their omission requires sajdah al-sahw but does not invalidate the prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Wajibat of Sitting, Salam, and Special Acts: Qunut and 'Eid Takbirs
Enumeration of wajibat related to sitting, salam, and special acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rulings on the first sitting, tashahhud, standing for the third rak'ah, salam, qunut in witr, and the 'Eid takbirs, and identify the mufta bihi positions.

Core Idea
The first sitting and its tashahhud, salam, qunut, and 'Eid takbirs are all wajib; each has specific evidence and consequences.

This lesson covers the remaining wajibat from the passage: the first sitting (qa'dah ula) and its tashahhud, the final tashahhud, standing for the third rak'ah, the wording of salam, qunut in witr, and the takbirs of 'Eid. These acts are established by the Prophet's constancy and some companion reports, with internal disputes on a few.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six wajibat
From the text, list: (1) القعود الأول (first sitting), (2) قراءة التشهد فيه (tashahhud in first sitting), (3) قراءة التشهد في الجلوس الأخير (tashahhud in last sitting), (4) القيام إلى الثالثة من غير تراخ (standing for third without delay), (5) لفظ السلام مرتين (saying salam twice), (6) قنوت الوتر (qunut in witr) and (7) تكبيرات العيدين ('Eid takbirs).
Technically seven, but we can group them.
2
Analyze the evidence
The main evidence is the Prophet's constancy (muwazabah) and his sajdah al-sahw when he omitted the first sitting. For qunut, the attribution to the prayer indicates wujub. For 'Eid takbirs, similarly.
3
Note the disputes
The first sitting: some say sunnah, but the text says 'as-sahih' that it is wajib. Qunut: Abu Hanifa says wajib, the two disciples say sunnah. The text adopts Abu Hanifa's view.
4
Apply rules of omission
If one forgets the first sitting and stands, they must return and perform sajdah al-sahw. If one intentionally omits qunut, the prayer is valid but sinful and requires sajdah al-sahw (according to Abu Hanifa).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي جميع ركعات الوثرِ والنَّفْلِ. وتَعْيِينُ القراءة في الأُولَيَيْنِ، وتقديم الفاتحة على السورة، وضم الأنف للجبهة في السجود، والإتيان بالسجدة الثانية في كلِّ ركعة، قبل الانتقال لغيرها، والاطمئنان في الأركان
بالقراءة في الأولى بالعبارة وفي الثانية بدلالة النص، وتجب قراءة الفاتحة (و) ضــم ســورة (في جميع ركعات الوثر)، (وَ) جميع ركعات (النَّفْل ) لما روينا ، ولأن كل ركعتين من النافلة صلاة على حدة، فلذا خالفت الفرض والوتر مشابهة للنفل . (وَ) يجب ( تَعْيِينُ القراءة) أي: قراءة الفاتحة وسورة (في الأُولَييْن) من الفرض؛ لمواظبة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم على القراءة فيهما، ولما روي أن عمـــره تــرك القراءة في ركعة من المغرب فقضاها في الثالثة، ولم تجب في الأخريين لقول علي ه: « القـــراءة في الأولِيَّيْنِ قَراءَةٌ في الأُخريين ) (، وعن ابن مسعود وعائشة التخيير في الأخريين « إِنْ شَاءَ قَرَأ، وإِنْ شَاءَ سَبَّحَ » ( و ) يجب ( تقديم الفاتحة على قراءة ( السُّورة)؛ لمواظبة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم على ذلك، حتى لو قرأ من السورة ابتداء فتذكر يقرأ الفاتحة ثم يقرأ السورة ويسجد للسهو، كما لو كـرر الفاتحة قبل قراءة السورة (وَ) يجب (ضَمُّ الأَنْفِ) أي: ما صلب منه للجبهة في السجودِ) للمواظبة عليه، ولا يجوز الاقتصار على الأنف في السجود على الصحيح كما قدمناه . (و) تجب مراعاة الترتيب فيما بين السجدتين، وهو (الإتيانُ بالسجدة الثانية في كلِّ ركعة) من الفرض وغيره (قَبْلَ الانْتِقَالِ لِغَيْرِهَا أي: لغير السجدة من باقي أفعال الصلاة للمواظبة على ذلك، ولما قدمناه في بيان الفرائض، حتى لو نسي سجدة من الركعة الأولى، أو غيرها أو تركها عمداً، فقضاها في آخــر صلاته صحت وسجد للسهو ) وأثم في العمد. (وَ) يجب ( الاطْمِثْنَانُ) وهو التعديل (في الأركان) بتسكين الجوارح في الركوع والسجود، حتى تطمئن مفاصله، وهو الصحيح؛ لأنـه شـرع لتكميل الركن فكان واجباً كقراءة الفاتحة لا ركنا ولا سنة، كما قال ( الجرجاني » : يسن سنة مؤكدة وأدناه مقدار تسبيحة، وقال أبو يوسف: هو فرض لقوله : « لِمَنْ خَفَّفَ الصَّلاةَ، وَيُقَالُ لَهُ: الْمَسِيء صَلَاتَه: صَلِّ فَإِنَّكَ لَمْ تُصَلِّ ). وسئل محمد رحمه الله عن ترك الطمأنينة فقال: إني أخاف أن لا تجوز. وعن أبي حنيفة فيمن لم يتم ركوعه وسجوده، ولم يقم صلبه فقال: أخشى أن لا تجوز صلاته، وقيدنــا بالطمأنينة في الأركان لأن الطمأنينة في القومة والجلسة سنة عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد، ومقتضى الدليل وجوب الطمأنينة في الأربعة، ووجوب نفس الرفع من الركوع والجلوس بين السجدتين، للمواظبة على ذلك كله وللأمر في حديث المسيء صلاته، وإليه ذهب المحقق « الكمال بن الهمام»، وتبعه تلميذه ابن أمير حاج وقال: إنه الصواب فليتنبه له. (وَ) يجب ( القُعود الأوّلُ) في الصحيح وقيل: يسن، وقلنا بالوجوب المواظبة النبي عليه وسجوده للسهو لما تركــه وقــام سـاهياً، والمراد بالأول الأول ولو حكماً، فيشمل قعود المسبوق فيما يقضيه، فيجب وإن وجد منه حقيقة مع الإمام. (و) يجب ( قِرَاءةُ التَّشَهْدِ فِيهِ) أي: في القعود الأول وسنذكر لفظه ( إن شاء الله تعالى وقوله (في الصحيح) متعلق بكل من القعود الأول وتشهده، وهو احتراز عن القول بسنيتها أو بسنية التشهد وحده، وجه القول بالوجوب مواظبته ولم يكن فرضاً لما قدمناه من حديث ابن مسعوده: « إذا قلت هذا .... إلخ » (وَ) تجب (قِرَاءتُهُ) أي: التشهد في الجلوس الأخير) أيضـاً لـمـا ذكـرنـاه. (و) يجب (القيام إلى) الركعة (الثالثة، منْ غيرِ تراخ بَعْدَ) قراءة (التَّشَهدِ)، حتـى لـو زاد عليـه بـمـقـدار أداء ركن ساهياً يسجد للسهو لتأخير واجب القيام للثالثة. (و) يجب (لَفْظُ السّلام) مرتين في اليمين واليسار، للمواظبة عليه، وسيأتي)، حكم الالتفات به في السنن، ولم يكن فرضاً لما قدمناه من حديث ابن مسعود، دُونَ عَلَيْكُمْ إذ يحصل المقصود بلفظ السلام دون متعلقه، ويتجه الوجوب بالمواظبة عليه. (و) يجب قراءة (قُنوتُ الوِتْرِ ) عند أبي حنيفة، وكذا تكبيرة القنــوت كـمـا في «الجوهرة» ، ويسن صلاته عندهما، واستدل لوجوبه بأنه يضاف للصلاة فيقال: قنوت الوتر، فدل على أن من خصائصها هو إما بالفرض وهو منتف، أو بالواجب وهو متعين بخلاف التسبيح ونحوه فإنه يضاف إلى الركوع فقط، فلا يجب الجابر بتركه بخلاف القنوت. (وَ) يجب (تَكْبِيرَاتُ العِيدَيْنِ) كلها، وكل واحدة منها واجبة يجب بتركها سجود السهو، وتسمى الزوائد، وهي: ثلاث في كل ركعة، وجه الوجوب الإضافة إلى الصلاة كما ذكرنا.

And standing for the third rak'ah without delay after the tashahhud is obligatory, so if he adds to it by the measure of performing a pillar forgetfully, he performs the prostration of forgetfulness for delaying the obligation of standing for the third. And the wording of the salutation twice, to the right and left, is obligatory due to constancy, and the ruling of turning during it will come in the sunan, and it was not obligatory due to what we have mentioned from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, [and it is] without 'alaikum, because the purpose is achieved by the word of salutation without its complement, and the obligation is established by constancy. And recitation of the qunut of witr is obligatory according to Abu Hanifa, and likewise the takbir of qunut as in al-Jawhara, and according to [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] its prayer is sunnah. And evidence for its obligation is that it is attributed to the prayer, so it is said 'qunut of witr', indicating that it is among its specific characteristics; it is either obligatory (which is negated) or wajib (which is established), unlike glorification and the like, which are attributed only to bowing, so the compensator is not required for leaving it, unlike qunut. And all the takbirs of the two 'Eids are obligatory, and each one of them is wajib, requiring the prostration of forgetfulness for leaving it, and they are called the additional [takbirs]; they are three in every rak'ah, and the basis for obligation is the attribution to the prayer as we have mentioned.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Nur al-Idah enumerates the wajibat (obligatory acts) of salah according to the Hanafi school. The author, Shaykh al-Imam, presents each wajib with its evidence (dalil), primarily from the Prophet's constant practice (muwazabah) and from hadith. The structure follows the order of the original matn, expanding each point. The passage begins with recitation in witr and nafl, explaining that every two rak'ahs of nafl are an independent prayer, thus requiring recitation in each. For fard prayers, recitation is wajib only in the first two rak'ahs; the last two are optional between recitation and tasbih. The order of Fatiha before surah is wajib; if reversed, one must recite Fatiha and repeat the surah, then perform sajdah al-sahw. Including the nose in sujud is wajib; confining to the nose alone is invalid. The second sajdah must be performed before moving to the next action; if missed, it must be made up later with sajdah al-sahw. Tranquility (itminan) in the four pillars (bow and prostration principally) is wajib according to the relied-upon view, though there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf considers it fard, while the text affirms it as wajib, citing the hadith of the man who prayed badly. The first sitting (qa'dah) and its tashahhud are wajib, as is the tashahhud in the last sitting. Standing for the third rak'ah must occur immediately after the tashahhud; delaying causes sajdah al-sahw. The wording of the salam is wajib twice, but without 'alaikum; the essential is the word 'salam'. Qunut in witr is wajib according to Abu Hanifa, while the two disciples consider it sunnah; the evidence is its attribution to the prayer. Finally, the additional takbirs of 'Eid prayers are wajib; each of the three per rak'ah requires sajdah al-sahw if omitted. This passage illustrates the Hanafi methodology of deriving wajib from the Prophet's constant practice and distinguishing it from fard and sunnah. The mufta bihi position is that these acts are all wajib, not fard nor sunnah, and their omission necessitates sajdah al-sahw.

Key Terms
القعود الأول (al-qa'dah al-ula): The first sitting after the second rak'ah in prayers of three or more rak'ahs, where the tashahhud is recited.
القنوت (al-qunut): A supplication recited in witr prayer, usually after the ruku' of the last rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on reciting the tashahhud in the last sitting of prayer?
A) It is fard.
B) It is wajib.
C) It is sunnah.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
The first sitting, tashahhud in both sittings, standing for the third rak'ah, salam, qunut, and 'Eid takbirs are all wajib in Hanafi fiqh; their omission requires sajdah al-sahw and is sinful if intentional.

Obligation of the First Sitting and Reciting Tashahhud
Explains the obligation of the first sitting and tashahhud with evidence and ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of the first sitting and tashahhud, identify the proof based on the Prophet's constant practice and sajdat al-sahw, and explain the Hanafi distinction between wājib and fard in this context.

Core Idea
First sitting and tashahhud are wājib: Prophet's constant practice and sajdat al-sahw prove it.

In this passage, the author of Imdād al-Fattāḥ clarifies the legal status of the first sitting and the recitation of the tashahhud within it. While some scholars consider these acts merely sunnah, the relied-upon Hanafi position is that they are wājib. This lesson explores the evidence from the Prophet's practice (muwāẓabah) and his sajdat al-sahw, explaining why these acts are obligatory but not fard.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Acts and Their Ruling
The passage discusses two acts: the first sitting (al-qu‘ūd al-awwal) and reciting the tashahhud in it. The author states they are wājib in the correct view (في الصحيح).
Note that the ruling applies to both acts together.
2
Recognize the Ikhtilāf
Some scholars hold these acts to be sunnah. The passage notes this as a discarded view (قول بسنيتها). Understanding the difference is key: wājib requires compensation if omitted; sunnah does not.
This ikhtilāf is intra-Hanafi and also with the Shāfi‘ī school.
3
Examine the Dalīl
The proof is the Prophet's constant practice (muwāẓabah) and his sajdat al-sahw when he once left the first sitting unintentionally. The hadīth of Ibn Mas'ūd is also referenced.
The hadīth is not quoted in full but serves as additional support.
4
Analyze the Legal Reasoning (Wajh al-Dalālah)
The Prophet's sajdat al-sahw for omitting the first sitting indicates two things: (a) omission does not invalidate the prayer (so it is not fard), but (b) it requires compensation (so it is wājib). Constant practice (muwāẓabah) alone would imply sunnah, but the addition of sajdat al-sahw raises it to wājib.
This is a classic Hanafi usul reasoning: an act consistently done by the Prophet and compensated by sajdat al-sahw when missed is wājib.
5
Apply the Ruling to Special Cases
The author clarifies that the 'first sitting' includes the ruling-wise first sitting of a latecomer (masbūq). Even if he performed the sitting with the imam, it is considered his own first sitting.
This shows the practical application of the ruling to a common scenario.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقعود الأول، وقراءةُ التَّشَهُدِ فيه في الصحيح. (وَ) يجب ( القُعود الأوّلُ) في الصحيح وقيل: يسن، وقلنا بالوجوب المواظبة النبي عليه وسجوده للسهو لما تركــه وقــام سـاهياً، والمراد بالأول الأول ولو حكماً، فيشمل قعود المسبوق فيما يقضيه، فيجب وإن وجد منه حقيقة مع الإمام. (و) يجب ( قِرَاءةُ التَّشَهْدِ فِيهِ) أي: في القعود الأول وسنذكر لفظه إن شاء الله تعالى وقوله (في الصحيح) متعلق بكل من القعود الأول وتشهده، وهو احتراز عن القول بسنيتها أو بسنية التشهد وحده، وجه القول بالوجوب مواظبته ولم يكن فرضاً لما قدمناه من حديث ابن مسعوده: « إذا قلت هذا .... إلخ »
And the first sitting, and recitation of tashahhud in it in the correct view. (And) the first sitting is obligatory in the correct view, and it is said it is sunnah, and we say it is obligatory due to the Prophet's constant practice and his prostration of forgetfulness when he left it and stood unintentionally. And what is meant by 'first' is the first ruling-wise, so it includes the sitting of the latecomer in what he makes up, so it is obligatory even if he actually performed it with the imam. And recitation of tashahhud in it (i.e., the first sitting) is obligatory, and we will mention its wording, God willing. And his saying 'in the correct view' relates to both the first sitting and its tashahhud, and it is a safeguard against the view that they are sunnah or that only the tashahhud is sunnah. The basis for the view of obligation is his constant practice, and it was not an obligatory duty due to what we have presented from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'When you have said this... etc.'
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage establishes the obligation of the first sitting and reciting the tashahhud during it. The author notes a difference of opinion: some scholars hold it to be sunnah, but the relied-upon position (in the ṣaḥīḥ) is that it is wājib. The proof is the Prophet's constant practice (muwāẓabah) and that he performed sajdat al-sahw when he inadvertently omitted the first sitting and stood up, which indicates that omitting it necessitates compensation. The author also clarifies that the 'first sitting' includes the ruling-wise first sitting of a latecomer (masbūq) when he completes his missed rak‘ahs after the imam. Regarding the tashahhud, its obligation is similarly based on the Prophet's constant practice and the understanding that it is not an integral (fard) because the hadith of Ibn Mas‘ūd shows that the prayer is valid without it, but it is still obligatory to the extent that leaving it requires sajdat al-sahw.

Key Terms
القعود الأول (al-qu‘ūd al-awwal): The first sitting in prayer after the second rak‘ah when one is not performing a four-rak‘ah prayer with a second sitting; or the first sitting in any multi-rak‘ah prayer.
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The recitation of the testimony of faith (ashhadu an lā ilāha illallāh, etc.) during the sitting.
المواظبة (al-muwāẓabah): The Prophet's constant and consistent practice of an act, which in Hanafi uṣūl indicates wujūb when there is sajdat al-sahw for omitting it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the Prophet performed sajdat al-sahw when he omitted it.
B) Because it is mentioned in the Quran.
C) Because the majority of scholars say so.
D) Because it is a pillar of prayer.

Key Takeaway
The first sitting and its tashahhud are wājib in the Hanafi school, as proven by the Prophet's constant practice and his sajdat al-sahw when he omitted them.

Obligation of Reciting Tashahhud in the Last Sitting
States the obligation of reciting tashahhud in the last sitting as wājib.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that reciting tashahhud in the last sitting is wajib in the Hanafi school and identify the consequence of omitting it.

Core Idea
Reciting tashahhud in the last sitting is wajib, not fard — omission requires sajdat al-sahw.

This passage confirms that the tashahhud in the last sitting is obligatory, just as in the first sitting. Understanding the distinction between fard and wajib is essential: a missed wajib does not invalidate the prayer but requires compensation via sajdat al-sahw, while a missed fard invalidates it. This lesson clarifies the ruling and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting the tashahhud in the last sitting. The ruling is that it is wājib (obligatory but not a pillar).
Wājib in Hanafi terminology means the evidence is strong but not definitive (zannī).
2
Recall the evidence
The evidence is the Prophet's constant practice (muwāẓaba) and that he performed sajdat al-sahw when he omitted it. This establishes obligation but not at the level of fard.
The passage refers to 'what we have mentioned' earlier, i.e., the same proof for the first sitting.
3
Distinguish fard vs. wājib
Fard is proven by decisive evidence (qat‘ī) and its omission invalidates prayer. Wājib is proven by probable evidence (zannī) and its omission requires sajdat al-sahw but does not invalidate prayer.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school.
4
Apply to practice
If one forgets the tashahhud in the last sitting, one must perform sajdat al-sahw before the salām. The prayer remains valid.

Source Text

(And) its recitation (i.e., the tashahhud) is obligatory in the last sitting as well, for what we have mentioned.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This short passage confirms that reciting the tashahhud in the last sitting (al-julūs al-akhīr) is also obligatory. The author refers to the same evidence presented earlier for the first sitting: the Prophet's constant practice and his sajdat al-sahw for omission. The last sitting is the sitting after the final rak‘ah before the salām, and the tashahhud in it is a wājib, not a fard.

Key Terms
الجلوس الأخير (al-julūs al-akhīr): The final sitting in prayer after the last rak‘ah, before giving salām.

Obligation of Standing to the Third Rak'ah Without Delay
Explains the obligation of standing for the third rak'ah promptly after tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that standing for the third rak'ah is wajib and identify when sajdat al-sahw becomes necessary due to delay.

Core Idea
Standing for the third rak'ah is a wajib; delaying it by the time of a rukn requires sajdat al-sahw.

This lesson focuses on a specific wajib act within the prayer: standing for the third rak'ah immediately after the first tashahhud. The Hanafi school emphasizes promptness, such that even an unintentional delay equivalent to performing an extra rukn triggers a requirement for sajdat al-sahw. Understanding this ruling helps maintain the proper sequence and obligation of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is standing up to perform the third rak'ah after the tashahhud. The ruling is that it is wājib (obligatory).
Wājib differs from farḍ: omission of wājib requires sajdat al-sahw, not invalidation of the prayer.
2
Locate the condition of immediacy
The standing must occur immediately after completing the tashahhud, without any delay ('min ghayri tarākhin').
Any intentional or unintentional delay that is more than negligible can affect the ruling.
3
Determine the consequence of delay
If one delays unintentionally by the time it takes to perform a pillar (rukn) — e.g., an extra rak'ah movement — then sajdat al-sahw becomes obligatory.
The measurement is the duration of a typical rukn, not a specific number of seconds.
4
Understand the rationale
Sajdat al-sahw compensates for delaying a wājib act. The prayer remains valid but requires this prostrations of forgetfulness.
This is consistent with Hanafi usul: omission of wājib does not invalidate but requires compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يجب (القيام إلى) الركعة (الثالثة، منْ غيرِ تراخ بَعْدَ) قراءة (التَّشَهدِ)، حتـى لـو زاد عليـه بـمـقـدار أداء ركن ساهياً يسجد للسهو لتأخير واجب القيام للثالثة.
(And) standing to the third rak'ah is obligatory, without delay, after recitation of the tashahhud, such that if he adds after it (i.e., after the tashahhud) an amount equal to performing a pillar unintentionally, he performs sajdat al-sahw for delaying the obligatory standing for the third.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage establishes that standing to begin the third rak'ah is a wājib act. It must be done immediately after completing the tashahhud in the first sitting. If one delays even unintentionally by the time it takes to perform a pillar (like an extra rukn), then sajdat al-sahw becomes necessary because the wājib of standing has been delayed. This highlights the importance of promptness in continuing the prayer after the first sitting.

Key Terms
القيام إلى الثالثة (al-qiyām ilā al-thālithah): Standing up to perform the third rak'ah of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Obligation of the Wording of Salām
Explains the obligation of saying 'al-salāmu 'alaykum' twice without 'alaykum being obligatory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the wājib component of the final salām in Hanafi prayer and explain the proof from the Prophet's constant practice.

Core Idea
The wājib in salām is the word 'al-salāmu' alone; 'alaykum is not wājib because the objective is achieved with the essential greeting.

This lesson clarifies precisely what is obligatory in the final salutation of the prayer. The Hanafi school holds that uttering 'al-salāmu' twice is wājib, but the word 'alaykum' is not required. Understanding this distinction is crucial for knowing when sajdat al-sahw is necessary. The proof comes from the Prophet's constant practice (muwāẓabah), which establishes wujūb, and from the hadith of Ibn Masʿūd, which shows that the prayer is valid even without a specific wording of salām.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is uttering the final salām at the end of prayer. The text states it is wājib (obligatory) twice.
2
Determine the essential wording
The text explicitly says 'without 'alaykum', meaning only the word 'al-salāmu' is part of the obligation. The object 'alaykum is not required.
The phrase 'دُونَ عَلَيْكُمْ' is key.
3
Locate the proof
The obligation is proven by the Prophet's constant practice (muwāẓabah) on saying the salām. It is not fard because the hadith of Ibn Masʿūd indicates that the prayer is valid without a specific wording.
Muwāẓabah in Hanafi usul indicates wujūb, not fard.
4
Understand the consequence
Since it is wājib, omitting it requires sajdat al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness), but the prayer remains valid.
This differs from a rukn, whose omission would invalidate the prayer.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Shāfiʿīs consider the full phrase including 'alaykum as a rukn. Hanafis distinguish between the essential 'al-salāmu' and the additional 'alaykum.
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether sajdat al-sahw suffices or the prayer is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يجب (لَفْظُ السّلام) مرتين في اليمين واليسار، للمواظبة عليه، وسيأتي حكم الالتفات به في السنن، ولم يكن فرضاً لما قدمناه من حديث ابن مسعود، دُونَ عَلَيْكُمْ إذ يحصل المقصود بلفظ السلام دون متعلقه، ويتجه الوجــوب بالمواظبة عليه.
(And) the wording of salām is obligatory twice, to the right and left, due to the constant practice upon it, and the ruling of the turning (during it) will come in the sunan, and it was not an obligatory duty due to what we have presented from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, without 'alaykum because the objective is achieved by the wording of salām without its object, and the obligation is based on the constant practice upon it.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage explains that uttering the word 'al-salāmu' (i.e., 'al-salāmu 'alaykum') twice, once to the right and once to the left, is wājib. The additional word 'alaykum is not required because the essence of greeting is achieved with 'al-salāmu' alone. The obligation is established through the Prophet's constant practice (muwāẓabah). It is not fard because the hadith of Ibn Mas'ūd indicates that prayer is valid without a specific wording of salām. Delaying or omitting this wājib requires sajdat al-sahw.

Key Terms
لفظ السلام (lafẓ al-salām): The wording of the salutation to end prayer: 'al-salāmu 'alaykum wa raḥmatu llāh' twice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Both 'al-salāmu' and 'alaykum' are wājib

Key Takeaway
Only the word 'al-salāmu' said twice is wājib in the final salām; 'alaykum is not obligatory.

The Obligation of Qunūt in Witr: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains the obligation of qunūt in witr with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on qunūt al-witr, identify the dispute between Abū Ḥanīfah and the two companions, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf regarding sajdat al-sahw.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, qunūt al-witr is wājib according to Abū Ḥanīfah, but sunnah according to the Sahibayn.

This passage addresses a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the qunūt supplication in the witr prayer. While the two companions (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad al-Shaybānī) consider it sunnah, Imām Abū Ḥanīfah holds it to be wājib, meaning its unintentional omission requires the prostration of forgetfulness (sajdat al-sahw). Understanding the evidence and the practical consequence is essential for Hanafi fiqh accuracy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the two positions: Abu Hanifa says wajib, Sahibayn say sunnah.
2
Analyse the Dalil
The text attributes qunūt to the prayer (qunūt al-witr), showing it is a special characteristic. Since it is not fard, it must be wajib.
This is an aqli istidlal (reasoning by elimination).
3
Contrast with Tasbīḥ
Tasbīḥ in rukū‘ is only attributed to rukū‘ and is not wajib, hence no compensation for omission.
Tasbīḥ is purely sunnah; qunūt has a stronger link.
4
Determine the Thamarah
If one omits qunūt unintentionally, according to Abu Hanifa sajdat al-sahw is required; according to Sahibayn it is not.
This is the practical consequence of the difference.
5
Identify the Muftā Bihī
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa: wajib.
This is the view adopted for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يجب قراءة (قُنوتُ الوِتْرِ ) عند أبي حنيفة، وكذا تكبيرة القنوت كما في «الجوهرة» ، ويسن صلاته عندهما، واستدل لوجوبه بأنه يضاف للصلاة فيقال: قنوت الوتر، فدل على أن من خصائصها هو إما بالفرض وهو منتف، أو بالواجب وهو متعين بخلاف التسبيح ونحوه فإنه يضاف إلى الركوع فقط، فلا يجب الجابر بتركه بخلاف القنوت.
(And) recitation of qunūt al-witr is obligatory according to Abū Ḥanīfah, and likewise the takbīr of qunūt as in 'al-Jawharah', and its prayer (i.e., the qunūt) is sunnah according to them (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad). And evidence for its obligation is that it is attributed to the prayer, so it is said 'qunūt al-witr', indicating that it is among its special characteristics, either as an obligatory duty (which is negated) or as an obligatory (wājib) which is determined, unlike the tasbīḥ and the like, for they are attributed to the rukū‘ only, so no compensator is required for leaving them, unlike the qunūt.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage presents a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute. According to Imām Abū Ḥanīfah, reciting the qunūt supplication in the witr prayer is wājib, and similarly the takbīr that accompanies it. According to the two companions (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad al-Shaybānī), it is sunnah. The evidence for Abū Ḥanīfah's position is that the qunūt is specifically attributed to the witr prayer (as in 'qunūt al-witr'), showing it is a distinctive feature. Since it is not a fard (obligatory duty), by elimination it must be wājib. This is contrasted with tasbīḥ in rukū‘, which is only attributed to the rukū‘ and is not considered wājib. The binding ruling (muftā bihī) in the Hanafi school is the view of Abū Ḥanīfah, i.e., wājib.

Key Terms
قنوت الوتر (qunūt al-witr): A special supplication recited in the witr prayer, after the rukū‘ or before, depending on the school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abū Ḥanīfah, what is the status of qunūt al-witr?
A) Fard
B) Wājib
C) Sunnah
D) Mustaḥabb

Key Takeaway
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, qunūt al-witr is wājib, and its unintentional omission necessitates sajdat al-sahw.

The Obligation of the Extra Takbīrāt in Eid Prayers
Explains the obligation and consequence of omitting extra takbīrāt in Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of the extra takbīrāt in Eid prayer, explain why they are wājib, and determine the consequence of omitting them.

Core Idea
Each extra takbīr in Eid prayer is individually wājib; omitting any requires sajdat al-sahw.

This passage clarifies the legal status of the extra takbīrāt recited during Eid prayers. While many worshippers may assume they are sunnah, the Hanafi school holds them to be wājib—a distinct level requiring compensation if missed. Understanding the basis for this ruling helps in correctly performing and completing these special prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the extra takbīrāt in Eid prayer (three per rak'ah). The ruling: each one is wājib.
This is a ruling from the matn, expanded by the commentator.
2
Locate the proof
The author states 'the basis for the obligation is the attribution to prayer' (al-idāfah ilā al-ṣalāt), meaning these takbīrāt are specifically assigned to the Eid prayer, indicating they are a distinctive and required element.
The same reasoning applies to qunūt in witr prayer.
3
Distinguish from other categories
These takbīrāt are not fard (the prayer is valid without them) nor sunnah (they require compensation if omitted). They fall into the wājib category.
Hanafi fiqh distinguishes fard (proven by qat’ī dalīl) from wājib (proven by zannī dalīl).
4
Determine the consequence
Omitting any one of them necessitates sajdat al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) after the salam.
This is the standard compensation for a missed wājib in prayer.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
The Shāfi‘ī school considers these takbīrāt sunnah, not wājib, and would not require sajdat al-sahw for omission.
This ikhtilāf arises from different usūl regarding the interpretation of the Prophet’s practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) يجب (تَكْبِيرَاتُ العِيدَيْنِ) كلها، وكل واحدة منها واجبة يجب بتركها سجود السهو، وتسمى الزوائد، وهي: ثلاث في كل ركعة، وجه الوجوب الإضافة إلى الصلاة كما ذكرنا.
(And) the takbīrāt of the two Eids are all obligatory, and each one of them is wājib; leaving it obligates sajdat al-sahw. They are called the extra (takbīrāt), and they are three in each rak'ah. The basis for the obligation is the attribution to prayer, as we mentioned.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage establishes that all the extra takbīrāt in Eid prayers (three in the first rak'ah before recitation, and three in the second after the standing and before recitation, according to the Hanafi method) are wājib individually. Omitting any one of them requires sajdat al-sahw. The proof is similar to that for qunūt: these takbīrāt are specifically attributed to the two Eid prayers (hence 'takbīrāt al-'īdayn'), indicating they are a distinctive feature of these prayers. Since they are not fard (the prayer would still be valid without them), they fall into the category of wājib.

Key Terms
تكبيرات العيدين (takbīrāt al-'īdayn): The extra takbīrāt recited in the Eid prayer, three in each rak'ah, before recitation.

Key Takeaway

The Wujūb of Ta‘yīn al-Takbīr and Takbīrat al-Rukū‘ in the Second Rak‘ah of Eid
Ruling with proof on ta‘yīn al-takbīr and takbīrat al-rukū‘ in Eid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the opening takbīr must be 'Allāhu Akbar' for every prayer (wājib) and explain why the takbīr for rukū‘ in the second rak‘ah of Eid is also wājib.

Core Idea
The opening takbīr is wājib for every prayer; the rukū‘ takbīr in Eid's second rak‘ah is wājib because it follows the extra takbīrāt.

This passage clarifies that the specification of the opening takbīr (saying 'Allāhu Akbar') is not limited to Eid prayers but applies to all prayers. This ruling is based on the Prophet's constant practice (muwāẓabah). Additionally, the takbīr for bowing in the second rak‘ah of Eid is also wājib because it directly follows the extra takbīrāt. Understanding this distinction helps avoid confusion about Eid prayer rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage gives two distinct rulings: (a) ta‘yīn al-takbīr (specifying the wording 'Allāhu Akbar' for opening the prayer) is wājib for every prayer; (b) takbīrat al-rukū‘ in the second rak‘ah of the two Eids is wājib.
The first ruling is general, the second is specific to Eid.
2
Trace the dalīl for the first ruling
The proof is the Prophet's constant practice (muwāẓabah). In Hanafi uṣūl, consistent practice indicates wujūb unless proven otherwise. The text explicitly says: 'مواظبة النبي الله على التكبير عند افتتاح كل صلاة.'
This is a sunnah ahad evidence, giving zannī certainty.
3
Understand the ikhtilāf about Eid
Some scholars (unnamed) thought the opening takbīr for Eid could be different. The author clarifies that ta‘yīn applies to all prayers, and cites al-Sarakhsī who said it is not disliked to start with other than takbīr for Eid, but the preferred view is that it is wājib and disliked to omit.
The phrase 'لا العيدين خاصة' means the ruling is not only for Eid, but for all prayers.
4
Examine the second ruling's logic
The takbīr for rukū‘ in the second rak‘ah is wājib because it immediately follows the extra takbīrāt (which are also wājib). In the first rak‘ah, the rukū‘ takbīr is not part of the extra set, so it remains sunnah.
The text says: 'تبعاً لتكبيرات العيدين، لأنها تليها.'

Source Text

And specification of takbīr for opening every prayer, not for the two Eids specifically. And takbīrat al-rukū‘ in the second of the two Eids. And therefore we say: The takbīr is not specified for opening the prayer of the two Eids specifically, as a precaution against what some have said, and to that points the saying of al-Sarakhsī: The most correct view is that it is not disliked to start with other than takbīr, as in 'al-Tabyīn'. Commentary
This passage covers two points. First, opening every prayer with the word 'Allāhu Akbar' (takbīrat al-tahrīmah) is wājib due to the Prophet's constant practice. It is specific to this wording; starting with another phrase is disliked. Some scholars thought the opening takbīr for Eid prayers could be different, but the author clarifies that the specification is for all prayers, not just Eid. Second, the takbīr for bowing (takbīrat al-rukū‘) in the second rak'ah of Eid prayers is also wājib, because it follows the extra takbīrāt. In the first rak'ah, the takbīr for rukū‘ is not part of the extra takbīrāt and is simply a regular sunnah.

Key Terms
تعيين التكبير (ta‘yīn al-takbīr): Specifying the wording 'Allāhu Akbar' for the opening takbīr of prayer.
تكبيرة الركوع (takbīrat al-rukū‘): The takbīr said when moving into bowing (rukū‘) in prayer.

Key Takeaway
